1  General provisions 
1.1 The Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP Unit 1 
(hereinafter referred to as TSSO), which contains rules and basic operation 
techniques, general procedure of safety  related operations, limits and conditions of 
safe operation, as well as operation limits of basic parameters and operation 
conditions based on the state of operability of safety related systems (components) in 
the normal operation mode of the Unit, is the main document that determines the safe 
operation of the NPP Unit. 
1.2 TSSO is developed with the participation of NPP and RP designers in 
accordance with the NPP design and Preliminary safety analysis report in compliance 
with the standard specification. 
1.3 TSSO is designed in accordance with the requirements of 
RPR.0534.0.0.OP.BZ0002 [31]. 
1.4 The TSSO and the changes made to it shall be agreed with the 
organizations involved in the development of the specified specification. 
1.5 Operation instructions for equipment and  systems are developed based 
on the TSSO, as well as design and engineering documentation. Operation instruction 
for equipment and systems shall not contradict the requirements of the technical 
specification. 
1.6 The TSSO scope is the control of the Unit durin g normal operation and 
in case of disturbances of normal operation. 
1.7 Technical support of TSSO is provided by Rooppur NPP. 
1.8 TSSO adjustment is performed based on the obtained results at the 
stages of first approach of criticality and power start -up, and the final safety analysis 
report of Rooppur NPP Unit No. 1. 
1.9 Changes to the technical specification are made by notice of change, 
which shall be agreed with the organizations that have agreed on the specification, 
approved by the operating organization and appr oved by the national regulatory 
authority in the prescribed manner (BAERA). 
1.10 The technical specification of safe operation is adjusted before putting 
the Unit into operation on the basis of the final safety analysis report of Unit No.1. 
1.11 Scope and frequency of inspections and tests of safety related systems 
(system components) as well as criteria, when equipment is considered operable, are 
given in the document “Regulations for inspections and tests of safety related 
systems” for Unit No. 1 of Rooppur NPP. [ 35]. 
1.12 The document contains excessive pressure values i n accordance with the 
values of displaying information at the MCR (ODM mimic panel and MCR operators 
automated workstations), except for specially specified cases. 
1.13 The TSSO validity period is set as 5 y ears from the date of putting into 
effect the final TSSO version, after which the document is subject to revision.

2 Operation state and modes of the Unit 
2.1 Safe operation limits are established in relation to the operation states of 
the Unit implemented during its operation: 
 S1 state - power operation (PO); 
 S2 state - minimum controlled power level (MCPL); 
 S3 state - hot state (HS); 
 S4 state - cold state (CSt); 
 S5 state - shutdown for repair (SR); 
 S6 state - refueling (RF); 
 S7 state - heat-up (HU); 
 S8 state - cooldown (CD). 
2.2 The boundaries between the states are set as follows: 
1) Between the S6 state ( refueling) and the S5 state (shutdown for repair) - 
removal/installation of hydraulic locks between the fuel pool and the reactor pit; 
2) Between the S5 state (shutdown for repair) and the S4 state (cold) - 
decompression of one of/seals of all joints of the primary circuit; 
3) Between the S4 state (cold) and the HU state (heat -up) - the temperature 
of the primary circuit coolant at the reactor outlet is less/more than 70 °C above zero; 
4) Between the S7 state (heat-up) and the S3 state (hot) - the temperature of 
the primary circuit coolant at the reactor inlet is less/more than 260 оС above zero; 
5) Between the S3 state (hot) and S2 state (MCPL) - all CPS CR groups are 
completely injected into the core/CPS CR groups extraction from the core is started; 
6) Between the S2 state (MCPL) and S1 state (power operation) - neutron 
power less/more than 1% Nnom; 
7) Between the S3 state (hot) and S8 (cooldown) - the temperature of the 
primary circuit coolant at the reactor inlet is more/less than 260 оС above zero; 
8) Between the S8 state (cooldown) and the S4 state (cold) - the 
temperature of the primary circuit coolant at the reactor outlet is more/less than  
700 оС above zero. 
2.3 Modes implemented during RP operation within NO and DNO states are 
selected in order to provide analysis of equipment strength and are given in  
Appendix C: 
- normal operation modes in Table C.1 (Appendix C); 
- modes of operation with deviations (failure modes) in Table C.2  
(Appendix C); 
- emergency modes in Table C.3 (Appendix C); 
2.4 The S1 operation state (“Power operation”) is characterized by the 
following values of the main parameters and characteristics: 
 the reactor is critical, Keff = 1 (in steady state); 
 reactor power is more than 1% Nnom; 
 primary circuit pressure P1 = (16.1±0.3) MPa (in steady state); 
[PAGE 11]
Rooppur NPP 
Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
9 
 primary circuit coolant temperature at reactor inlet is more than 285°С 
above zero; 
 steam pressure at SG outlet (6.7-6.9) ± 0.1 MPa; 
 at least two RCPS are in operation. 
2.5 The S2 operation state (MCPL) is characterized by the following values 
of the main parameters and characteristics: 
 Кeff ≤ 1; 
 reactor neutron power  ≤  1% Nnom; 
 primary circuit pressure PI = (16.1±0.3) MPa; 
 primary circuit coolant temperature at reactor inlet at the moment of 
reaching MCPL is more than 275 - 285оС above zero; 
 steam pressure at SG outlet is (5.8 - 6.7) MPa; 
 at least two RCPS are in operation. 
2.6 The S3 operation state (hot state) is characterized by the following 
values of basic parameters and characteristics: 
 all CPS CR on the bottom limit switches (or on LAS); 
 primary circuit coolant temperature at the reactor inlet is 2 75-284 оС above 
zero; 
 primary circuit pressure PI = (16.1±0.3) MPa; 
 steam pressure at SG outlet РII is 5,75 до 6,7 MPa; 
 the reactor is sub-critical, the conditions for ensuring sub-criticality depend 
on the further planned operation modes: 
1) at subsequent reaching MCPL - reactor sub -criticality at any time of the 
cycle at all CPS CR taken up is provided by boric acid. H3ВО3 concentration in the 
primary circuit provides subcriticality not less than 0.01 in the core state with the 
maximum effective multiplication factor without taking into  account the CPS CR 
inserted into the core and is determined in accordance with the album of neutron -
physical characteristics; 
2) during subsequent cooldown - sub-criticality, not less than 0.01, is provided 
by injected CPS CR taking into account the stick ing of one of the most effective CR. 
Prior to cooldown, boric acid concentration is provided in accordance with the 
requirement defined for S4 (“cold” state). 
2.7 The S4 operation state (cold state) is characterized by the following 
values of the main parameters and characteristics: 
 reactor is in sub -critical state, Н 3ВО3 concentration in the primary circuit 
provides at least 0.02 sub-criticality without taking into account the CPS CR injected 
into the core; 
 all CPS CR are on the bottom limit switches (or on LAS); 
 primary circuit coolant temperature at the reactor outlet is below 70 oC 
above zero; 
 combination of pressure and temperature of the reactor vessel meets the 
brittle fracture resistance criterion. 
[PAGE 12]
Rooppur NPP 
Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
10 
2.8 The S5 operation state (shutdown for repair) is characte rized by the 
following values of the main parameters and characteristics: 
 the reactor is sub -critical, Н 3ВО3 concentration in the primary circuit 
provides sub -criticality of at least 0.02 without taking into account the CPS CR 
injected into the core and i s determined in accordance with the album of neutron -
physical characteristics; 
 all CPS CR are on the bottom limit switches (or on LAS); 
 primary circuit is unsealed; 
 primary circuit coolant temperature at the reactor outlet is below 70 oC 
above zero; 
 primary circuit coolant pressure is equal to atmospheric one; 
 the level in the reactor shall be 300 -400 mm lower than the main reactor 
joint or reduced for repair work, but not lower than the level value by (600 ± 50) mm 
higher than the axis of the “cold” reactor nozzles; 
 a concentration of boric acid corresponding to the S6 state (refueling) shall 
be created in the primary circuit coolant in case of PTU extraction. 
2.9 The S6 operation state (refueling) is characterized by the following 
values of the main parameters and characteristics: 
 the reactor is subcritical, the concentration of Н3ВО3 in the primary 
circuit is at least 16 g/dm3 and provides subcriticality of at least 0.02 without taking 
into account CPS CR inserted into the core;  
 coolant temperature at reactor outlet is less than 60 °С above zero; 
 UU and PTU are removed; 
 RFP and FP are filled to the required level with Н 3ВО3 solution with a 
concentration of at least 16 g/dm3. 
 hydraulic lock is removed, reactor pit is combined with fuel pool. 
 
Note - the main parameters and characteristics are the parameters and characteris tics 
of the NPP, which significantly affect the parameters characterizing the NPP safety in 
the respective state. 
 
2.10 The S7 operation state (heat-up) is transient one from S4 to S3, in which 
tightness checks and hydraulic tests of the primary and secondary c ircuits are 
performed. In the process of heat -up, the operating personnel shall connect and/or 
monitor the readiness of Unit systems and equipment. 
The reactor in this state is sub -critical, Н 3ВО3 concentration in the primary 
circuit provides sub -criticality of at least 0.02 without taking into account the CPS 
CR injected into the core and is determined in accordance with the album of neutron -
physical characteristics; 
2.11 The S8 operation state (cooldown) is transient one from S3 to S4 in 
which, as the RP is cooled down, the operating personnel perform and/or monitor the 
shutdown of the appropriate systems and equipment of the Unit.  
[PAGE 13]
Rooppur NPP 
Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
11 
The reactor in this state is sub-critical. The Н3ВО3 concentration in the primary 
circuit provides sub -criticality of at least 0.02 without taking into account the CPS 
CR injected into the core and is determined in accordance with the album of neutron -
physical characteristics. 
2.12 Various operation modes at NPP can be considered within each state, 
including inspections and tests stipulated by the specification, which shall be taken 
into account when forming safe operation limits. 
2.13 Scheduled MT and repair of safety system channel are allowed in S6 
(refueling) and S5 (shutdown for repair) states only after completion of refueling 
when assembling the reactor.

3 Safe operation limits and conditions 
3.1 Limits of safe operation by process parameters 
3.1.1 Safe operation limits (SOL) are design -specified values of process 
parameters, deviations from which can lead to an accident. 
SOL characterize the possibility of radioactive substances and/or ionizing 
radiation release beyond the boundaries of physical barriers on the way of their 
spreading into the environment. 
3.1.2 SOL are divided as follows by impact on physical barriers: 
1) SOL by impact on the physical barrier are established for process 
parameters, the exceedance of which beyond these limits may lead to damage to the 
barrier. Exceeding the SOL by impact on the physical barrier indicates the RP 
changeover to the “pre-emergency” state. 
2) SOL by the physical barrier state are established for the process parameters  
that characterize the amount of radioactive substances and/or ionizing radiation that 
went beyond the design boundaries for normal operation. Exceeding the SOL by the 
physical barrier state indicates a disturbance of the physical barrier integrity and the  
fact of accident occurrence. 
3.1.3 Main RP parameters that determine the integrity of physical barriers 
and their limit values, deviation from which may lead to disturbance of safe operation 
limits are given in Table 3.1. 
3.1.4 Monitoring of parameters by which SOL a re established shall be 
performed in accordance with Table 3.1. 
3.1.5 The subsection shows the SOL in various states of the Unit normal 
operation, as well as personnel actions to change over the RP to a safe state when the 
SOL are exceeded. The range of process parameters determined by the established 
SOL is monitored by safety systems, which actuate when the controlled parameters 
reach the respective actuation setpoints. Safety system actuation setpoints are given 
in Appendix A of this specification. 
3.1.6 SOL for the  release of radionuclides from TPS with SNF are given in 
Table 3.2. 
3.1.7 SOL parameters that characterize the impact on the respective physical 
barriers are given in Table 3.4. 
3.1.8 Method and place of measurement of parameters of safe operation 
limits by impact on physical barriers are given in Table 3.3 
3.1.9 Information on the type of monitoring of the safe operation limit 
parameters with indication of necessary operating personnel actions in case of loss of 
monitoring equipment of the respective safe operation limits is given in Table 3.5. 
3.1.10 After disturbance of safe operation conditions and limits for equipment 
and pipelines, as well as in case of equipment failures, it is necessary to perform their 
extraordinary technical examination. 
[PAGE 17]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur 
NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
15 
3.1.11 In case of complete loss of the mon itoring equipment of the parameter 
that characterize SOL, including indirect methods, the subsequent operation of the 
Unit is not allowed and it shall be stopped. 
3.1.12 In case of disturbance of SOL, it is necessary to immediately perform: 
 shutdown of NPP Unit; 
 depending on the consequences of SOL disturbance: perform the necessary 
inspection procedures (inspection) of equipment (damaged physical barrier) or 
eliminate the consequences of SOL disturbance.  
 perform repair work (if necessary) and inspection of the r espective  
equipment to exclude the general cause of SOL disturbance; 
 perform the reliability analysis of indications of the monitoring equipment 
of the parameter that characterize the SOL. 
3.1.13 In case of SOL disturbance, the operating personnel shall change o ver 
the reactor plant to the S5 state (shutdown for repair). In case of SOL disturbance in 
the S5 state, this state shall be preserved until the disturbance consequences are 
eliminated. 
3.1.14 In case of SOL disturbance, the operating organization shall investiga te 
the disturbance causes and consequences to exclude the occurrence of such 
disturbance in the future. 
3.1.15 Inspection is performed for a physical barrier that has been 
overexposed from a parameter for which SOL is established. 
3.1.16 In case of disturbance of SOL th at characterize the impact on the first 
or second physical barriers, it is necessary to identify FAs that have been subjected to 
excessive impact that lead to SOL disturbance. 
3.1.17 For these FAs, perform CIM and, based on the results, decide on the 
method of their further storage in the FP. 
3.1.18 In case of disturbance of SOL by the level of activity of reference 
radionuclides in the primary circuit coolant and confirmation (fulfillment of sampling 
conditions, steady state, operation of primary circuit coolant purific ation systems) of 
a disturbance, the operating personnel shall shut down the reactor plant, change it 
over to the S5 state (shutdown for repair) with further performance of CIM of all FAs 
to identify leaky FAs and replace them. 
3.1.19 In case of disturbance of a SOL that characterizes the impact on the 
primary circuit coolant boundary or on the secondary pressure boundary, the metal of 
equipment and pipelines shall be inspected by the respective monitoring systems to 
identify possible defects, discontinuities, cracks, etc., which can lead to the formation 
of primary or secondary circuit coolant leaks in the process of further operation. 
3.1.20 Further operation of the equipment and pipelines is possible only with 
the approval of the respective equipment/pipelines designer  with an additional 
assessment of the impact of SOL disturbance on the equipment life and approval of 
the supervisory authority. 
3.1.21 In case of integrity disturbance of the boundaries of the third physical 
barrier and the formation of a leak, as a result of wh ich the limits of safe operation 
[PAGE 18]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur 
NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
16 
were disturbed, the operating personnel shall shut down the reactor and change over 
the Unit to the S5 state (shutdown for repair). These actions reduce the impact of 
leakage on radiation consequences for personnel and the public within the established 
dose limits. Further personnel actions to isolate the leak, restore the operable state of 
the primary circuit boundary are performed depending on the place of leakage and the 
radiation situation in the NPP premises. 
3.1.22  In case o f disturbance of SOL that characterize the impact on the 
second physical barrier of FA in the fuel pool (item 6, item 12 of Table 3.1), it is 
necessary to make a decision on the method of further storage of FA available at the 
time of disturbance in the fu el pool, as well as on methods for eliminating the 
consequences (if any) of safe operation limit disturbance agreed with the nuclear fuel 
supplier and approved by the operating organization.

3.1.23 In case of SOL disturbance, the operating personnel shall: 
 perform (monitoring of) NPP Unit shutdown; 
 depending on the consequences of SOL disturbance, perform the necessary 
inspection procedures (inspection) of e quipment corresponding to the potentially 
damaged physical barrier or eliminate the consequences of SOL disturbance. 
3.1.24 After the repair work (if necessary), the respective equipment shall be 
inspected to exclude the general cause of SOL disturbance and indic ations reliability 
of the monitoring equipment of the parameter that characterizes the SOL, for which a 
disturbance was detected, shall be analyzed. 
[PAGE 30]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP 
Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
28 
3.1.25  In case of violation of the safe operation limits, the operating personnel 
changes over the reactor plant to the S5 state (shutdown for repair) and takes 
appropriate measures to eliminate the cause of the violation, including transfer of the 
RP to a safe state and prevention of the violation consequences. In case of SOL 
disturbance in the S5 state, this state shall be preserved until the disturbance 
consequences are eliminated. 
3.1.26 In case of disturbance of safe operation limits that characterize the 
impact on the first or second physical barriers, it is necessary to identify FAs that 
have been subjected to excessi ve impact resulting in the safe operation limit 
disturbance. 
For these FAs, CIM shall be performed and a decision shall be made on the 
method of their further storage in the fuel pool based on the results. 
3.1.27 Further operation of these FAs and their use in en ergy production is 
possible only with the approval of the FE/GFE designer and the approval of the PRB 
supervisory authority (BAERA). 
3.1.28 In case of safe operation limit disturbance by the level of activity of 
reference radionuclides in the primary circuit coolant and confirmation (fulfillment of 
sampling conditions, steady state, operation of primary circuit coolant purification 
systems) of a disturbance, the operating personnel shall shut down the reactor plant, 
change it over to the S5 state (shutdown for rep air) with further performance of CIM 
of all FAs to identify leaky FAs and replace them. 
3.1.29 In case of disturbance of a safe operation limit that characterizes the 
impact on the primary circuit coolant boundary or on the secondary pressure 
boundary, the metal of equipment and pipelines shall be inspected by the respective 
monitoring systems to identify possible defects, discontinuities, cracks, etc., which 
can lead to the formation of primary or secondary circuit coolant leaks in the process 
of further operation. 
3.1.30 Further operation of the equipment and pipelines is possible only with 
the approval of the respective equipment/pipelines designer with an additional 
assessment of the impact of safe operation limit disturbance on the equipment life and 
approval of the PRB supervisory authority (BAERA). 
3.1.31 In case of integrity disturbance of the boundaries of the third physical 
barrier and the formation of a leak, as a result of which the limits of safe operation 
were disturbed, the operating personnel shall shut down the r eactor and change over 
the Unit to the S5 state (shutdown for repair). Further personnel actions to isolate the 
leak, restore the operable state of the primary circuit boundary are performed 
depending on the place of leakage and the radiation situation in the NPP premises. 
3.1.32 In case of disturbance of SOL that characterize the impact on the 
second physical barrier of FA in the fuel pool (item 6, item 12 of Table 3.1), it is 
necessary to make a decision on the method of further storage of FA available at the 
time of disturbance in the fuel pool, as well as on methods for eliminating the 
consequences (if any) of safe operation limit disturbance agreed with the nuclear fuel 
manufacturer, general designer and approved by the operating organization.

Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP 
Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2

3.2 Safe operation limits by radiation parameters 
3.2.1 NPP safe operation limits are values of design process parameters, 
deviations from which can lead to an accident.  
3.2.2 An accident is a disturbance in the NPP operation, at which radioactive 
substances and/or ionizing radiation we re released beyond the design limits for 
normal operation in quantities exceeding the established limits of safe operation. 
3.2.3 Monitoring of process parameters, maintaining them within operation 
limits during normal operation and limitation during operation w ith deviations 
provides prevention of safe operation limits disturbance. 
3.2.4 Disturbance of SOL characterizes the possibility of release of radioactive 
substances and/or ionizing radiation due to the damage to the physical barrier on the 
way of ionizing radiation and radioactive substances spread into the environment. 
3.2.5 In case of disturbance of safe operation limits by radiation parameters 
when being in the S1 state (power operation), S2 (MCPL) the reactor plant shall be 
immediately stopped with EP button and changed over to the S4 state (cold state). 
In case of disturbance of safe operation limits by radiation parameters when 
being in the S3, S7, S8 states, it is immediately changed over to the S4 state. 
The reactor plant is changed over to the S5 state (shutdow n for repair) to 
eliminate safe operation limit disturbance by radiation parameters in the S4 state.  
3.2.6 In case of SOL disturbance in the S5 state, this state shall be preserved 
until the disturbance consequences are eliminated.  
3.2.7 SOL for the NPP Unit for emi ssions and discharges in accordance with 
SP AS -03 are set at the level of admissible discharges (AD) and maximum 
permissible emissions (MPE), and are given in Tables 3.6 and 3.7. 
3.2.8 The SOL and EP values set for one NPP Unit shall not exceed the value 
during operation of all two NPP Units.  
3.2.9 The upper boundary (quota) of the annual population exposure dose from 
gas-aerosol emissions and discharges for the entire NPP site shall be in the amount of 
100 μSv/year. This quota is divided into two equal parts between gas -aerosol 
emissions and liquid discharges - 50 μSv for each of these radiation factors. 
3.2.9.1 Upper boundary (quota) for population exposure from emissions and 
discharges during NPP normal operation, μSv per year is given in Tables 3.6 and 3.7. 
3.2.9.2 Annual operation limits (OL) for emissions are s et at the level of 
permissible emissions (PE), annual operation limits (OL) for discharges are set at the 
level of 20% of admissible discharges (AD). 
3.2.10 The lower boundary (target limit) of the annual effective population 
exposure dose is established as the t arget limit when optimizing radiation protection 
in normal operation mode. This value for both gas -aerosol emissions and liquid 
discharges is 10 μSv/year per one Unit

3.2.11 Primary circuit coolant leakage into blowdown water and 131I 
radionuclide specific activity value in SG blowdown water a ccording to safe 
operation limits: 
 limit value of primary circuit coolant leakage for individual steam 
generators is 5 kg/h; 
 the limit value of reduced specific activity of 131I in blowdown water from 
the “salt” compartment of each steam generator of the Unit is 740 Bq/kg. 
3.3 Operational conditions 
3.3.1 List of operational conditions and their scope in different RP states are 
given in Table 3.8 “Operational conditions (OCs) and their scope in different RP 
states”, 
3.3.1.1 It is prohibited to operate the Unit equipment that  has exhausted its 
design life of cyclic loading. Operation can be continued if the substantiation analysis 
submitted by the operating organization is agreed under the established procedure. 
Restrictions on equipment loading conditions are given in Appendix C. 
3.3.1.2 Disturbance of OCs shall be recorded at the moment of start of RP 
shutdown to the hot or cold state (or changeover to “shutdown for repair” state from 
cold state) given in column 6 of Table 3.8. Disturbance elimination in the initial 
(current) RP state within the permissible time given in column 5 of Table 3.8 is not a 
disturbance of OCs (the time specified in brackets in column 5 corresponds to the 
initial RP state given in brackets in column 2).

1.1.2 JNG50 emergency reactor core cooling system (passive part) 
1.1.2.1 ECCS passive part is operable. 
Each accumulator shall contain boric 
acid solution with a temperature 20-70 
°С above zero, concentration 16-20 
g/dm3 at nitrogen pressure in tanks (5.9 
±0.1) MPa and solution level in tanks 
(7350±50) mm. The system is connected 
to the primary circuit (except for the 
primary circuit hydraulic tests mode) in 
the “heat-up” state at a pressure in the 
primary circuit of more than 6.37 MPa. 
The system is disconnected from the 
primary circuit in the “cooldown” state 
with a decrease in the primary circuit 
pressure less than 8.83 - 9.81 MPa

4 Operation limits  and conditions 
4.1 Operation limits by process parameters 
4.1.1 Operation limits (OL) - values of parameters and characteristics of the 
state of system (components) and NPP as a whole set in the design project for norm al 
operation. 
4.1.2 Operation conditions (OC) - conditions necessary for operation without 
violation of operation limits by the number of operating systems (components) and 
conditions by characteristics and state of operability of systems (components). 
4.1.3 OL are established in order to ensure limitations on the implementation 
(minimization of the number) of transient modes with disturbances of normal 
operation of the Unit, to ensure actuation failure (minimization of the number of 
actuations) of safety systems due t o the action of limitation functions being put into 
operation by process protections and interlocks, or prescribed personnel actions. 
4.1.4 Compliance with OL shall be checked constantly, recording - at least 
once a shift. 
4.1.5 The subsection contains OL that charact erize the integrity of physical 
barriers and the performance of safety functions, the boundaries of their action in 
various RP states, the automatic actions of controllers, interlocks, protection and 
personnel actions to maintain the parameter (characteris tics) within the operation 
limits. Protection actuation setpoints, power operation, reaching MCPL are given in 
the appendix to this specification, setpoints of automatic actions of controllers, 
interlocks are described in the operation instructions of the respective systems. 
4.1.6 OL and OC of safety related systems (components) (SRS) are specified 
in the operation instructions for the respective systems. 
4.1.7 It is prohibited to operate the SRS equipment in cases of deviation of its 
characteristics from OL or beyond the tolerances specified in manufacturer data 
sheets and operation instructions. 
4.1.8 Operation of equipment and systems in non -design-basis modes of 
equipment operation is allowed only in case of beyond design -basis accidents 
according to the duly agreed procedures. 
4.1.9 Table 4.1 shows the operation limits of measured and calculated 
parameters that characterize the state (integrity) of physical barriers. 
4.1.10 Table 4.2 shows the operation limits of measured and calculated 
parameters that characterize the impact on physi cal barriers and performance of 
safety functions. 
4.1.11 Table 4.3 shows the operation limits of the parameters of the primary 
circuit and SG during the tightness check and during hydraulic strength tests. 
4.1.12 OL for quality of working media of primary and secondary circuits, as 
well as operation limitations and personnel actions in case of deviation from them are 
defined in Appendix D.

4.2 Operation limits for power density irregularity. 
Power density irregularity factors by core volume Kv(i,j) monitored by 
MCDS indications shall not exceed Kv lim.(i,j) determined by the following ratio: 
Kv lim (i,j) = Kv perm(i,j)/(0.17+0.83Ncur/Nperm),  
where i is the number  of the elevation layer of the core with numbering from 
the core bottom (i=1,2,...,n);  
j - FA number (j = 1,2,..., 163);  
n - number of monitored layers by core height;  
Kv perm(i,j) - maximum permissible value Kv(i,j) at the nominal reactor 
power level;  
Ncur - current reactor power;  
Nperm - permissible reactor power depending on the number of operating 
RCPS.  
For the first cycle, the array Kv perm(i,j) for all FA (for all j values) is set 
based on the data given in Table 4.4. 
Table 4.4 - Power density value by core height 
Name Value 
Coordinate from the core bottom, %  7.1 21.4 35.7 50.0 64.3 78.6 92.9 
Volume power density irregularity 
factor, Kv perm(i,j) 1.90 1.90 1.90 1.90 1.74 1.58 1.42 
Note - with an arbitrary number of monitoring points, the values of Kv perm(i,j) above 50% of the 
core bottom are determined by linear interpolation from 1.90 (by the height of 50%) to 1.33 by the 
height of 100%  
For the second and all subsequent fuel loads, the calculation of the maximum 
permissible values of volu metric power density Kv perm(i,j) for each FA is 
performed in accordance with the procedure developed by OKB GIDROPRESS. 
Specific values of Kv perm(i,j) are determined during neutron -physical calculations 
and shall be given in the “NPH Report” and “NPH Alb um” for each current load. 
Values of factors Kv perm(i,j) for different moments of fuel loading are calculated 
with time increments of not more than 40 effective days. In this case, the minimum 
values of the factors from ones obtained at the boundaries of this interval are used at 
the burnup intervals.  
Limit values Kv perm(i,j) are set in MCDS as alarm setpoint and change 
automatically depending on the current value of reactor power.  
Algorithms for prevention and elimination of exceeding the maximum 
permissible values of Kv(i,j) are given in Appendix F.  
4.3 Operation limits for current frequency deviation conditions in the 
power system 
[PAGE 166]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
164 
RP operation is allowed in conditions of current frequency deviation in the 
power system from the nominal value given the following time limits: 
- in the range of 50.5 - 51.0 Hz - not more than 3 minutes in each individual 
case and not more than 500 minutes for the entire service life;  
- in the range of 49.0 - 50.5 Hz - without limitations;  
- in the range of 49.0 - 48.0 Hz - not more than 5 minutes in each individual 
case and not more than 750 minutes for the entire service life;  
- in the range of 48.0 - 47.0 Hz - not more than 1 min in each individual case 
and not more than 180 min for the entire service life;  
- in the range  of 47.0 - 46.0 Hz - not more than 10 s in each individual case 
and not more than 30 minutes for the entire service life.

4.4 Operation limits for radiation parameters 
4.4.1 In accordance with Chapter 16 of the SAR, It em 16.2.1.24.1, the 
operation limits for emissions of radioactive gases and aerosols into the atmosphere 
of the Rooppur NPP Unit shall be set at the level of annual permissible emissions of 
radionuclides (PE).  
4.4.2 A minimum significant dose equal to 10 μSv per year is taken as the 
lower limit of the radiation dose from a separate radiation factor, when optimizing 
radiation protection of the population in the NPP normal operation mode. 
4.4.3 The radiation risk for the popul ation during NPP operation is certainly 
acceptable (< 1·10-6  per year) given the technically achieved level of NPP safety in 
the normal operation mode (when actual NPP emissions and discharges create a dose 
of exposure of persons from the population less than 10 μSv per year for each impact 
factor). In this regard, the values of permissible emissions (hereinafter referred to as 
PE) and admissible discharges (hereinafter referred to as AD) are calculated based on 
the population exposure dose of 10 μSv per year.  
4.4.4 The procedure for monitoring compliance with the SOL at  the request of 
the RSD of the REA branch shall be brought into line with the SAR, when the 
condition for compliance with the SOL appears in the latter. 
4.4.5 The main contribution to the population ex posure dose in the NPP 
normal operation mode by inert radioactive gases (argon, krypton, xenon) and 131I, 
60Co, 134Cs, 137Cs radionuclides is taken into account when establishing annual PE of 
radioactive gases and aerosols into the atmosphere. Rationing an d monitoring the 
activity of other radionuclides detected in NPP emissions is impractical due to their 
negligible contribution to the radiation dose. 
4.4.6 The annual permissible release of radioactive gases and aerosols from 
NPP into the atmosphere is given in Table 4.6 in accordance with Table 11.3.3.2.1 of 
Chapter 11 and Table 16.2.1.24.1 of Chapter 16 of the SAR. 
Table 4.6 - Annual permissible emission of radioactive gases and aerosols from the 
NPP into the atmosphere (PE)

experimental studies. Clarification is made by the operating organization and is 
specified at the SAR stage. The standards for permissible emissions of radioactive 
gases and aerosols into the atmosphere, as well as reference levels are developed and 
established by the operating organization and are specified at the SAR stage.  
4.4.7 In accordance with Item 16.2.1.24.1 of Chapter 16 of the SAR, the 
operation limit for the release of radioactive gases and aerosols into the atmosphere is 
set at the level of annual permissible emission (PE). 
4.4.8 In accordance with Item 5.15 of SanPiN 2.6.1.24 -03 “Sanitary 
regulations for nuclear plant design and operation (SP AS -03)”, the maximum 
permissible release of radioactive substances (MPE) for NPPs under design and 
construction is set at the level 5 of PE.

5 Safe operation rules and main methods  
5.1 Unit operation in the “cold” state  
5.1.1 Operational conditions in “cold” state. 
Requirements for Unit operation organization are defined in Section 9. 
5.1.1.1 Before the Unit is changed over to “cold” state, the operational 
conditions given in Table 3.8 for this state shall be met. 
5.1.1.2 Before the Unit is changed over to “cold” state, the requireme nts for 
the state of operability of systems and equipment given in column 4, Table G.1, 
Appendix G of this specification shall be met. 
5.1.1.3 “Cold” state is characterized by the following RP conditions and 
parameters: 
- the reactor is sub-critical, all CPS CR are on BLS or on lower abutment stops; 
- all CPS drive rods are engaged with their CPS AR. The engagement of drive 
rods with CPS AR was checked; 
- electric joints are connected to CPS drives; 
- electric connection of power density monitoring channels and tem perature 
monitoring channels with ICIS equipment was performed using plug connectors; 
- boric acid concentration in the primary circuit coolant provides reactor sub -
criticality of at least 2% (excluding CPS CR submerged into the core); 
- difference of boric acid concentrations in the primary circuit and PRZ is less 
than 0.5 g/dm3; 
- primary circuit coolant temperature in the primary circuit at the reactor outlet 
is not more than 70 °С above zero; 
- level in SG (from 3700 to 3800 mm) mm  
Note - Nominal level in SG is specified based on test results (SAW); 
- primary circuit pressure: 
a) not more than 1.96 MPa when reactor coolant circuit emergency and 
planned cooldown and fuel pool cooling system is connected to the primary circuit; 
b)  not more than 3.43 MPa in all the other cases. 
- reactor coolant circuit emergency and planned cooldown and fuel pool 
cooling system is in operation to remove residual FA heat; 
- primary circuit is sealed; 
- pressurizer safety devices shall be serviceable on the reactor with sealed 
primary circuit, except for pressure tests. 
c) Measures have been taken to prevent pressurization of the primary circuit 
with a pressure above 3.43 MPa: 
- electric circuits of TEH units are disassembled; 
- electric circuits of JND emergency boron injection syst em pumps are 
disassembled; 
[PAGE 178]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
176 
- the electric circuits of JNА12(22)АР001 high pressure pumps of the reactor 
coolant circuit emergency and planned cooldown and fuel pool cooling system are 
disassembled; 
- the pressure in the ECCS HA is not more than 3.43 MPa; if this condition is 
not met, the valves on the HA-reactor line shall be closed, locked, the electric circuits 
shall be disassembled; 
- I&CD measuring channels are actuated for measuring pressure in the primary 
circuit; 
- the primary circuit overpressure protection is put into operat ion that switches 
off the makeup pumps and PRZ TEH and enables a ban on opening the fast -acting 
gate valves of the ECCS passive part when the primary circuit pressure rises above 
3.43 MPa in case the primary circuit coolant temperature is below 100 ºС. 
d) Operability check of SG SV PD from ADP at SG pressure not more than 0.1 
MPa shall be performed during PPM with refueling after repair works on SG POSV. 
5.1.2 General procedure for performance of safety related operations 
5.1.2.1 It is allowed to increase the primary circuit pressure to 3.43 MPa with 
the primary circuit coolant temperature at the reactor inlet of at least 50 ºС above zero 
and the temperature of the outer wall of the reactor vessel of a t least 15 ºС above 
zero. 
5.1.2.2 The level in the PRZ shall be maintained from (10900 ± 150) mm to 
300÷400 mm below the MRJ before putting the RP into the “shutdown for repair” 
state. 
5.1.2.3 Optical-acoustic acceleration indicators (OAI) of NFME set in 
operation are swi tched on. Protection setpoints for power level and acceleration 
period are set in accordance with the requirements of the design and operation 
instructions. 
5.1.2.4 The JNB51,52,61,62,71,72,81,82AA001,002,003 PHRS air gates shall 
be in closed position, the JNB50,6 0,70,80AA001,002,003,004 shut -off valves on 
PHRS steam -condensate path shall be in open position. The 
JNB51,52,61,62,71,72,81,82AA004 cooling air flow rate control devices are 
connected to the secondary circuit. 
5.1.2.5 The primary circuit equipment joint tightnes s monitoring system is in 
operation. There is no pressure in the inter-gasket space of the joints. 
5.1.2.6 After the refueling ends: 
- safety devices and cross-beam are installed on the UU; 
- hydraulic lock is installed between the FP and reactor pit; 
- FP is filled with boric acid solution with concentration of 16 - 20 g/dm3 to the 
level of 25.35 - 25.55 m, including in the absence of spent fuel. Quality indicators of 
primary circuit coolant when filling the primary circuit and FP water comply with the 
requirements of Appendix D; 
- drains to containment are open from FP container compartment, RVI 
inspection cavities and PTU. 
[PAGE 179]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
177 
5.1.2.7 The ECCS HA of stages 1, 2 and the PCFS tanks are filled to the 
nominal level with a boric acid solution with a concentration of at least 16 g /dm3 and 
a temperature of at least 200 ºС above zero, the concentration shall be monitored 
continuously and automatically. The quality of the solution for the rest of the 
parameters shall comply with the requirements of Appendix D and be checked at 
least twice a month, as well as during filling and additional filling. 
5.1.2.8 At least the one KPM channel is in operation (containment system), to 
which blow -offs are directed from the reactor compartment equipment (pressure 
relief tank, controlled leakage heat exchanger, controlled leakage tank, primary 
circuit coolant storage tanks). 
5.1.2.9 Operational diagnostics systems (put into commercial operation) shall 
be in operation in the scope sufficient to ensure monitoring of the parameters of the 
diagnosed equipment in operation or on standby. 
5.1.2.10 The standard search and telephone operational communication with 
the premises and workplaces of the Unit, as well as direct communication channels 
(FD, security, etc.) have been checked and are serviceable. 
5.1.3 Rules and basic methods of safe operation in the “cold” state. 
5.1.3.1 If necessary, the RCPS system (pump with auxiliary systems) shall be 
operable: 
1) long-term operation of one, two and three RCPS at the primary circuit 
coolant pressure of at least 1.47 MPa is allowed (Appendix E to this specificati on) 
and the availability of a nitrogen blanket in the pressurizer; 
2) it is allowed to perform two RCPS start -ups in a row from the cold state to 
the nominal rotation rate. It is allowed to start the RCPS at the return flow of the 
primary circuit coolant in the loop (with other operating RCPS). 
5.1.3.2 Additional filling and check of primary circuit tightness with pressure 
of 3.2 MPa: 
1) additional filling of the primary circuit is performed by KBA makeup 
pumps. Before starting additional filling, make sure that the qual ity of the boric acid 
solution supplied to the makeup pumps suction meets the requirements of  
Appendix D; 
2) perform additional filling with boric acid solution with concentration of 
16÷20 g/dm3 and temperature of (20÷60) ºС above zero at open air vent valve s of the 
reactor, SG, PRZ, nuclear circuits of RCPS. 
It is prohibited to fill the primary circuit if the makeup water temperature 
differs from the metal temperature of the reactor vessel, RCPS, RCPL, SG by more 
than 30 ºС above zero. 
3) raise the primary circ uit pressure to 0.49 MPa upon completion of the 
primary circuit additional filling; 
4) at pressure of 0.49 MPa perform air removal from all air vent valves of 
the primary circuit. Inspect the primary circuit equipment for leaks; 
[PAGE 180]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
178 
5) before the primary circuit pre ssure rises above 1.47 MPa, disconnect the 
low pressure pipelines of the reactor plant auxiliary systems, except for the pipelines 
of the emergency planned cooldown system and the FP cooldown system (JNA); 
6) makeup water flow rate shall be not more than 40 m 3/h at PRZ level up to 
5100 mm and not more than 20 m3/h at PRZ level more than 5100 mm. 
7) Makeup water flow rate shall be reduced to the minimum 10÷15 m 3/h at 
PRZ level of 10.900 mm; 
8) monitoring of primary circuit filling shall be performed by the level in 
PRZ and in the reactor; 
9) closing of air vent valves of the primary circuit after 30 minutes of 
blowdown through air vent valves to drain system; 
10) disconnect the JNA reactor coolant circuit emergency and planned 
cooldown and fuel pool cooling system before pre ssure rise in the primary circuit 
above 1.96 MPa; 
11) increase pressure in the primary circuit to 3.2 MPa. The rate of pressure 
change in the reactor shall not exceed 0.49 MPa per minute; 
12) inspect the primary circuit equipment for leaks at a pressure of 3.2 MPa . 
Check the absence of pressure in the inter -gasket space of reactor joints, PRZ, SG, 
ECCS HA of stages 1, 2 and RCPS. Check the absence of leaks through the internal 
gaskets of flange joints of CPS drives, ICDA outputs. In the availability of leaks, 
release pressure, eliminate them and perform the tightness tests again; 
13) reduce the pressure in the primary circuit to the value of 2.4 MPa and 
maintain this pressure during the secondary circuit testing for tightness with a 
pressure of 1.96 MPa. When the primar y circuit pressure drops to 1.96 MPa, connect 
the JNA reactor coolant circuit emergency and planned cooldown and fuel pool 
cooling system to the primary circuit. 
5.1.3.3 Filling and testing of SG tightness over the secondary circuit with 
pressure of 1.96 MPa: 
1) check the state of the secondary circuit boundary valves; disconnect low 
pressure pipelines of secondary circuit auxiliary systems; 
2) filling of SG to the level from 3700 to 3800 mm shall be performed with 
feedwater by AFWP operation from the deaerator at open a ir vent valves over the 
secondary circuit and shall be completed before the primary circuit test for tightness 
of 3.2 MPa. 
3) feedwater quality meets the requirements of Appendix D, water 
temperature - (20÷60) °С above zero and shall not differ from SG metal temperature 
by more than 60 °С above zero. 
4) perform additional filling of SG and raise the secondary circuit pressure in 
stages to 0.49 MPa and 1.96 MPa, inspect secondary circuit equipment for leaks; 
5) when checking the secondary circuit tightness, it is prohibited to reduce 
the primary circuit pressure below the secondary circuit pressure according to nuclear 
safety conditions in order to avoid secondary-to-primary circuit leaks. 
[PAGE 181]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
179 
6) reduce pressur e and drain the secondary circuit to the level in each SG 
(3700÷3800) mm. 
5.1.3.4 The indications of I&CD measuring channels of the primary and 
secondary circuits were checked, if necessary, the pulse lines of the sensors were 
blown down. 
5.1.3.5 The pressure relief tank gas volume shall be continuously blow down 
over the design circuit. Hydrogen content in the pressure relief tank gas volume shall 
not exceed the nominal value (3% volumetric). 
5.1.3.6 In order to prevent explosive concentrations of hydrogen in the primary 
circuit in the “cold” state mode, ensure the following: 
1) injection of boric acid and water exchange during cooldown is 
performed at maximum blowdown of the primary circuit with provision of at least 
three-fold water exchange of the primary circuit coolant until the  temperature is less 
than 100C above zero with monitoring of hydrogen concentration and activity in the 
primary circuit coolant; 
2) hydrazine and ammonia are not dosed into make -up water in “cold 
state”; 
3) after pressure release and lowering the level in the r eactor to MRJ, it is 
necessary to provide the dismantling of UU or disassembly of three central CPS 
drives with the extraction of of the motion unit within no more than a day and arrange 
nitrogen blowdown over the path: nitrogen system → reactor → CPS driv e 
housings→ central hall, with monitoring of hydrogen concentration in the central hall 
air; 
4) if long -term reactor staying in the assembled state is required, provide 
the water level corresponding to the axis of the “hot” RCPL legs, reactor and SG 
ventilation over the path: nitrogen system → air vent valves of the headers of each 
SG → reactor air vent valve → housings of three CPS drives → central hall, with 
monitoring of hydrogen concentration in the central hall air. 
5) when the RP is in downtime for more tha n two days and the reactor is 
assembled with the UU, the SG headers shall be unsealed with the nitrogen 
ventilation of the volume under the reactor cover. 
6) as an alternative, a diagram of nitrogen ventilation of the upper points of 
the RP equipment without unsealing of the CPS drives and SG headers using the 
equipment of the emergency gas removal system and hydrogen combustion system 
can be used. For this purpose, ensure that the water level corresponds to the axis of 
the hot legs of the RCPL. To remove hydr ogen from the upper point of the reactor, 
nitrogen is supplied to the air ducts of the headers of all SG, then the gas medium 
flows through the hot legs of the RCPL through the reactor air ducts and the PRZ, 
and then through the pipelines of the emergency gas removal system through the 
bypass, bypassing the pressure relief tank, to the hydrogen combustion system. To 
remove hydrogen from the upper points of SG headers, nitrogen is supplied to the 
reactor air duct, then the gas medium is supplied to the hydro gen combustion system 
by hot legs of the RCPL through the air ducts of SG and PRZ headers, and then to the 
[PAGE 182]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
180 
emergency gas removal system through the pipelines bypassing the pressure relief 
tank. 
5.2 Unit operation in the “heat-up” state 
5.2.1 Operational conditions in “heat-up” state 
Requirements for Unit operation organization are defined in Section 9 
“Operation organization”. 
The operational conditions given in Table 3.8 of subsection 3.3.1 for this state 
shall be met before Unit changeover to “heat-up” state. 
The requirements for the state of operability of systems and equipment given in 
column 5, Table G.1, Appendix G of this specification shall be met before Unit 
changeover to “heat-up” state. 
The RP “heat-up” state is characterized by the following conditions: 
- the reactor is sub-critical, all CPS CR are on BLS; 
- concentration of boric acid solution in the primary circuit coolant provides 
reactor sub-criticality of at least 2% (excluding CPS CR submerged into the core).  
The following shall be in operation: 
- emergency planned cooldown system, if primary circuit pressure is less than 
2.1 MPa and primary circuit coolant temperature is less than 130 °C above zero; 
- at least one RCPS, if the reactor coolant circuit emergency and planned 
cooldown and fuel pool cooli ng system is not in operation and a nitrogen blanket is 
created in PRZ, it is allowed to disconnect the RCPS for the duration of hydraulic 
tests of the primary circuit for tightness and strength, as well as for the duration of 
connection of the emergency p lanned cooldown system to the primary circuit. At the 
same time, check the availability of a boiling margin of at least 15 °С above zero; 
- component cooling system water shall be supplied to RCPS at primary circuit 
coolant temperature of more than 70 °С above zero.  
 Pressure relief tank is filled to nominal level of 1700 mm. Integrity of its 
rupture discs was checked. Water temperature within the specified limits is 20÷60 °С 
above zero. Systems for maintaining the level and blow-offs from pressure relief tank 
are ready for operation. 
State of the main circuit of Unit electric connections, as well as power supply 
systems and equipment of the Unit auxiliaries: 
- protection, control, monitoring, automation systems, including circuit-breaker 
failure protection devices, are in operation with design settings of equipment of the 
main circuit of electric connections put into operation;  
- unit transformers carry the load of Unit auxiliaries and standby auxiliary 10 
kV lines are set under voltage from auxiliary standby transformers (AST);  
- 10ВВА, 10ВВВ, 10ВВС and 10ВВD 10 kV normal operation sections are 
powered by auxiliary standby transformers (AT). The switches of standby inputs of 
these sections are ready for operation with the respective ALT, protection and control 
devices;  
[PAGE 183]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
181 
- the 0.4 kV sections are powered by the operating inputs. Standby input 
switches with respective ALT, protection and control devices are prepared for 
operation;  
- auxiliary power supply system components (including power supply 
components - AT, AST) and auxiliary loads are ready for operation with the 
necessary settings of protection, control, monitoring, automation and support systems 
(ventilation, air conditioning, lighting, etc.), as well as fire alarm and automatic fire 
extinguishing;  
- DC boards are powered according to standard circuits, storage batteries are 
fully charged and are in constant recharging mode; 
- MCR and ECR power supply is provided from operating and standby power 
supply sections, power is supplied to local control boards of Unit systems;  
- operating and emergency lighting of MCR and ECR is provided from 
operating and standby power supply sections.  
During RP heat -up, corrective treatment systems, turbine condensate 
purification and secondary circuit working medium qu ality control plant shall be 
operable. 
The quality of demineralized water supplied before start -up for filling and 
makeup of the secondary circuit shall meet the requirements given in Appendix D. 
During heat -up, the rate of pressure change in the primary c ircuit shall not 
exceed 0.98 MPa per minute. 
It is prohibited to raise the primary circuit pressure more than 3.43 MPa if the 
temperature of metal of the primary circuit equipment is less than that specified in 
Tables C.4 and C.5 of Appendix C of this spec ification, if the temperature of the 
primary circuit coolant is less than 105 ºС above zero in the initial period of operation 
and later in accordance with Table C.6 of Appendix C. 
The following conditions shall be provided for PRZ during heat-up: 
- PRZ TEH are operable;  
- the primary circuit pressure controller is operable;  
- PRZ level maintenance controller is set to automatic mode.  
LAB main feedwater pipeline system is in operation: 
- LAA deaeration and feeding plant is put into operation; 
- pre-start washing of the condensate and feedwater path with subsequent 
filling of SG is performed;  
- LAH auxiliary feedwater system IS put into operation, AFWP is in operation;  
- at least two FWP out of five are ready for operation;  
- shut-off and control valves are put into operation;  
- I&CD, PPI, alarm are put into operation in full scope.  
Water chemistry of steam generators meets the requirements given in 
Appendix D. The body temperature during filling is from 20 to 60 ºС above zero. In 
SG, water levels shal l be maintained from 3700 to 3800 mm at the heat -up stage to 
170 - 180 ºС above zero. 
[PAGE 184]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
182 
It is prohibited to raise pressure in SG over the secondary circuit more than 2.5 
MPa if the metal temperature of the secondary circuit components is less than one 
specified in Table C.5 of Appendix C, if the water temperature in SG is less than 110 
ºС above zero (Table C.7 of Appendix C). 
The required pressure in the primary circuit shall be provided due to the 
creation of a nitrogen blanket in the PRZ at the water temper ature in the PRZ below 
210 ºС above zero at the initial stage of the heat-up mode. 
When the water temperature in the PRZ is higher than 210 - 230 ºС above zero, 
it is necessary to replace the nitrogen blanket in the PRZ with steam by gas blow -off 
from the PRZ. After that, the pressure in the primary circuit is provided by exceeding 
the water temperature in the PRZ over the water temperature in the RCC. The excess 
shall be maintained by the cooldown controller at 55 ºС above zero. 
It is not allowed to start TEH units at water level in the PRZ less than 3600 
mm. 
Operation of more than three RCPS is prohibited at primary circuit temperature 
less than 200 ºС above zero. 
The temperature difference between the metal of the upper and lower parts of 
the SG housing during heat-up shall not exceed 40 ºС above zero. 
5.2.2 General procedure for performance of safety related operations 
5.2.2.1. The following stages of works are performed during reactor plant 
heat-up: 
- heat-up of the primary and secondary circuits to the temperature of hydraulic 
tests;  
- check of the primary circuit for tightness;  
- hydraulic tests of the primary circuit (if necessary) for strength;  
- check of the secondary circuit for tightness;  
- hydraulic tests of the secondary circuit (if necessary) for strength;  
- after completion of tests of circuits I and II for tightness and strength, 
performance of tests for containment tightness;  
- reactor plant heat-up to nominal parameters;  
- in parallel with the heat-up of the primary circuit, the turbine generator is 
prepared for start-up, for which the process systems of the turbine compartment are 
prepared and put into operation in accordance with column 5, Table G.1, Appendix 
G, as well as secondary circuit APCS is also prepared in full.  
5.2.2.2. At the tightness test press ure, perform the final tightness test of the 
reactor plant equipment, systems and pipelines in the places specified by the 
program. 
Check the absence of pressure in the inter -gasket space of the reactor joints, 
PRZ, SG, ECCS HA, RCPS, PHRS heat exchangers.  Check the absence of leaks 
through the internal gaskets of flange joints of CPS drives, ICDA outputs. If cracks, 
breaks, leaks, visible residual deformations are detected, depressurize the primary 
[PAGE 185]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
183 
circuit, cool the primary circuit, if necessary, and perfo rm preparation and repeated 
hydraulic testing after defects are eliminated. 
The temperature on the outer surface of the upper unit thermal protection shall 
not exceed 60 ºС above zero. 
5.2.2.3. The operating personnel shall act in accordance with the requirements 
of the “Operation instruction for the reactor plant of Rooppur NPP Unit No. 1 ” when 
performing hydraulic tests of the secondary circuit in terms of determining safe 
operation methods. 
5.2.2.4. Rules and basic methods of RP safe operation during cooldown. 
Before the pressure rise in the primary and secondary circuits more than 1.47 
MPa, it i s necessary to bring the boundary valves to a state that provides reliable 
separation of sections of high and low pressure pipelines excluding pipelines of the 
cooldown system (JNA). 
Before the pressure rise in the primary circuit above 1.96 MPa, it is nec essary 
to bring the boundary valves of the emergency planned cooldown system (JNA) to 
the state, which provides reliable disconnection of the low pressure pipeline sections 
of the system from the primary circuit. 
Perform the following during RP heat-up: 
- check the indications of level sensors in PRZ, SG, if necessary, blow down 
pulse lines in accordance with the work program; 
- check the indications of the primary circuit pressure and temperature sensors, 
boric acid concentration monitoring channels in the coolant;  
- operability check and calibration of ICIS primary circuit thermal monitoring 
sensors according to a special program, if necessary, introduce corrections for sensor 
indications.  
The following conditions shall be observed when the RCPS is switched on: 
- simultaneous actuation of two adjacent RCPS is prohibited, start -up of 
opposite loops is allowed; 
- it is prohibited to start and operate RCPS without nitrogen or steam blanket in 
the PRZ;  
- it is prohibited to start and operate RCPS at pressure  in the primary circuit 
less than 1.47 MPa. The allowable pressure value is specified in Appendix E of this 
specification (Figure E.1); 
- operation of more than three RCPS at the primary coolant temperature less 
than 200 ºС above zero is prohibited. 
RCPS v ibration amplitude shall not exceed permissible values during RCPS 
operation. 
Air removal from the independent circuit of each RCPS and water circulation 
over this circuit shall be provided during the entire heat -up process. Gas blowing 
from the RCPS indep endent circuit is performed continuously if there are a nitrogen 
blanket in the PRZ and operating RCPS. 
Fulfill the following requirements during heat-up: 
[PAGE 186]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
184 
- surge of boiling margin by primary circuit coolant temperature at the reactor 
core outlet is not less than 15 ºС above zero;  
- temperature difference between makeup water and primary circuit coolant 
purification system water is not more than 120 ºС above zero;  
- primary circuit heat-up rate shall not exceed 20 °С/h; 
- reactor cavity concrete heat-up rate is less than 10 °С/h.  
Primary circuit coolant heat -up for hydraulic tests shall be performed to a 
temperature not exceeding 135 °С above zero. Heat the metal of the equipment and 
pipelines. During primary circuit heat -up, monitor the expansion process  of 
equipment and pipelines, the position of hydraulic shock absorbers. 
The holding time at a pressure of 17.64 MPa is determined by the time required 
for inspection, but not more than four hours. 
Before the start of pressure rise in the primary circuit mo re than 19.6 MPa, 
switch off the TTC sensors, which cannot operate at a pressure more than 19.6 MPa. 
Before the start of pressure rise in the secondary circuit more than 8.63 MPa, 
switch off the TTC sensors, which cannot operate at a pressure more than 8.63 MPa. 
Holding at the primary circuit hydraulic test pressure for strength shall be not 
less than 10, but not more than 60 minutes. 
The holding time at 19.6 MPa is determined by the time required for the 
inspection. 
When performing hydraulic tests of the s econdary circuit, the primary circuit 
pressure shall be higher than the secondary circuit pressure according to nuclear 
safety conditions in order to avoid water leakage from SG secondary circuit to the 
primary circuit. 
Holding at the pressure of hydraulic  tests of the secondary circuit for strength 
shall be at least 10 minutes. For the time of hydraulic tests of the primary circuit it is 
allowed to fully fill the PRZ. 
At the initial stage of RCC heat -up mode (until the end of the nitrogen blanket 
replacement in the PRZ with steam one), the level in the PRZ is 10.900 ± 150 mm, 
after creating a steam blanket in the PRZ, maintain the level - 5100 ± 150 mm. 
The PRZ heat-up rate shall not exceed 20 °С/h before replacement of nitrogen 
blanket in the PRZ. After replacement of nitrogen blanket in the PRZ with steam by 
gas blow-off from the PRZ and level decrease in PRZ, it is allowed to heat water in 
the PRZ at the rate of not more than 30 °С/h due to operation of electric heaters. 
Water level decrease in SG from 3700 - 3800 mm at the beginning of heat -up 
up to the nominal value is allowed after water temperature increase in SG to 170 -180 
°С above zero (in case of  boiling in SG). SG makeup, when they are in hot standby, 
shall be continuous. 
At the temperature of the metal of the primary circuit equipment above the 
minimum hydraulic test temperature specified in Appendix C, check the operability 
and putting to stand by of ejector pumps of the JNA primary circuit emergency 
planned cooldown system and the JND emergency boron injection system pumps. 
[PAGE 187]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001

If the pressure in the primary circuit is more than 3.0 MPa, connect the 
hydraulic accumulators of the JNG10 system (PCFS) to the primary circuit: 
- monitor automatic closing of double check valves at primary circuit pressure 
increase up to 3.3 MPa;  
- when the primary circuit pressure reaches at least 3.5 MPa after closing the 
double check valves, open the shut -off gate valve s of all hydroaccumulators 
remotely.  
If the pressure in the primary circuit increases more than 6.37 MPa, connect the 
ECCS HA of the JNG50 -80 system to the primary circuit, open the Dn300 shut -off 
gate valves of the ECCS accumulators 
Simultaneous opening of more than two bellows valves on the bypass of check 
valves of one channel of the JNG50-80 system at the primary circuit pressure of more 
than 6.37 MPa is prohibited. 
It is prohibited to simultaneously check two or more fast shut-off gate valves of 
the JNG50-80 system. 
The operating personnel shall do the following during heat -up of the primary 
circuit: 
- monitor the acceleration period and neutron flux level by NFME;  
- monitor the concentration of boric acid in the primary circuit coolant;  
- monitor th e implementation of measures to prevent water ingress into the 
primary circuit with boric acid concentration below the circuit one;  
- monitor the water chemistry of the primary and secondary circuits, their 
auxiliary systems and perform its correction in accordance with the requirements of 
the water chemistry standards;  
- monitor the process parameters of the primary and secondary circuits, their 
auxiliary systems and maintain them within the permissible limits;  
- check the tightness of flange joints of the primary circuit equipment 
(according to the indications of the tightness monitoring system);  
- provide readiness for operation of all systems in accordance with process 
necessity of their use and operation instructions;  
- monitor the implementation of OCs for the current RP state.  
The following shall be checked after repair or downtime of the Unit for more 
than 10 days: 
- serviceability of thermal insulation;  
- state of thermal displacement indicators;  
- serviceability and absence of foreign objects in RCPS, SG supports;  
- freedom of temperature movements of equipment and pipelines;  
- indications of temperature displacement measurement sensors and their 
correspondence to the actual temperature of the primary circuit;  
- state of valves on sampling lines;  
- state of drains and air vent valves;  
- state of thermal monitoring devices.  
The deficiencies identified during inspection shall be eliminated.

It is allowed to block PRZ POSV operation during hydraulic tests and primary 
circuit tightness test. 
During hydraulic testing of equipment and pipelines, measures shall be taken to 
prevent accumulation of gas bubbles in cavities filled with liquid. 
Disconnect the RCPS for the duration of hydraulic tests or tightness tests of the 
primary circuit, as well as for the duration of connection to the primary circuit, if 
necessary, the reactor coolant circuit emergency and planned cooldown and fuel pool 
cooling system. 
It is allowed to block the operation of SG POSV (11LBA10,20,30,40AA901,

Ammonia and potassium hydroxide solutions shall be injected into the primary 
coolant after the start of forced circulation. After heat -up of the primary circuit 
coolant to a te mperature of 80-90 °C above zero, start injecting hydrazine hydrate to 
the primary circuit in an amount providing two to three times its excess in relation to 
the oxygen concentration in the coolant in order to reduce the oxygen concentration. 
The primary circuit coolant temperature increase more than 120 °С above zero is 
allowed after the mass concentration of dissolved oxygen in the coolant decreases to 
0.02 mg/dm3 and below.

5.3 Unit operation in the “hot” state  
5.3.1 Operational conditions for “hot” state  
Requirements for Unit operation organization are defined in Section 9. 
Before U nit changeover to “hot” state, the operational conditions given in 
Table 3.8 for this state shall be met. 
Before Unit changeover to “hot” state, the requirements for the state of 
operability of systems and equipment given in column 6, Table G.1, Appendix G  of 
this specification shall be met. 
The “hot” state is characterized by the following RP conditions and 
parameters: 
- the reactor is sub-critical, all CPS CR are on BLS or LAS;  
- concentration of boric acid solution in the primary circuit coolant provides 
reactor sub-criticality of at least 1% (excluding CPS CR submerged into the core);  
- primary circuit coolant temperature at the reactor inlet is 275-285 ºС above 
zero; 
- pressure in the primary circuit (16.1±0.3) MPa;  
- PRZ is in steam mode;

- level in SG (Hnom ± 50) mm.  
The PRZ level maintenance controller is started in the automatic mode. The 
primary circuit pressure controller is started in the automatic mod e. PRZ electric 
heaters are in operation. Interlocks for JEF12,13AA002, JEF11AA201,
