5.3.2  Rules and basic methods of safe operation in “hot” state 
5.3.2.1 The operating personnel shall do the following in the “hot” state: 
1) monitor the acceleration period and neutron flux level by NFME; 
2) monitor the concentration of boric acid in the primary circuit and maintain 
its value in the range of 16÷20 g/dm 3 in case of shutdown with subsequent 
changeover to the “s hutdown for repair” or “refueling” states. For cases of 
unscheduled shutdown, maintain the concentration of boric acid not lower than the 
value that provides the reactor sub -criticality of at least 1% (excluding CPS CR 
submerged into the core); 
3) monitor on a shift basis the implementation of measures to prevent water 
from entering the primary circuit with boric acid concentration below the circuit one 
with registration of test results in the operational logbooks; 
4) maintain the temperature of the primary circu it coolant at the reactor inlet 
within the range of 275÷285 ºС above zero by secondary circuit steam discharge 
through BRU -SN (10LBF10,20AA201) to other loads or through BRU -K 
(10MAN11,12,21,22,31,32,41,42AA201) to the turbine condenser, it is allowed to 
[PAGE 191]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
189 
discharge steam from the MSH through the drain steam pipeline to the drain tank or 
TG condenser; 
5) monitor the water chemistry of the primary and secondary circuits, their 
auxiliary systems and perform its correction in accordance with the requirements of 
Appendix D of this specification; 
6) ensure the readiness for operation of all systems in accordance with the 
operation conditions of their use; 
7) monitor the pressure in the inter -gasket cavities of the hatches of the 
primary and secondary circuits each shift wit h a record in the logbook of the reactor 
shop shift personnel (time, monitoring point, pressure value, no pressure); 
8) All SGs shall be simultaneously blow down from the Dn 32 sleeves of 
“pockets” of headers and Dn 50 nozzles on the lower generatrix of the housing. 
9) Blowdown flow rate from one Dn 32 sleeve shall be up to 10 t/h and from 
one Dn 50 nozzle up to 20 t/h. Transition to the next Dn50 sleeve and Dn32 nozzle 
on each of the SG shall be performed cyclically one after another. Constant water 
outlet with a flow rate of up to 5 t/h shall be arranged from the “salt” compartment to 
allow sampling. Duration of actuations is determined by the blowdown system 
operation schedule. 
5.4 Unit operation in the “MCPL” state 
5.4.1 Operational conditions in the “MCPL” state 
5.4.1.1 Requirements for Unit operation organization are defined in  
Section 9. 
5.4.1.2 Before Unit changeover to the “reaching MCPL” state, the 
operational conditions given in Table 3.8 for this state shall be met. 
5.4.1.3 Before Unit changeover to the “reaching MCPL” state, the 
requirements for the state of operability of systems and equipment, given in column 
7, Table G.1, Appendix G of this specification shall be met. 
5.4.1.4 The RP “reaching MCPL” state is characterized by the following 
conditions and parameters: 
 Keff ≤ 1; 
 reactor neutron power is not more than 1% Nnom;  
 CPS CR groups (No. 1÷8) shall be located on ULS;  
 in steady mode, control groups (9÷11) shall be on ULS, the position of 
operating group 12 is defined in Appendix F (Figure F.3);  
 current concentration of boric acid in the primary circuit corresponding to 
the critical state of the reactor core;  
 primary circuit coolant temperature at the reactor inlet is not more than 
275 ºС above zero;  
 primary circuit pressure is (16.1 ± 0.3) MPa;  
 level in PRZ is (5100±50) mm;  
 at least two RCPS are in operation.  
[PAGE 192]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
190 
 steam pressure at SG outlet is (5.8 - 6.7) ± 0.1 MPa;  
 level in SG (Hnom ± 50) mm. 
5.4.1.5 The operation of PRZ and SG level meters was checked by 
comparing the indications of different level meters. 
5.4.1.6 The following parameters shall be measured at the beginning of each 
cycle in accordance with the measurement pr ogram: the effectiveness of emergency 
protection (given the jamming of one of the most effective CPS CR in the upper limit 
position) and the operating group, as well as reactivity coefficients for boric acid 
concentration, temperature reactivity coefficient and barometric reactivity coefficient. 
The results of these measurements shall confirm the data of previous physical 
calculations. 
5.4.1.7 Bringing the reactor to a critical state and further power operation 
with a positive reactivity coefficient for the temperature of the primary circuit coolant 
or with a negative one for the tightness of the primary circuit coolant are not allowed. 
Compliance with the requirements for reactivity coefficients is checked by 
preliminary physical calculations. In this case, the rea ctor shall be changed over to a 
sub-critical state. 
5.4.1.8 The core reactivity inventory is determined by the critical 
concentration of boric acid in the primary circuit coolant. If the measured 
concentration of boric acid differs from the design concentration by  more than 
0,6 g/ dm3, measures shall be taken to clarify such a deviation and determine the 
appropriate actions to correct the situation. 
5.4.1.9 Controlled leaks of the primary circuit are not more than 2.5 t/h. 
5.4.1.10 CPS AR movement speed in control mode is (20.0 ± 1 .5) mm/s 
during reactor core operation. The position of each CR of the operating group in 
relation to any other CR of this group shall not differ by more than 60 mm. 
5.4.1.11 Reaching MCPL is not allowed without actuation of optical -acoustic 
acceleration indicators (OAI). Reaching MCPL is performed at operation of NFME 
range selection circuit in automatic mode. 
5.4.1.12 The reactor is brought to a critical state when monitoring the reactor 
power and period through all NFME channels in the mode of automatic selection of 
monitoring sub -ranges In this case, both optical -acoustic acceleration indicators 
(OAI) at the MCR shall be in operation. 
5.4.1.13 After PPM or in case of RP disassembly, it is allowed to reach 
MCPL upon confirmation of non -exceedance of CPS CR drop time for more than 4  
seconds. 
5.4.2 General procedure of safety related operations for reactor plant 
changeover to the “reaching MCPL” state 
5.4.2.1 The following work stages are performed when the RP is changed 
over to the minimum controlled power level: 
 groups No. 1 -11 taking -up. CPS CR in group mode are sequentially 
extracted from the core in the order of their numbers;  
[PAGE 193]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
191 
 bringing the reactor to a critical state by reducing the concentration of boric 
acid in the primary circuit coolant using the volume and chemical control system;  
 measurement of neutron -physical characteristics of the core (during start -
up after PPM).  
Bringing the reactor to a critical state, reaching power level after refueling, 
after overhaul or medium repair, as well as after downtime for more than three days 
shall be  performed only after assessing the degree of sub -criticality and reactivity 
inventory according to the NFF album data. 
5.4.2.2 The CPS CR taking-up is performed in the following order: 
 groups with No. 1 -11 in group mode are sequentially extracted from the 
core in the order of their numbers at intervals of 36 cm (output of control action to 
CPS CR drives for no more than 19 seconds) with time delay between intervals of at 
least 60 seconds at stable NFME indications;  
 group No. 12 is raised in the same order to a he ight of 70-90% of the lower 
position (a specific value is indicated in the Unit start-up program).  
5.4.2.3 In order to reduce the concentration of boric acid in the primary 
coolant, the water exchange shall be stopped in the process of water exchange upon 
reaching the start -up interval for a time sufficient to equalize the concentration of 
boric acid in the primary circuit, PRZ, and the blowdown deaerator (the concentration 
difference is not more than 1 g/dm3). 
5.4.2.4 During water exchange up to the start -up interval and  when the boric 
acid concentration is equalized, samples shall be taken to monitor the boric acid 
concentration at least once every 30 minutes in addition to continuous automatic 
monitoring. 
5.4.2.5 Permissible value of distillate flow rate is determined based on the 
properties of current fuel load. The rate of injection of pure condensate in the start -up 
range shall provide the r ate of positive reactivity injection not more than 
0.02βeff/min. 
The flow rate of pure condensate in the start -up interval shall not exceed  
10 t/h. 
5.4.2.6 If when moving CPS CR or removing boric acid by NFME 
indications, a change in neutron power or a decrease i n the reactor period of less than 
60 s is observed, stop operations until the indications of neutron flux devices are 
stabilized and the period is increased to 999 s. Stabilize the reactor power at 1% 
Nnom by affecting the CPS CR of the operating group. 
Record the parameters at which the MCPL power was reached after the 
reactor is brought to MCPL, after the boric acid removal from the primary circuit is 
stopped and the concentration of boric acid in the reactor, PRZ and blowdown 
deaerator is equalized: 
 boric acid concentration in the primary circuit coolant;  
 CPS CR position;  
 primary circuit pressure and temperature;  
 channel-by-channel neutron power indications;  
[PAGE 194]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
192 
 number of effective days spent by the reactor after refueling until start-up.  
5.4.2.7 The engagement of CPS drive rods with the CPS AR shall be checked 
after the reactor is brought to MCPL. 
The check shall be performed by moving the CPS CR down from the upper 
position to the determined distance (within 35 -70 cm). The availability of 
engagement is determin ed by the change in reactivity or neutron flux, as well as by 
the change in temperature at the FA outlet. 
5.4.3 Rules and basic methods of safe operation in the “reaching MCPL” 
state 
5.4.3.1 Continue blowdown at all SGs simultaneously in accordance with 
the mode specified in Item 5.3.2.2 to ensure cleanliness of the lower generatrix of the 
housing and “pockets” of the headers. 
5.4.3.2 The required amount of corrective chemical additives and effective 
feedwater deaeration shall be provided. UDP is put into operation. 
5.4.3.3 SG makeup shall be continuous. 
5.4.3.4 When operating steam pipelines, monitor: 
- constant drainage of moisture from places where it can accumulate (bags, 
areas upstream measuring and throttling devices);  
- correct the settings and operation of the controller (opening and cl osing) 
upon actuation of BRU -K (10MAN11,12,21,22,31,32,41,42AA201) and BRU -A 
(11LBA10AA201, 11LBA20AA201, 12LBA30AA201, 12LBA40AA201);  
- reliable remote control of BRU-K (10MAN11,12,21,22,31,32,41,42AA201), 
BRU-A (11LBA10AA201, 11LBA20AA201, 12LBA30AA201,  12LBA40AA201), 
while paying special attention to valves fitting.  
5.4.3.5 When operating feedwater pipelines, monitor: 
- accuracy of maintaining the specified parameters and constant operation in 
automatic mode of SG level controllers;  
- reliability of indicatio ns of measuring channels of pressure and feedwater 
flow rate by ULCS video frames.  
5.4.3.6 Stop CPS CR extraction immediately if the reactor period decreases 
to 60 s during CPS CR extraction. CPS CR groups extraction shall be continued after 
period increase to 999s. In the event of an increase in neutron power indications with 
the constant position of the CPS CR groups for at least one NFME channel, stop 
further lifting immediately, lower the taken up CPS CR group to BLS to clarify the 
circumstances that led to a spontaneous increase in neutron flux. Further works on 
CPS CR lifting shall be continued after analysis and elimination of the causes that led 
to the above situation. 
Reaching MCPL is prohibited in case of disturbance of logical sequence of 
CPS CR group movement transfer. 
In case of loss of indication of CPS CR position, stop lifting the group, find 
out the cause of the loss, eliminate the faults and continue lifting the group. 
During lifting of CPS CR groups, provide continuous monitoring of: 
[PAGE 195]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
193 
- synchronous movement of individual CRs in the group;  
- actuation of intermediate limit switches and automatic transfer of movement 
from the previous CR group to the next one when the previous group reaches the 
ULS;  
- actuation of ULS and synchronicity of shutdown o f all CR of the group by 
102.4% of the core height.  
5.4.3.7 The period of increasing the reactor neutron power shall be at least 
60 seconds when reaching the critical state. 
5.4.3.8 The following is prohibited when bringing the reactor to MCPL 
within the start-up range: 
- performance of operations that lead to change of primary circuit coolant 
temperature and its tightness;  
- perform any repair works on reactor CPS and NFME equipment and 
circuits. The water exchange shall be stopped if it is necessary to perform these 
works;  
- simultaneous performance in any combination of operations for CPS CR 
extraction from the reactor core, change of boric acid concentration in the primary 
circuit water and change of the primary circuit water temperature at the reactor inlet 
less than 275 °С above zero;  
- RCPS switching on or off;  
- remove boric acid from the primary circuit in the start -up interval at a flow 
rate of more than the regulated value (not more than 10 t/h). Follow the requirements 
of Item 5.4.2.5 when starting from a poisoned state;  
- perform steam extraction from SG, which causes rapid pressure decrease in 
SG from steady-state value;  
- switch on KBE filters in the start-up interval; 
- perform any other operations that may lead to a spontaneous change in the 
reactor core reactivity.  
5.4.3.9 Do not inject distillate into the primary circuit in the following cases: 
- EP controls not taken up;  
- non-operating RCPS and natural circulation of the primary circuit coolant.  
5.4.3.10 Stabilize the temperature of the primary circuit by steam e xtraction 
through BRU -SN (10LBF10,20AA20) or BRU -K 
(10MAN11,12,21,22,31,32,41,42AA201) and through the steam pipeline drains to 
the turbine drain tank. 
5.4.3.11 Pressure in SG is maintained by BRU -K 
(10MAN11,12,21,22,31,32,41,42AA201), BRU-SN (10LBF10,20AA201), SG levels 
are maintained by the LAB30-60AA201 start-up control valves. 
5.4.3.12 The operating personnel shall do the following when operating the 
reactor plant at MCPL: 
- monitor the change period and neutron flux level in the reactor by NFME 
indications;  
[PAGE 196]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
194 
- when the CPS CR of the operating group reaches the upper or bottom limit 
of the specified control interval, change the content of boric acid in the primary 
circuit water, so that it is possible to return the CPS CR of this group to the control 
area;  
- prevent uncontrolled ingress of media with low concentration of boric acid 
into the coolant;  
- maintain the temperature of the primary circuit coolant at the reactor inlet 
more than 275÷285°C above zero by steam discharge from the secondary circuit;  
- monitor the wa ter chemistry of the primary and secondary circuits, their 
auxiliary systems and perform their correction in accordance with the requirements of 
Appendix D. 
5.4.3.13 When the reactor plant is changed over from MCPL to the “hot” state 
with subsequent RP cooldown, the operating personnel shall: 
- before changeover operations start, provide free volume in KBB system 
tanks not less than 500 m3; 
- change over the reactor to a sub -critical state by injecting boric acid into the 
primary circuit coolant from the KBA system.  Boric acid concentration change shall 
be periodically checked with an interval of 30 minutes;  
when injecting boric acid, perform purification of the primary circuit coolant 
by making makeup and blowdown of the primary circuit with a maximum flow rate 
(60 m3/h) during operation of KBE system. The blowdown deaerator shall operate in 
deaeration mode.  The dissolved hydrogen concentration is maintained at a minimum 
of 1.3 mg/dm3 prior to the start of the cooldown process; 
- stop water exchange when the steady-state concentration of boric acid in the 
primary circuit coolant is reached, which provides the reactor sub -criticality of at 
least 1% (excluding submerged CPS CR); 
- lower all CPS CR to BLS;  
- take measures to prevent ingress of media with boric acid co ncentration 
below the standby one into the primary circuit.  
Note – During cooldown, the concentration of dissolved hydrogen is decreased to the value 
of less than 0.5 mg/dm3.. 
5.5 Unit operation in the “power operation” state 
5.5.1 Operational conditions for power operation 
5.5.1.1 Requirements for Unit operation organization are defined in  
Section 9. 
5.5.1.2 Before Unit changeover to the “power operation” state, the 
operational conditions given in Table 3.8. 
5.5.1.3 Before Unit changeover to the “power operation” state, the 
requirements for the state of operability of systems and equipment given in column 8 
of Table G.1 of Appendix G of this Procedure shall be met. 
5.5.1.4 Operation limits are specified for the RP operation conditions in the 
steady-state mode when the Unit operates in the basic load-bearing mode. 
[PAGE 197]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
195 
5.5.1.5 The RP “power operation” state is characterized by the following 
conditions and parameters: 
- the reactor is critical, Keff = 1 (in steady state); 
- reactor power in the range from 1 to 100% Nnom; 
- position of CPS CR operating group in a ccordance with Figure F.2 of 
Appendix F;  
- current boric acid concentration in the primary circuit depending on reactor 
power and operating group position 
- primary circuit coolant temperature;  
-  in “cold” legs up to 285 °С above zero; 
- temperature of the primary circuit coolant in the primary circuit in “hot” legs 
not more than 332°С; 
-  pressure above the core (16.1 ± 0.3) MPa;  
- level in PRZ (Hnom ± 150) mm;  
- pressure in SG (at SG steam header outlet) (6.9 ± 0.1) MPa;  
- level in SG (Hnom ± 50) mm.  
5.5.1.6 Power operation is the main RP state in which long-term operation of 
the RP is allowed: 
- at nominal power level (or less than nominal) with four switched on RCPS;  
- with incomplete number of primary circuit loops (with incomplete number 
of switched on RCPS) at reduced power levels.  
5.5.1.7 RP process parameters shall be determined with the accuracy given 
in Tables 5.1, 5.2.

5.5.1.9 RP normal operation is provided if RCPS head value changes within 
(0.624±0.025) MPa (with 4 operating RCPS). 
5.5.1.10 When distillate or boric acid solutions, potassium hydroxide or 
ammonia are injected into the primary circuit, hydrazine hydrate solution is dosed to 
the makeup water in an amount that provides two to three times its excess in relation 
to the oxygen concentration in these solutions. 
5.5.1.11 Continuous and periodic blowdown of LCQ10 -40 steam generators 
is performed to maintain the secondary circuit WC. In this case, prevent effect of 
blowdown of individual SGs on each other, as well as clogging of blowdown lines 
with sludge. 
Blowdown of each SG is performed from the “salt” compartment of the cold 
end through the Dn50 nozzle and from the combined blowdown line (from four Dn50 
nozzles of the housing and four Dn32 sleeves of SG primary circuit coolant headers). 
The maximum  flow rate of blowdown water through Dn50 blowdown line 
from the “salt” compartment of each SG (for one, two or three SG) is 40 t/h.  
Continuous blowdown of each SG from the “salt” compartment is up to 15 t/h 
and from the combined blowdown line of each SG to maintain the pipelines of the 
combined blowdown line in the “hot” state - up to 5 t/h. 
Periodic blowdown of each SG is performed from the combined blowdown 
line.  
[PAGE 201]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
199 
The maximum flow rate from each Dn50 nozzle of SG housing is 20 t/h, and 
total flow rate of blowdown water from four Dn32 nozzles of primary circuit coolant 
headers is 20 t/h. 
Periodic blowdown allows blowdown water to be outlet either from all four 
Dn50 nozzles and four Dn32 nozzles simultaneously, or from each Dn50 nozzle 
separately, or from four or two Dn32 sleeves simultaneously, or in any of the above 
combinations. Main parameters of steam generators blowdown are given in  
Table 5.5. 
Periodic blowdown is performed both by one SG and four SG simultaneously. 
The total flow rate of blowdown wa ter from each SG is up to 35 t/h with 
simultaneous blowdown of all SGs. Blowdown from the “salt” compartment of each 
SG increases to 35 t/h in transient, start-up operation modes and in case of blowdown 
water quality deviations from the standards.  
The max imum total blowdown rate of all SGs with the actuated periodic 
blowdown of one SG is up to 140 t/h inclusive. 
Blowdown flow rates are determined by flow rate meters with measurement 
accuracy of not more than ± 0.5 t/h. 
In case of deviation of nominal indic ators of blowdown water quality from 
the SG “salt” compartments from permissible values within the limits of the first and 
second levels, the flow rate of blowdown water from these compartments shall be 
increased to the maximum possible. In this case, it i s allowed to temporarily stop 
periodic blowdown until the quality of blowdown water is restored to the nominal 
values. 
In transient and start -up modes of RP operation, the blowdown water flow 
rate shall be maintained at the maximum possible level in order to achieve the 
nominal parameters of the working medium quality.

5.5.1.12 The working medium shall be treated with reagents before RP 
shutdown for a period of more than three days in order to preserve the secondary 
circuit equipment. The working medium for preservation of the secondary circuit 
equipment may not be treated in case of short -term RP shutdowns for up to three 
days. 
Treatment of the working medium of the condensate and feedwater path with 
reagents before shut down is performed in accordance in accordance with WC 
standards for secondary circuit 10JAA-MEC0029 523 D3. 
5.5.1.13 When the CPS CR operating group goes beyond the permissible 
limits, the personnel shall return the CPS CR operating group to the permissible 
range using the volume and chemical control system (changing the concentration of 
boric acid in the primary circuit coolant) (Appendix F, Figure F.3). 
When the reactor power decreases, it is allowed to submerge the control 
groups without limiting their limit position, after which, within 12 hours, groups 9, 10 
and 11 shall be extracted to ULS and group 12 changed over to the permissible 
position interval. 
CPS CR of the APP group shall be extracted to ULS within not more than 3 
hours after the drop. 
5.5.1.14 The position of  each CR of the operating group in relation to any 
other CR of this group shall not differ by more than 60 mm. CPS AR movement 
speed in control mode is (20.0 ± 1.5) mm/s during reactor core operation. 
5.5.1.15 FGC shutdown is allowed during Unit power operation if this does 
not require power reduction. FGC shall be switched on for operation in information 
mode during power operation of the Unit, as well as during its shutdown. 
5.5.2 General procedure for performance of safety related operations 
5.5.2.1 Reactor power rise above MC PL and power decrease to MCPL are 
performed in accordance with the requirements and established procedure for 
performing operations on the Unit equipment and systems given in the “Operation 
instruction for reactor plant”, in accordance with Appendix F. 
5.5.2.2 The following work stages shall be performed when the reactor 
power rises above the minimum controlled power level: 
- rise of reactor thermal power up to 25 - 40% of nominal;  
- turbine start-up and power gain according to TG OI;  
- rise of reactor thermal power up to nominal.  
5.5.2.3 The reactor power increase is performed by changing the position of 
the CPS CR operating (regulating) group with its correction, if necessary, by 
changing the boric acid content in the primary circuit coolant. 
5.5.2.4 Set NFME setpoints in acco rdance with new set level (Nset + 7% 
Nnom) before the reactor power increase. Check the changeover of both NFME sets 
to the operating linear range (OR2) during the reactor power increase above 1% 
Nnom.

5.5.2.5 SG makeup shall be continuous. Feedwater supply to SG during Unit 
start-up (up to level 3 - 4% Nnom.) is performed from AFWP through start-up control 
valves. 
5.5.2.6 FWP are started at a power level of about 3 -4% Nnom and standard 
control valves are put into operation after the start -up and control valve is fully 
opened. As the RP power increases and the feedwater flow rate to the SG increases, 
monitor the operation of the main LAB30 -60AA001 makeup controllers in the 
automatic mode, check the partial closing to 50% and the actuation of the watchdog 
mode of the start-up LAB30-60AA201 makeup controllers. 
During RP power operation the nominal steam pressure at the SG steam 
header outlet shall be automatically maintained equal to (6.9 ± 0.1) MPa. Maximum 
steam capacity of SG is 1714 t/h. Humidity of generated steam at the steam generator 
outlet at water level in SG is (2700 ± 50) mm (specified during separation tests) shall 
not exceed 0.2% (wt). 
Steam humidity is determined at 100% Nnom power in the following cases: 
- when testing the Unit before its putting into operation in order to confirm 
the design thermal characteristics;  
- periodically, if necessary, during operation, according to a special program 
using the KUP-KVPP-1200 system (JEA50). Rated steam humidity at SG outlet shall 
be provided by SG level maintenance. Wat er level fluctuations in SG in steady mode 
shall not exceed ± 50 mm. At the power level from 0 to 95% of the nominal value, 
the required steam humidity is provided in the range of level change up to + 150 mm 
of nominal value. At power from 95 to 100% Nnom,  the required steam humidity is 
provided at the nominal water level with a tolerance of ± 50 mm; 
- when the design thermal technical characteristics of SG change;  
- in case of indirect signs of damage of SG internals that affect steam 
humidity;  
- after possible reconstructions of SG internals that affect steam humidity.  
5.5.2.7 Before starting the turbine, the thermal power of the reactor can be 
increased to 40% Nnom. Maintain steam pressure in the MSH with the degree of 
BRU-K (10MAN11,12,21,22,31,32,41,42AA201) opening to the turbine condenser 
in automatic mode. 
5.5.2.8 Perform turbine rotor start -up from rest at the reactor power level of 
30-35% of nominal one (up to 40% is allowed with steam discharge through BRU -K 
(10MAN11,12,21,22,31,32,41,42AA201).  
5.5.2.9 Check the following during turbine start-up from rest: 
- absence of touching in the flow part; 
- constant pressure maintenance in the MSH; 
- maintenance of nominal levels in SG; 
- turbine unit parameters.

5.5.2.10 It is not allowed to start and operate the turbine at power with faulty 
check valves on regenerative extraction pipelines. The state of check valves of 
extractions shall be carefully monitored when operating the turbine unit. 
5.5.2.11 It is allowed to operate the turbine at idle run for 24 hours when the 
turbine is started from the cold state for electric tests of the generator after installation 
or overhaul. The idle run time after load shedding shall not exceed 15 minutes. The 
duration of operation on the auxiliaries load after shedding the electric load shall not 
exceed 45 minutes. 
5.5.2.12 The turbine generator can be connected to the mains if: 
- SG is powered by FWP;  
- TG ECS is in operation;  
- steam pressure in the MSH is equal to the nominal value;  
- total flow rate of main steam through BRU -K 
(10MAN11,12,21,22,31,32,41,42AA201) to turbine condensers provides taking of 
installation load.  
5.5.2.13 Synchronize and connect the generator to the mains at the reactor 
power level of 30-40% of nominal one. Load TG up to 100-300 MW. 
It is allowed to operate the turbine with auxiliaries load at a p ressure in the 
condenser of not more than 6.8 kPa (0.07 kgf/cm 2) for one hour, after which the 
turbine shall be stopped or loaded. 
5.5.2.14 Reaching power up to 50% of nominal one and power operation for 
no more than 3 days are allowed in case of loss of operability of the main and standby 
ICIS computing system, but with a fully operable LL CAS. Reactor parameters are 
monitored using LL CAS, ULCS, NFME, etc. 
5.5.2.15 The ICDA coordinates in the core are checked for compliance with 
the coordinates in the ICIS equipment after refueling at a power level of more than 
30% Nnom, before the Unit is connected to the mains. 
5.5.2.16 At power level of 75 - 80% Nnom, perform calibration of NFME 
channels in OR2 in case of mismatch of channel indications and weighted average 
thermal power by ICIS indications of more than 1% Nnom. 
5.5.2.17 Raise the RP power to the allowable level. Stabilize parameters of 
primary and secondary circuits. Take the following printouts after the reactor has 
operated for at least one hour at a stable power level: 
- maps of power density distribution by core height;  
- maps of temperatures at FA outlet;  
- power density irregularity coefficients by core volume. 
5.5.2.18 Adjustment of EP and PP setpoints for the primary circuit coolant 
temperature in the “hot” legs of loops shall be performe d when RP reaches 100% 
Nnom after reactor refueling and every 60 eff. days. Correction can be performed 
only after RP operation at constant power level and at stable position of operating 
(regulating) group of CPS CR for at least 72 hours. In this case, th e RP thermal 
power shall be determined (by heat balance).

5.5.2.19 Reactor and turbine generator power shall be maintained in 
accordance with the dispatch schedule at the permissible level for the reactor. 
The Unit power is maintained and changed using an APC -R tha t operates 
together with the turbine ECS. Automatic coordination of APC -R and TG ECS 
operation modes shall be provided. 
It is allowed to maintain and change power using remote control in 
accordance with the requirements of this specification and operation instructions for 
systems and equipment. It is allowed to raise the reactor power using remote control 
during the operation of the main automatic controllers of the Unit. 
5.5.2.20 Reactor power change, core power density control, including 
prevention and compensatio n of subsequent xenon processes, shall be performed in 
accordance with Item F.5.2 of Appendix F. 
5.5.2.21 Reactor power reduction to MCPL is performed in accordance with 
Item F.5.2 of Appendix F by maintaining constant pressure in MSH (6.7 - 6.9) ± 0.1 
MPa. 
5.5.2.22 When RP power changes, monitor: 
- rate of reactor power change;  
- synchronism of movement and absence of clamping of CPS CR of operating 
(control) group; 
- correspondence of operating (control) group position with reactor power;  
- normal operation of RP main co ntrollers and main parameters of primary 
and secondary circuits.  
5.5.2.23 After the RP power change is completed, stabilize the power at the 
achieved level. Record the parameters: indications of NFME devices, position of all 
CPS CR, boric acid concentration in the  primary circuit coolant, primary circuit 
coolant temperature and primary circuit pressure. 
5.5.3 Rules and basic methods of safe operation during power operation 
5.5.3.1 It is prohibited to exceed the makeup flow rate above the blowdown 
flow rate of more than 14 m3/h to ensure the required temperature difference between 
the water of the cold leg of the primary circuit loop and makeup water of less than 30 
°С above zero. 
5.5.3.2 During operation, APC -R shall provide the maintenance of the 
specified pressure value in the secondar y circuit (steam header) with the controller 
dead band not more ± 0.05 MPa and maintenance of neutron flux density level with 
the dead band not more ± 1% of the nominal value. 
5.5.3.3 The APP system shall be in operation if the RP power is more than 
75% of Nnom. 
5.5.3.4 Permissible reactor power change rates during normal operation are 
given in Table 5.4. 
5.5.3.5 Simultaneous opening of two sequential valves on the lines of the 
КТР emergency gas removal system is prohibited during the check. 
[PAGE 207]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
205 
5.5.3.6 During power operation, all valves of the drain system of RCPL U -
shaped sections shall be closed and the electric circuits shall be disassembled. 
5.5.3.7 It is prohibited to move the gates of JNG50-80AA001,002 fast-acting 
gate valves by the electric drive when the differential pressure on the gate is more 
than 2.45 MPa. 
Simultaneous opening of valves on two bypass lines of check valves of ECCS 
passive part is prohibited during RP operation at Р1c more than 6.37 MPa. 
5.5.3.8 Switch NFME setpoints in a timely manner with a given change in 
reactor power. EP setpoints by neutron power level in the operating range for each 
NFME channel shall be set as follows: 
1) Set the setpoints according to this expression in case of reactor power 
increase before the start of power increase operations: 
Рs = Рset + d, %Nnom, 
where Ps is the EP actuation setpoint value; 
- Pset - set power value for operation at steady level; 
-d - EP actuation margin equal to 7% Nnom. 
2) Set the setpoints according to this expression in case of reactor power 
decrease after reactor power reduction operations and stabilization at the new power 
level: 
Ps = Rset + d,% Nnom. , 
where - Ps - EP actuation setpoint value; 
- Pset - set power value for operation at steady level; 
-d - EP actuation margin equal to 7% Nnom. 
5.5.3.9 NFME operating range detection units (DU) shall be set so that drift 
of indications during CR control group operation during pow er change and during 
xenon vibration suppression in the core does not lead to channel mismatch within the 
equipment set more than 5%. 
5.5.3.10 In all cases of unplanned shutdown, including after EP actuation, it is 
necessary to start boric acid injection into the p rimary circuit. Stop boric acid 
injection if the concentration of boric acid after stabilization of temperature and 
pressure in the primary circuit turned out to be not lower than the value that provides 
the reactor sub -criticality of at least 1% (excludin g the CPS CR submerged into the 
core). 
5.5.3.11 The tightness of fuel cladding shall be monitored at the operating 
reactor by periodically checking the activity of the primary circuit coolant. The scope 
of CIM during reactor core refueling is determined based on th e results of fuel 
element cladding tightness test. 
FE CIM shall be performed in accordance with the special instruction by 
measuring the total specific activity of 131I-135I iodine radionuclides in the primary 
circuit coolant. Perform check once a week if the iodine total activity is less than 
7.4х106 Bq/kg or 131I  less than 3.7х105 Bq/kg. The measurements shall be performed 
[PAGE 208]

Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001

206 
daily if the iodine total activity exceeds 7.4х106 Bq/kg or 131I activity exceeds 3.7х105 
Bq/kg. 
5.5.3.12 Regular monitoring of primary circui t coolant primary -to-secondary 
circuit leaks through leaks in steam generators shall be performed. In case of SG 
leakage less than 0.5 kg/h, this SG shall be checked at least once a week; at leakage 
values from 0.5 kg/h to 2 kg/h, all SG shall be checked daily. 
5.5.3.13 Once a week, take samples of the primary circuit coolant 
synchronously (within no more than 30 minutes) with a sample of blowdown water 
from the “salt” compartment of each SG. 
5.5.3.14 The JNB51,52, 61,62, 71,72,73,81,82, AA001, 002,003 PHRS air 
gates shall be in closed position, JNB50,60,70,80AA001,002,003,004 shut-off valves 
on PHRS steam -condensate path shall be in open position. Drives of 
JNB51,52,61,62,71,72,73,81,82AA004 cooling air flow rate control devices are 
connected to the secondary circuit. 
5.5.3.15 The pressure relief tank gas volume shall be continuously blow down 
over the design circuit. Hydrogen content in the pressure relief tank gas volume shall 
not exceed the nominal value (3% volumetric). 
5.5.3.16 Auxiliaries steam pipelines from the ABH and from the BRU -SN 
(10LBF10,20AA201) to the auxiliaries steam header shall be constantly heated up 
during power operation of the Unit. 
5.5.3.17 Long-term operation of the Unit is allowed with the HPH switched 
off.  
5.5.3.18 SG operation is allowed at a constant feedwater temperature in 
accordance with Table 5.6 when the load changes in the range of 20-100% Nnom.

5.5.3.19 The following requirements shall be met at planned shutdown 
(connection) of HPH: 
- APC-R shall be switched to operation in the mode of maintaining constant 
neutron power before HPH shutdown;  
- before disconnection (connection) of HPH, set the power setpoints of 
protections to values corresponding to the new permissible power level of the reactor;  
- steam shutdown of HPH shall be performed in such a way that the rate of 
change of feedwater temperature downstream HPH does not exceed the permissible 
value (55 ºС/h);

- HPH connection shall be performed in compliance with the requirement to

5.5.3.20 Planned shutdown of one RCPS of three (four) operating ones: 
- before disconnection of one RCPS, the RP sh all be unloaded to the 
permissible power not exceeding the regulated value specified in Table 5.2 and 
corresponding to the remaining number of operating RCPS;  
- after RCPS disconnection, power setpoints of protections shall be set to 
values corresponding to the new permissible power level of the reactor;  
- by NPP CE written order, it is allowed to disconnect the SG loop with non -
operating RCPS from feedwater, blowdown water and steam, provided that the BRU-
A valve (11LBA10AA201, 11LBA20AA201, 12LBA30AA201, 12LBA40AA201) is 
changed over to remote control. Water level in the disconnected SG shall be 
maintained within the operation limits. The water quality in the disconnected SG 
shall be maintained in accordance with the WC standards for secondary circuit 
established in accordance with Appendix D as per SG blowdown water readings; 
- after RCPS shutdown, with closed valves on the main pipelines of the 
primary circuit coolant purification system, valves on the bypass line shall be open to 
reduce temperature stresses in the primary circuit makeup nozzles.  
  
5.5.3.21 Connection of one RCPS to two or three operating ones: 
- before the RCPS connection, the reactor power shall be reduced to the 
appropriate level (20% or 30%, respectively) of the nominal one;  
- actuation of RCPS of non -operating loop shall be performed at temperature 
difference bet ween “hot” leg of non -operating loop and “cold” lines of operating 
loops not more than 15 ºС above zero;  
- after connecting the RCPS and stabilizing the parameters, the reactor power 
can be increased to a value corresponding to the new number of operating  RCPS, 
while the reactor protection setpoints shall be set in advance to values corresponding 
to the new power level.  
5.5.3.22 RP operation mode with incomplete number of loops. 
If the loop with the disconnected RCPS is left on “hot” standby, the following 
conditions shall be met: 
- reactor power shall not exceed the permissible value specified in Table 5.2 by 
the number of operating RCPS;  
- level in disconnected SG shall be maintained within ± 100 mm of nominal 
level in the SG;  
- SG shall be fed by FWP (AFWP).  
5.5.3.23 The following requirements shall be met during power rise and 
during RP further operation: 
- monitoring over tightness of RP equipment joints in the primary and 
secondary circuits;

5.5.3.24 The operating personnel shall: 
- monitor the operation of process, electrical equipment , APCS hardware in 
order to identify deviations from the prescribed modes and make decisions on their 
elimination;  
- monitor the operation of automatic controllers;  
- find the reasons for actuation of protections and interlocks, perform the 
necessary act ions to bring the equipment into operating state after actuation of 
protections and interlocks;  
- perform operability checks of equipment and systems;  
- monitor the water chemistry of the primary circuit coolant, secondary circuit 
coolant, working media of the systems and tank facility, if necessary, adjust it;  
- monitor the separation of high and low pressure pipelines of primary and 
secondary circuits in accessible places and disconnect low pressure pipelines of RP 
auxiliary systems by alarm using:  
- boundary valves of these systems from high pressure pipelines;  
- immediately use the EP, PP key in case of EP, PP actuation criteria by 
instrument indications and absence of the respective signal of the root cause and 
action of EP, PP;  
- in case of condi tions that cause ECCS start -up and failure to automatically 
start ECCS mechanisms, the operator shall start them manually;  
- monitor the temperature of equipment and structures;  
- at least once a day check the serviceability of the alarm on the remote co ntrol 
board of hydraulic shock absorbers and the availability of liquid in the tanks of 
hydraulic shock absorbers by secondary monitoring devices located on the board. 
Monitor the position of hydraulic shock absorber pistons every shift by the board 
devices;  
- in steady and transient operation modes in the range of 30 -100% Nnom, if 
necessary, control the axial distribution of power density in the reactor core in 
accordance with Appendix F to this specification;  
- monitor the position of individual CPS CRs  in the control group and align 
them by height, preventing mismatch by more than 2%; 
- monitor sufficiency of CPS and upper unit drives cooling;

5.5.3.25 The following limitations on power distribution in the reactor core 
shall be observed during normal power operation: 
1)  linear heat generation rate of FA (GFE) shall not exceed the values given 
in Appendix F, Figure F.7; 
2)  the relative power of any FE  and GFE at the nominal power of the 
reactor shall not exceed more than 1.57 times (1.35 times for GFE) the average of this 
value for the core; 
3) non-uniformity factors in the core shall not exceed the established maximum 
permissible values given in Table 4.4. 
If at least one of the above conditions is not met, the reactor power shall be 
reduced accordingly. 
5.5.3.26 Personnel shall monitor the metrological characteristics of ICIS and 
perform core monitoring functions with in-core sensors. 
DCD and TT state analysis  is performed at least once a shift based on the 
results of temperature and power density field measurements. Upon completion of the 
PPM, and then, if necessary, confirm the operability of the DCD, but at least once 
every three months, measure the insulation resistance of signal and background DCD 
cores,  in accordance with the ICIS operation documentation. 
5.5.3.27 Monitoring of power density in the core volume is performed in ICIS 
in two different ways. In ICIS CAS-P and in ICIS computing system. 
The ICIS CAS-P algorithms are designed in such a way that each CAS-P 
channel, each monitored point in the core volume have an in -core detector belonging 
to this ICIS CAS-P channel. In case of detector failure, the core points monitored by 
[PAGE 212]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
210 
it become uncontrolled in this ICI S CAS-P channel, but are monitored by other 
detectors belonging to other ICIS CAS-P channels. 
At the upper level (ICIS computing system), an algorithm for restoring the 
power density field is implemented using the indications of all ICDA in the core.  
Two approaches to determining the degrees of degradation are implemented in 
accordance with the algorithms for determining power density in ICIS CAS-P and 
ICIS computing system. These approaches take into account the peculiarities of using 
signals of in-core detectors in each of the algorithms.  
An appropriate alarm is generated for the operating personnel when the 
conditions that characterize a certain degree of “degradation” of ICIS sensors are 
reached. 
ICDA degradation degrees for ICIS CAS-P:  
 the first degr adation degree of ICDA for ICIS CAS-P - when some 
measuring channels are not capable of performing their measuring functions with a 
given error due to a decrease in insulation resistance or DCD failure, or a significant 
level of interference on cable route s, or failure of any component of the ICIS CAS-P 
equipment and uncontrolled volume does not exceed 13 FA provided that there are no 
“local uncontrolled areas”. 
A “local uncontrolled area” is a core section in which all FAs adjacent to the 
FA uncontrolled d ue to ICDA failure are also uncontrolled due to the respective 
ICDA failure. FA is considered uncontrolled due to ICDA failure, if among the three 
ICDA that control it two (or more) are faulty. ICDA is considered faulty if more than 
two DCD located nearby fail; 
 the second degree of ICDA degradation for ICIS CAS-P - when for the 
reasons described above, the uncontrolled volume is not more than 13 FA provided 
that there is at least one “local uncontrolled area”; 
 the third degree of ICDA degradation for ICIS CAS-P occurs when the 
uncontrolled volume of the core ranges from 14 to 82 FA; 
 the fourth degree of ICDA degradation for ICIS CAS-P occurs when the 
part of the core uncontrolled by the DCD is 82 or more FA. 
ICDA degradation degrees for ICIS computing system 
FA power density monitoring in the ICIS computing system is performed not 
only by ICDA installed in the controlled FA, but also by means of surrounding 
ICDA. The first row of the environment comprises FA adjacent to the controlled FA. 
The second row of th e environment comprises FA adjacent to the first row of the 
environment. The third row of the environment comprises FA adjacent to the second 
row of the environment, etc. Figure 2 shows an example of FA rows surrounding the 
controlled FA No. 96. 
 Figure 5. 1 shows an example of FA rows surrounding the controlled FA  
No. 96. 
[PAGE 213]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
211 
 
Figure 5.1 - Rows of FA surrounding the controlled FA 
The following are definitions of degrees of degradation and conditions of their 
occurrence determined for each FA in the core. 
1) Zero degree of degradation  absence of degrees of “degradation” from 
the first to the fourth. 
2) The first degree of degradation  availability of uncontrolled FA with the 
following conditions: 
‒ there is not a single operable ICDA in FA or FA of the first row of the 
environment and there are less than two FA with operable ICDA in the second row of 
the environment of this FA.  
3) The second degree of degradation  availability of uncontrolled FA with 
the following conditions: 
‒ availability of conditions of the first de gree of degradation and the 
availability of less than three FA with operable ICDA in the second and third rows of 
the environment of this FA.  
4) The third degree of degradation  availability of uncontrolled FA with the 
following conditions: 
‒ number of operable ICDA more than 30 and less than 50% and availability 
of conditions of the second degree of degradation. 
5) The fourth degree of degradation  the number of operable ICDAs is less 
than or equal to 30%.  

[PAGE 214]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001

The priority is the degree of “degradation” with a large number. 
Personnel actions when ICIS sensors “degradation” degrees are reached are 
given in Section 7 of Table 7.1.  
5.5.3.28 The recirculation air purification system in the containment can be 
disconnected in case of decrease or loss of the main functions: decre ase of air flow 
rate; decrease of air purification from radionuclides according to radiation monitoring 
data, with start-up of standby equipment. 
5.5.3.29 During the reactor operation it is necessary to perform testing 
(starting) of CPS CR drives located on the upp er limit switch in the individual mode 
of CPS CR movement by two to three steps down from ULS and back with a 
frequency of at least once a month. 
5.5.3.30 RP changeover to MCPL: 
- RP unloading shall be performed with the use of automatic control system 
means during APC-R operation in the mode of pressure maintenance in the secondary 
circuit; it is allowed to perform RP unloading using automatic control system means 
during APC -R operation in “N” mode with indication of target power levels and 
power change rate not more than 3% Nnom/min;  
- check operation switching of detection units from the operating range to the 
start-up range by the indicator. Support the operating group of CPS CR in the control 
area periodically by injecting boric acid solution to the primary circuit;  
- steam pressure in SG shall be maintained within operation limits. Discharge 
excess steam through BRU -K (10MAN11,12,21,22,31,32,41,42AA201) to turbine 
condenser in case of non -compliance of steam production of SG and steam 
consumption by turbine;  
- further power reduction shall be performed by injecting boric acid into the 
primary circuit.  
5.5.3.31 Before RP shutdown: 
- record the state of systems and equipment, parameters of primary and 
secondary circuits;  
- make sure that the I&CD is serviceable and that all automatic protection and 
interlock systems are started;  
- check the readiness for operation of the reactor coolant circuit emergency 
and planned cooldown and fuel pool cooling system, circuit of steam supply for 
auxiliaries;  
- test the systems and equipment in operation that provide TG shutdown;  
- check the availability of the permissible inventory of boric acid concentrated 
solution (39.5 ÷ 44.5 g/dm3) in the KBC40-60 system tanks and free volume (at least 
500 m3) in the KBB system tanks for receiving the primary circuit coolant.  
5.5.3.32 RP operation in the cycle extension mode using the reactivity power 
coefficient. 
After the reactivity margin is exhausted, RP operation in the cycle extension 
mode is allowed using the reactivity power coefficient if the maximum burnup depth 
[PAGE 215]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
213 
and time limitations on FA operation in the reactor given in the fuel technical 
requirements are not disturbed. 
The “Album of neutron -physical characteristics” of the current cycle shall 
contain the necessary calculations of neutron -physical characteristics of the reactor 
core in this mode. 
At the end of the Unit operation using the reactivity power coefficient, the 
reactor thermal power shall not be less than 70% of nominal one at the position of the 
control group 90% of the core bottom. 
RP operation in the cycle extension mode using the reactivity power 
coefficient is allowed for no more than 30 effective days. 
5.5.3.33 When the reactor plant operates in the mode using the reactivity 
power effect, the pressure in the primary and secondary circu its, as well as the 
temperature of the primary circuit coolant at the reactor inlet shall be maintained at 
the nominal level. 
The start of RP operation in the cycle extension mode using the reactivity 
power effect shall be taken as the moment of the cycle when the design value of the 
critical boric acid concentration in the primary circuit coolant during reactor 
operation at the nominal power level and the current position of the operating group 
becomes zero. At the end of the fuel cycle, the boric acid concentration decreases to a 
minimum controlled value close to zero in operation conditions. If the RP was 
operated at a reduced power level at the end of the cycle, then the threshold value of 
boric acid concentration when switching to the mode using the reactivity power effect 
shall correspond to zero in terms of Ncur = Nnom At the current reactor power less 
than 70% of nominal one, the critical value of boric acid concentration in the primary 
circuit coolant shall not be lower than the value corresponding t o zero in terms of 
Ncur = 70% Nnom. 
If at the beginning of RP operation in the cycle extension mode using the 
reactivity power effect the current reactor power exceeds 70% of Nnom., then its 
reduction (to compensate for fuel burnup) is allowed to be performed by: 
- immersion of CPS CR operating group with its subsequent extraction (but 
not more than 90% of the core bottom);  
- increase of boric acid concentration in the primary circuit coolant with its 
subsequent reduction at increase of nuclear fuel burnup;  
- smooth reduction of turbine generator load, while maintaining pressure in the 
secondary circuit within the adjustment range.  
In case of reactor power reduction using CPS CR, power shall decrease 
stepwise at a rate of not more than 3% of Nnom. per min ute. In this case, it is not 
allowed to extract the operating group of CPS CR by height more than 5% per day. 
After each next change in the reactor power, the setpoint of the emergency protection 
actuation by the neutron power level shall be set 7% higher than its current value. If 
the reactor thermal power value and the power value by NFME indications mismatch 
is more than 1%, the NFME calibration shall be performed. 
[PAGE 216]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
214 
When the emergency protection actuates, the boric acid concentration in the 
primary circuit coolant shall be brought in line with the requirements for the end of 
burnup of the reactor core fuel load. After that, the reactor is brought to MCPL after 
CPS CR taking up by boric acid removal from the primary circuit at the operating 
position of the CPS CR control group. 
5.5.3.34 The following checks shall be performed during RP power rise (to a 
certain level): 
- the operability of all APC -R channels under different control laws shall be 
checked one by one at reactor power within auxiliary level (7 - 12% of Nnom); 
- at the power level of 10 -35% of nominal one, stabilize the parameters of the 
primary circuit and pressure in the MSH (at the level of (6.7-6.9) ± 0.1 MPa), analyze 
the operability of the ICIS power density channels and perform preliminary 
calibration of the NFME based on the results of reactor thermal power calculation.  
5.5.3.35 Blowdown in the basic mode as follows: 
- on SG, which is subjected to periodic blowdown:  
1) alternately increase the blowdown flow rate in each of the four Dn 32 
nozzles to 10 t/h; 
2) alternately increase the blowdown flow rate in each of the four Dn 50 
nozzles to 25 t/h; 
3) during this period, blow down from the “salt” compartment with a flow rate 
of up to 30 t/h; 
- continuous blowdown is performed on other SG:  
1) from all Dn 32 sleeves with flow rate up to 5 t/h; 
2) from all Dn 50 nozzles with flow rate up to 5 t/h; 
3) from the “salt” compartment with a flow rate of 15 t/h. 
Then cycle to periodic blowdown of the next SG in turn. 
In case of disturbance of water chemistry parameters,  set the following 
blowdown rates at all SG (including SG, on which periodic blowdown was 
performed): 
- from the “salt” compartment with increased flow rate of 25 t/h;  
- from all Dn 32 sleeves (header pockets) up to 5 t/h;  
- of all Dn 50 nozzles (on the bottom of the housing) up to 5 t/h.  
Return to the blowdown algorithm in the basic mode after restoration of SG 
water quality indicators. 
Frequency and duration of SG blowdown actuation are determined by the 
blowdown system operation schedule. 
5.6 Unit operation in the “cooldown” state 
5.6.1 Operational conditions in the “cooldown” state 
5.6.1.1 Requirements for Unit operation organization are defined in  
Section 9. 
5.6.1.2 Before Unit changeover to the “cooldown” state, the operational 
conditions specified for this state in Table 2.1 shall be met. 
[PAGE 217]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
215 
5.6.1.3 The requirements for the state of operability of systems and 
equipment given in column 9, Table G.1, Appendix G of this specification shall be 
fulfilled before Unit changeover to the “cooldown” state. 
5.6.1.4 RP “cooldown” state is characterized by the following conditions: 
- the reactor is sub-critical, all CPS CR are on BLS;  
- concentration of boric acid solution in the primary circuit coolant provides 
reactor sub-criticality of at least 2 % (excluding CPS CR submerged into the core).  
5.6.1.5 There sha ll be a steam or nitrogen blanket in the PRZ during 
cooldown, the level in the PRZ shall be maintained at 10,900 ± 150 mm during the 
entire process. 
5.6.1.6 When the water temperature in the PRZ is above 210 - 230 ºС above 
zero, the required pressure in the primary circuit shall be provided by exceeding the 
water temperature in the PRZ over the water temperature in the RCC. This excess 
shall be maintained by the cooldown controller at 55 ºС above zero. 
5.6.1.7 Operation of connected TEH units is not allowed at water level in the 
PRZ below 3600 mm. 
5.6.1.8 During cooldown at least two RCPS are in operation, the rest are 
ready for operation, cooling water of component cooling system and sealing water are 
supplied to them; RCPS oil system is in operation. Operation of more than three 
RCPS is prohibited at primary circuit temperature less than 200 ºС above zero. 
5.6.1.9 Levels shall be maintained in the SG from 3700 to 3800 mm at the 
cooldown stage to 120 ºС above zero. 
5.6.1.10 A day before the start of RP cooldown, ammonia and hydrazine 
hydrate injection from the reagent supply system to the primary circuit coolant, to the 
makeup water of the primary circuit is stopped in order to reduce the hydro gen 
concentration in the coolant to a value not lower than 1.3 mg/dm3. 
5.6.1.11 The “Cooldown mode” key on the safety system panels shall be 
switched to “On” after creation of the required concentration of boric acid in the 
primary circuit coolant and before the st art of operations to increase the levels in the 
PRZ and SG. 
5.6.1.12 During cooldown, the rate of pressure change in the primary circuit 
shall not exceed 0.98 MPa per minute. 
5.6.1.13 The rate of cooldown of the primary circuit coolant shall not exceed 
15 ºС/h with non-operating RCPS. 
5.6.2 General procedure for performance of safety related operations 
5.6.2.1 Fill PRZ to the level of at least 11600 ± 150 mm before cooldown. 
5.6.2.2 Before the SG filling begins, disable the protections to switch off the 
RCPS by level in the SG, change over the AH power supply from the CSAH. The 
steam generators shall be filled to the maximum possible controlled level of 3800 mm 
before cooldown. 
5.6.2.3 During cooldown, switch off the  primary circuit pressure controller, 
switch on the PRZ cooldown controller and start PRZ cooldown by injecting the 
[PAGE 218]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
216 
primary circuit coolant from the RCPS head. Begin to discharge steam from the 
steam generators through BRU -K (10MAN11,12,21,22,31,32,41,42AA 201) to the 
turbine condenser in an amount that provides the cooldown rate of the primary circuit 
coolant not more than 30 ºС above zero when the difference of 55 ºС above zero 
between the temperature in the PRZ and the temperature of the primary circuit 
coolant is reached. 
5.6.2.4 Make up the steam generators from the deaerator. Feedwater 
temperature shall decrease uniformly from 164 ºС to 40 ºС above zero. The 
temperature difference between the metal of the upper and lower parts of the SG 
housing shall not exceed 80 ºС above zero. 
5.6.2.5 It is necessary to change over feedwater supply to the SG from FWP 
to AFWP when feedwater flow rate in the SG decreases to 250 t/h. 
5.6.2.6 During RP cooldown, disconnect ECCS HA from the reactor at the 
primary circuit pressure of 8.8 - 9.8 MPa. 
Close the gate valves at all HA PCFS after pressure decrease in the primary 
circuit to 3 MPa. 
5.6.2.7 If the pressure in the primary circuit is less than 2.45 MPa (25 
kgf/cm2), the KBE50 -60 (KBE) bypass shall be open, the blowdown of the primary 
circuit shall be changed over to the controlled leakage tank. 
5.6.2.8 Open the valves on the line of nitrogen supply to the PRZ when the 
pressure above the core reaches 2.0 MPa. Nitrogen temperature is 40 -80 ºС above 
zero The volume of nitrogen supply reduced to a pressure of 2.0 MPa is 4 m 3, the 
supply time is 4 hours. 
When operating on a nitrogen blanket, monitor the concentration of dissolved 
gas in the primary circuit coolant, which shall not exceed the permissible value of 20 
mg/kg. Constant gas blowing from the RCPS independent circuit shall be performed 
when operating on a nitrogen blanket 
5.6.2.9 After nitrogen supply to the PRZ, disconnect the PRZ cooldown 
controller and perform further PRZ cooldown without maintaining temperature 
difference between the PRZ and the primary circuit coolant. 
5.6.2.10 During cooldown, continue blowdown at all SG simultaneously in 
the mode specified in Item 5.3.2 until the blowdown system pumps are shut down at a 
temperature of about 150 ºС above zero to provide cleanliness of the lower generatrix 
of the housing and “pockets” of the headers. 
5.6.2.11 Do the following when the primary circuit coolant temperature is less 
than 130 ºС above zero: 
а) disassemble the electric circuits of ejector pumps of  the JNA reactor coolant 
circuit emergency planned cooldown system; 
b) disassemble the electric circuits of the JND emergency boron injection 
system pumps; 
c) disassemble the electric circuits of PRZ TEH units; 
d) reduce pressure in the ECCS HA less than 3.43 MPa. 
[PAGE 219]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
217 
5.6.2.12 It is allowed not to reduce the pressure in the ECCS HA, at the same 
time, the fast -acting gate valves shall be closed, the electric circuits shall be 
disassembled and the gate valves themselves shall be locked, the drains between the 
gate valves shall be open. 
5.6.2.13 Connect the circuit of the reactor coolant circuit emergency and 
planned cooldown and fuel pool cooling system after the primary circuit coolant 
temperature decreases to 110-120 ºС above zero and the cooldown rate decreases less 
than 10 ºС/h. The second channel can be switched on to increase the cooldown rate . 
5.6.2.14 Before connecting the planned cooldown circuit of JNA system, 
reduce pressure in the PRZ to 1.5 -1.7 MPa (15 -17 kgf/cm2) by nitrogen discharge 
into the gas blow-off system. RCPS remain in operation. 
5.6.2.15 The operating and standby channels of the specified system shall be 
heated up before switching on the reactor coolant circuit emergency and planned 
cooldown and fuel pool cooling system to the planned cooldown mode. The 
temperature difference between water supplied from the system and in the primary 
circuit shall not exceed 40 ºС above zero. 
5.6.2.16 The cooldown stage with steam discharge from SG to turbine 
condensers with operating RCPS ends at the temperature level in the secondary 
circuit of 70 -80 ºС above zero Further SG cooldown is performed due to multiple 
water exchange. 
5.6.2.17 Switch off the RCPS remaining in operation when the water 
temperature in the RCC at the reactor core outlet reaches 60 - 70 ºС above zero or 
pressure in the RCPL decreases less than 1.96 MPa. 
The reactor coolant circuit emergency and planned cooldown and fuel pool 
cooling system remains in operation in the mode of residual heat removal of the core. 
5.6.2.18 After all RCPS switching -off, further PRZ cooldown shall be 
performed by water supply from the primary circuit makeup system to a temperature 
of 60 - 70 ºС above zero. 
5.6.2.19 Chemical washing of steam generators. 
Chemical washing of steam generators is performed in the process of Unit 
cooldown and/or Unit shutdown during PPM in accordance with  the technical 
specification for the operation of PGV-1000MKP steam generator. 
5.6.2.20 The cooling system of the upper unit equipment, the reactor pit 
volume shall be in operation during the entire cooldown process. 
5.6.2.21 Taking the systems and equipment out of operatio n is performed in 
accordance with the operation instructions given the need for their operation in this 
mode. 
5.6.3 Rules and basic methods of RP safe operation during cooldown 
5.6.3.1 PRZ cooldown shall be performed from RCPS. PRZ cooldown shall 
be performed from makeu p pumps in case of non -operating RCPS and impossibility 
of their actuation. The difference between the temperature of the primary circuit 
coolant in the PRZ and the temperature of the primary circuit coolant at the supply 
[PAGE 220]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
218 
from the water makeup pumps shall be less than 90 ºС above zero. Injection into PRZ 
from makeup pumps when the reactor is in natural circulation shall be performed at a 
flow rate of not more than 60 m3/h. 
5.6.3.2 In the process of RP cooldown, the minimum possible temperature 
difference at the primary circuit makeup nozzles shall be provided by operation of the 
primary circuit volume and chemical control system with the maximum possible 
capacity while maintaining the required level in the PRZ. 
5.6.3.3 Perform water exchange sequentially at each SG in compl iance with 
the following requirements at 120 0С above zero to reduce SG water quality 
indicators: 
- drain SG with flow rate of at least 60 t/h;  
- temperature difference between SG housing and supplied water during filling 
shall not exceed 60 0С above zero;  
- for the period of water exchange do not a llow the primary circuit coolant 
temperature to decrease less than 100℃ above zero.  
Upon completion of water exchange in the SG, restore the maximum possible 
controlled level of 3800 mm and continue cooldown of the primary circuit coolant 
using BRU-K (10MAN11,12,21,22,31,32,41,42AA201) to a temperature of 60 -70℃ 
above zero. 
5.6.3.4 Sealing water supply to all RCPS is mandatory at the level of the 
primary circuit coolant above the main RCPS joint. If the level of the primary circuit 
coolant is below the main RCPS joint, the sealing water is not supplied, the valves on 
its drain shall be open. 
5.6.3.5 Perform gas removal from the primary circuit and degassing of the 
primary circuit coolant. Ensure the following in order to exclude explosive 
concentrations of hydrogen in the primary circuit in the “cold” state: 
a) injection of boric acid and water exchange during cooldown shall be 
performed at maximum blowdown of the primary circuit with provision of at least 
three-fold water exchange of the primary circuit coolant until the t emperature is less 
than 100℃ above zero with monitoring of hydrogen concentration and activity in the 
primary circuit coolant; 
b) dosing of hydrazine hydrate and ammonia into makeup water during 
cooldown and in the “cold” state is not performed; 
c) operation of the primary circuit makeup deaerator in steam mode until the 
primary circuit coolant pressure drops less than 0.49 MPa. 
5.6.3.6 It is necessary to change over feedwater supply to the SG from FWP 
to AFWP when feedwater flow rate in the SG decreases to 250 t/h. 
5.6.3.7 During the time when the forced circulation through the reactor core 
is stopped, monitor the availability of natural circulation through the reactor core and 
the availability of temperature surge of boiling margin of at least 15 ℃ above zero at 
the FA outlet. In this case, heat is removed through the secondary circuit, BRU -A 
(11LBA10AA201, 11LBA20AA201, 12LBA30AA201, 12LBA40AA201) is in 
operation.
