Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
219 
5.6.3.8 The personnel shall ens ure the equipment preservation during RP 
planned shutdown. 
5.7 Unit operation in the “shutdown for repair” state 
5.7.1 Operational conditions in the “shutdown for repair” state 
5.7.1.1 Requirements for Unit operation organization are defined in  
Section 9. 
5.7.1.2 Before Unit chang eover to the “shutdown for repair” state, the 
operational conditions given in Table 3.8 for this state shall be met. 
5.7.1.3 The requirements for the state of operability of systems and 
equipment given in column 10, Table G.1, Appendix G of this specification shal l be 
met before Unit changeover to the “shutdown for repair” state. 
5.7.1.4 The RP “shutdown for repair” state is characterized by the following 
conditions and parameters: 
- reactor is sub-critical, all CPS CR are on LAS;  
- concentration of boric acid in the primary circuit is 16÷20 g/dm3;  
- primary circuit coolant temperature at the reactor outlet and in the PRZ is less 
than 70 ºС above zero;  
pressure in the primary circuit is equal to the atmospheric one;  
- the level in the reactor is 300 ÷ 400 mm lower than MRJ or reduced for repair 
work, but not lower than (600 ± 50) mm above the axis of “cold” reactor nozzles;  
- primary circuit is unsealed.  
5.7.1.5 Boron concentrate tanks of the KBC40 -60 system contain at least 
150 m3 of boric acid solution with boric acid concentration in the range of 39.5 - 44.5 
g/dm3. 
5.7.2 General procedure for performance of safety related operations 
5.7.2.1 The following is performed when RP is put to “shutdown for repair” 
state: 
- degassing of the primary circuit coolant; 
- primary circuit coolant drain to the required level that enables repair works.   
5.7.2.2 RCC unsealing is performed after the pressure in the primary circuit 
decreases to atmospheric one at the temperature of the primary circuit coolant at the 
reactor outlet 60-70℃. 
Before unsealing of the MRJ, disconnect the electrical connectors of the loops 
from the CPS drives, INDA, dismantle the removable parts of the insulation units of 
the cooling air ducts of the CPS drives, the air duct of the upper unit, electrical wiring 
and the reactor air duct, as well as install the covers of  the hatches of the air duct into 
the shaft of the RP. 
5.7.2.3 Before removal of UU, CPS drive rods shall be disengaged from 
CPS AR and installed to transport position on lock pins. It is prohibited to remove 
UU in the availability of CPS CR not disengaged from their rods. 
[PAGE 222]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
220 
ICDA channels shall be removed with monitoring of extraction force in 
accordance with the requirements of operational documentation for ICDA only with 
permission and under proper supervision of the radiation safety subdivision personnel 
during all transport and handling operations, including their disposal. Avoid flooding 
of ICDA channel connectors.  
5.7.2.4 The circulation of the primary circuit coolant shall be arranged no 
earlier than 48 hours after reactor shutdown over the “repair circuit”: water sup ply to 
the reactor on top of the core from the pump of the emergency planned cooldown 
system, water removal through the “cold” leg of the RCPL loop in order to perform 
repair works on the primary circuit equipment that require a decrease in the primary 
circuit coolant level by more than 400 mm from the MRJ elevation, but not lower 
than (600 ± 50) mm above the axis of the “cold” nozzles, and not require core 
unloading. 
5.7.2.5 Repair of valves on pipelines connected to the primary circuit (the 
first downstream on the primary circuit side) and located below (600 ± 50) mm above 
the axis of the “cold” nozzles (construction elevation +13.3) shall be performed 
subject to complete FA unloading from the core. 
5.7.2.6 The following operations shall be performed during RP preparation  
for refueling: 
- reactor is disassembled, UU and PTU are removed; 
- FP is inspected and there are free cells in sufficient quantity for emergency 
unloading of the whole reactor core;  
- lining of fuel pools, RVI inspection cavities is checked for tightness and there 
are no leaks;  
- load lifting cranes and slings, devices for storage of CPS drive rods and 
movement units, MRJ nut wrench, refueling machine and RM FCIMS are prepared 
for operation and accepted for cleanliness;  
- RMS system shall be prepared for operation, checked from neutron source.  
5.7.2.7 Drain the reactor to a level 300 ÷ 400 mm below RMJ after 
completion of refueling during reactor assembly. Decrease of level above 400 mm 
below the RMJ elevation is prohibited. 
5.7.2.8 Install the RMS sensors using the m ovement mechanisms to the 
bottom limit position. De -energize movement mechanisms. Take RMS out of 
operation. 
5.7.2.9 In accordance with the current operation documentation, assemble 
the primary circuit and reactor, including the installation of PTU and UU of the 
reactor according to a special program. 
5.7.2.10 Check the CPS drive rod engagement with the CPS AR according to 
the program. Monitor the rod retainer entering the CPS AR by 35 mm and the 
absence of CPS CR rubbing. Additionally, the engagement shall be monitored by 
weight increase on the rod key. 
Check the forces of moving the rod from the CPS AR in each cell for the 
3720 mm travel from the upper unit using a dynamometer. Forces shall not exceed 
[PAGE 223]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
221 
440 N when moving upwards and shall not be less than 240N when moving 
downwards. The acceptance criterion is the value of the friction force defined as the 
half-difference of the maximum (during the upward travel) and the minimum (during 
the downward travel) values of moving forces in each cell, which shall be no more 
than 100N when inspecting from the upper unit. It is necessary to constantly monitor 
the state of the reactor core through all channels of the NFME start -up range when 
implementing this Item. It is necessary to lower CPS CR into the core in case of 
neutron flux increase wh en checking rods engagement with CPS CR. Engagement 
testing operations can be continued after determining and eliminating the reasons for 
the neutron flux increase. 
The rod shall be lifted at a level in the reactor of 300-400 mm below the MRJ. 
Install CPS CR drive position sensors. 
5.7.2.11 Check the hydraulic resistance factor of the ECCS HA - reactor line 
on the unsealed circuit for compliance with the design values by spilling water from 
one of the HA. 
5.7.2.12 Install UU equipment, install safety devices and cross -beam on the 
UU. Take measures to avoid spontaneous pressure increase in the primary circuit. 
Perform MRJ and primary circuit sealing. 
5.7.2.13 Do the following in the “shutdown for repair” state when one safety 
system channel is taken out of the “Standby” state for plann ed M&R of thermal 
mechanical and electric parts in order to increase the reliability of the operating 
emergency planned cooldown system: 
1)  line up the electric circuit of the JNA system high pressure pump 
(11JNA12AP001, 12JNA22AP001); 
2)  put the high pr essure pump (11JNA12AP001, 12JNA22AP001) into 
operation in case of failure of the JNA system low pressure pump (11JNA11AP001, 
12JNA21AP001); 
3)  technical measures shall exclude the possibility of filling the equipment 
of the primary circuit from the FP du ring operation of the JNA system high pressure 
pump; 
4)  do not allow level increase in PRZ more than 8000 mm during operation 
of the JNA system high pressure pump. 
5.7.3 Rules and basic methods of safe operation in the “shutdown for repair” 
state 
5.7.3.1 When performing scheduled repairs of the RP and works directly on 
the primary circuit after pressure release and lowering the level in the reactor to MRJ, 
it is necessary to provide the dismantling of UU or disassembly of three central CPS 
drives with the extraction of position sensors within no more than a day and arrange 
nitrogen blowdown over the path: nitrogen system - reactor air vent valve - CPS drive 
housings - central hall, with monitoring of hydrogen concentration in the central hall 
air. Hydrogen concentration in the CH air in nitrogen outlet area from CPS housings 
shall not exceed 0.8%. 
[PAGE 224]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
222 
5.7.3.2 If long-term (more than 2 days) reactor staying in the assembled state 
is required, provide the water level in the reactor no more than the axis of the “hot” 
nozzles and arrange  blowdown of the upper points (SG header, reactor cover) over 
the path: nitrogen system - air vent valves of the headers of each SG - reactor air vent 
valve - housings of three CPS drives - central hall, with monitoring of hydrogen 
concentration in the central hall air. Hydrogen concentration in the CH air in nitrogen 
outlet area from CPS housings shall not exceed 0.8%. 
5.7.3.3 It is prohibited to unseal the primary circuit without preliminary 
repeated removal of radioactive gases from the RCC and with the gas puri fication 
system not in operation, as well as with faulty (not operating) FP ventilation systems. 
5.7.3.4 In case of primary circuit coolant temperature increase more than 70 
℃ above zero at the inlet to the emergency planned cooldown heat exchanger: 
- remove air from the heat exchanger;  
- switch to standby cooldown channel;  
- if necessary, switch on two channels in parallel operation.  
5.7.3.5 Level reduction in the SG to nominal value is allowed after 
cooldown of primary and secondary circuits to 60 ÷ 70 ℃ above zero. 
5.7.3.6 Shut-off devices shall be installed in SG headers when taking the SG 
out of service for repair in the headers over the primary circuit if there is a need to 
increase the primary circuit coolant level above the reactor hot nozzles. Stop repair 
works in the S G headers, remove the personnel, appoint the observer if shut -off 
devices are unavailable and there is a need to change the level of the primary circuit 
coolant in the reactor. 
5.7.3.7 Drain of the primary circuit over the loops drain line shall be 
performed at a flow rate of not more than 5 m 3/h at the temperature of the primary 
circuit coolant at the reactor outlet 60 -70 ℃ above zero. Reduce the drain flow rate 
by closing one of the loop drain valves when draining the primary circuit and 
increasing the activity of emissions into the ventilation stack. 
When draining the PRT and increasing the activity of emissions into the 
ventilation stack, stop draining the PRT, fill the hydraulic locks of the controlled 
leaks tank, operating grade primary circuit coolant storage tanks. Periodic monitoring 
of hydraulic locks state shall be performed. 
5.7.3.8 During internal inspection of PRZ, ECCS HA, PCFS and SG 
headers, it is necessary to thoroughly blow (ventilate) pipelines and tanks with air. 
5.7.3.9 Prevent the installation of a support in the open RCPS housing or any 
other devices that prevent water circulation in the reactor cooldown circuit when 
repairing the removed part of RCPS. If repair works are required in the RCPS volute, 
it is allowed to install supports or other devices that do n ot interfere with the primary 
circuit coolant circulation in the cooldown circuit. In this case, their application shall 
be duly agreed with the RP Chief Designer. 
5.7.3.10 Equipment and pipelines of the secondary circuit, which are not 
repaired, may be left filled  with feedwater during shutdown. When refilling 
equipment after repair, it is allowed to fill it with demineralized water. 
[PAGE 225]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
223 
5.7.3.11 Reactor disassembly is performed in compliance with the 
requirements of the current operation documentation. UU and PTU dismantling i s 
performed according to a special program. 
5.7.3.12 After UU dismantling, at least two pumps of the JNA reactor coolant 
circuit emergency and planned cooldown and fuel pool cooling system shall be ready 
for operation. 
5.7.3.13 Monitor the following parameters when lifting UU or PTU: 
- neutron power and reactor period;  
- level in the reactor and PRZ;  
- radiation situation in the central hall.  
When the neutron power indications or period, radiation situation change, the 
dismantling operations shall be stopped and the UU or  PTU shall be returned to their 
original place until the causes are clarified and eliminated. 
The inspection of the reactor core for the absence of foreign items shall be 
performed using the television camera of the refueling machine after removal of 
PTU. 
5.7.3.14 CPS drives may be replaced when the UU is in the inspection cavity, 
installation and removal of CPS drives may be performed at the reactor in exceptional 
cases with measures taken to prevent foreign items from entering the reactor. 
5.7.3.15 Install the RMS with mon itoring of sensors installation in the baffle 
channels in the reactor using the television camera, set RMS detection units to the 
upper limit position. Put the RMS into operation, put the reactor power and reactor 
period monitoring equipment on the refueling machine control panel into operation. 
5.7.3.16 Prepare the equipment of the systems necessary to provide the filling 
process of the FP. Check the operability of FP I&CD and alarm. 
5.7.3.17 Decontaminate and clean the bellows and reactor cavity. 
5.7.3.18 Close the valves of drains  and lower overflows from the FP, drain 
from the bellows of the reactor concrete cantilever to the active drain system drain, 
drains and overflows from the RVI and PTU inspection cavities, disassemble the 
electric circuits, lock the handwheels with chains,  put up posters “Do not turn on!” 
in-situ and in the control assemblies. 
5.7.3.19 Fill the reactor pit and RVI and PTU inspection cavities before 
overflow into the FP to the elevation of 25.35 ÷ 25.55 m. When filling, perform 
continuous monitoring of: 
- level in reactor and FP in-situ and at MCR;  
- neutron flux and reactor period and primary circuit coolant temperature in the 
reactor;  
- lining tightness in the pit volume;  
- tightness of the hatch covers of the UU air duct in the RP pit.  
Check the absence of leaks: 
- through plugs of reactor bellows drains;  
- through the hatch covers of the UU air duct in the RP pit;  
- on lining of FP and reactor pit.  
[PAGE 226]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
224 
Carefully remove air from the SG headers over the primary circuit and from 
the PRZ when filling the primary cir cuit and pit volume. Close and disassemble the 
electric circuits of valves on FP filling lines. 
5.7.3.20 Clean the water in the FP until the transparency is at least 95%. 
5.7.3.21 The operating personnel shall do the following in the “shutdown for 
repair” state: 
1)  perform continuous monitoring of neutron flux density; 
2)  monitor the concentration of boric acid in the primary circuit and FP, and 
maintain its value in the range of 16÷20 g/dm3; 
3)    monitor every shift the implementation of measures to prevent water from 
entering the primary circuit with boric acid concentration below the circuit one with 
registration of test results in operational logbooks; 
4)  provide automatic monitoring of the primary circuit coolant level in the 
reactor with registration at the MCR; 
5)  monitor the water chemistry of the primary and secondary circuits, their 
auxiliary systems and perform its correction. Observe the volume and frequency of 
chemical quality control of the primary circuit coolant and makeup water of the 
primary circuit. Monitoring of WC state of working media of primary and secondary 
circuits shall be performed in accordance with the requirements of Appendix D of 
this specification; 
6)  ensure the readiness for operation of all systems by the process need for 
their use and production instructions; 
7)  during operation of the emergency planned cooldown system over the 
repair cooldown circuit, do not allow the level in the reactor to decrease below (600 ± 
50) mm above the axis of the “cold” reactor nozzles, the temperature of t he primary 
circuit coolant at the emergency planned cooldown heat exchanger inlet to increase 
more than 70 ºС above zero. At the same time, observe measures to prevent the 
formation of fire and explosion hazardous concentrations of hydrogen. 
5.8 Unit operation in the “refueling” state 
5.8.1 Operational conditions in the “refueling” state 
5.8.1.1 Requirements for Unit operation organization are defined in  
Section 9. 
5.8.1.2 Before Unit changeover to the “refueling” state, the operational 
conditions given in Table 3.8 for this state shall be met. 
5.8.1.3 The requirements for the state of operability of systems and 
equipment given in column 11, Table G.1, Appendix G of this specification shall be 
fulfilled before Unit changeover to the “refueling” state. 
5.8.1.4 The RP “refueling” state is characterized by the following conditions 
and parameters: 
- reactor sub -criticality of at least 2 % is provided (excluding CPS CR 
submerged into the core), boric acid concentration in the primary circuit coolant, 
refueling pond and fuel pool is at least 16 g/dm3;  
[PAGE 227]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
225 
- primary circuit coolant temperature at the reactor outlet is less than 60 oC 
above zero;  
- primary circuit coolant temperature in the fuel pool during refueling 
operations is less than 60 ℃ above zero;  
- UU and PTU are removed;  
- refueling pond is filled with boric acid solution of proper quality with 
concentration of 16÷20 g/dm3 to the level of 25.35÷25.55 m;  
- hydraulic locks of transport channel are removed.  
5.8.2 General procedure for performance of safety related operations 
5.8.2.1 It is prohibited to start operations with nuclear fuel without fulfillment 
of the following conditions: 
- the ARMS syst em is operable, in operation and provides continuous 
monitoring in the reactor compartment (UJA) premises, including in the CH in the FP 
area;  
- the refueling system equipment power supply system is operable, the lighting 
network in the CH has been inspected, deficiencies have been eliminated; 
- the reactor is sub-critical for at least 72 hours and dismantled; 
- monitoring of neutron state of reactor core is provided with the help of six 
RMS channels and three channels of one of NFME sets at MCR and ECR, B SR-01 
optical-acoustic indicator is serviceable; 
- the process flow diagram of the upper FP overflows has been prepared; 
- the FP cooldown system pump is in operation and at least one more pump of 
the system is on standby, I&CD and alarm, protection and in terlocks of the system 
are serviceable and put into operation; 
- at least one process leg of the KBH system is operable (anion exchange filters 
- in boron form); 
- measures to eliminate the possibility of supplying media with boric acid 
concentration below 16 g/dm3 to the primary circuit, FP are provided;  
- refueling machine is operable, integrated check of RM is performed, no more 
than three days have passed since the end of protections and interlocks check; 
- communication between MCR, refueling machine panel, central hall and 
dosimetry service is provided; 
- the CIM system is operable, including the process part of FADS; 
- deviation of the main reactor joint plane from horizontal is checked; 
- water quality in the fuel pool shall meet the requirements of Appendix D. 
5.8.2.2 Irradiated fuel shall not be removed from the reactor core or FP if the 
water level above the irradiated fuel assembly is less than 2.3 m. 
5.8.2.3 All refueling operations shall be stopped during the process 
operations to change the water level in the FP or reactor. 
5.8.2.4 Emptying of the reactor is allowed only after complete unloading of 
fuel from the reactor. 
[PAGE 228]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
226 
5.8.2.5 The time of termination of forced circulation through the primary 
circuit due to the operation of the cooldown line is not limited when fuel is 
completely discharged from the reactor core. 
5.8.3 Rules and basic methods of safe operation in the “refueling” state 
5.8.3.1 Refueling operations shall be performed in a sequence defined by the 
working program and working schedule of fuel handling operations. 
5.8.3.2 The housing wi th fresh FA is transported to the dry container 
compartment of FP filled with water to the elevation plus 21,100 m and installed on 
the multi-purpose socket. 
5.8.3.3 Operations on spent fuel unloading from the reactor to the FP, fuel 
rearrangement inside the react or core and new fuel loading into the reactor are 
performed using RM. 
5.8.3.4 Refueling shall be stopped in the following cases: 
- primary circuit coolant temperature increase in the FP and at the reactor core 
outlet more than 70 ℃ above zero; 
- decrease of boric acid concentration in FP coolant, primary circuit below 16 
g/dm3; 
- in case of failure of one or more channels until the system is fully operational; 
- at decrease of water level in FP more than 100 mm of nominal one; 
- fall of FA, CPS AR or any other items into the reactor core or FP. 
In the event of a stable period of reactor power increase of 200 seconds or less 
recorded by at least one of the RMS channels, all nuclear -hazardous operations shall 
be stopped until the reasons for changing the RMS equipment indications are 
clarified and eliminated. 
5.8.3.5 During refueling, constant monitoring of water level and temperature 
in the FP  shall be performed. When the water level decreases or the temperature 
increases, the refueling of nuclear fuel immediately stops, the causes of such a 
deviation are clarified and eliminated. 
5.8.3.6 Periodic monitoring of boric acid concentration with sampling fr om 
the primary circuit shall be performed when refueling the reactor nuclear fuel. If an 
spontaneous decrease in the concentration of boric acid (less than 16 g/dm 3) in the 
reactor vessel is detected, refueling operations shall be stopped until the causes are 
clarified and the required concentration of boric acid is restored. 
5.8.3.7 Periodic monitoring of the implementation of measures to prevent 
spontaneous water supply with a boric acid concentration less than the regulated one 
(16 g/dm 3) to the primary circuit or FP shall be provided during refueling of the 
reactor. 
5.8.3.8 A gamma radiation dose rate monitoring channel with a sensor 
installed above the FP compartment and a measuring instrument shall be provided 
and serviceable as an additional measure of monitoring the  nuclear fission chain 
reaction during refueling and transportation of spent FA to the FP. It is necessary to 
monitor the state of the radiation situation in the CH. 
[PAGE 229]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
227 
Do not drain water from the FP without monitoring radiation situation. 
5.8.3.9 Perform constant mo nitoring of water temperature in the fuel pool, 
which shall not exceed 60 ºС above zero. If the water temperature in the FP increases 
more 60 ºС above zero, identify and eliminate the cause that led to the water 
temperature increase. 
5.8.3.10 When refueling nuclear  fuel, it is allowed to stop forced circulation 
through the reactor core when performing switching on the emergency planned 
cooldown system. In this case, monitor the temperature at the reactor outlet, which 
shall not exceed 80 ºС above zero Allowable time  of circulation termination is not 
more than 2.5 hours with filled FP. 
5.8.3.11 The time for stopping forced circulation is not limited when nuclear 
fuel is completely discharged from the reactor. Emptying of the reactor is allowed 
only after complete unloading of nuclear fuel from the reactor. 
5.8.3.12 Removal and installation of the hydraulic lock between the reactor 
cavity and the FP shall be performed when the RM is in the pool area adjacent to the 
transport channel. The RM shall be above the FP when performing installat ion-
removal of hydraulic lock in transport channel between the FP and the FP container 
compartment. 
5.8.3.13 During NF refueling, the operating personnel shall monitor the water 
chemistry in the reactor core and in the fuel pool and, if necessary, adjust it. 
5.8.3.14 Simultaneous horizontal and vertical movement of FA, CPS AR in 
RM controls is prohibited. 
5.8.3.15 The entire complex of transport and handling operations with FA, 
CPS AR performed by the refueling machine shall be monitored using a television 
camera installed on the RM. 
5.8.3.16 It is prohibited to perform work with a refueling machine in the 
reactor core, in the FP with a faulty television camera. 
5.8.3.17 In case of detection of FA or CPS AR damage during transport and 
handling operations, the issue of possibility of their use shall be decided together with 
representatives of the Chief Designer and manufacturer plant by making a technical 
decision. 
5.8.3.18 The fuel cladding tightness shall be checked during refueling. CIM 
scope and procedure during PPM at the shut down reactor plant is determine d 
according to the CIM data at the operating reactor, by the core refueling program. 
5.8.3.19 If it is necessary to perform FE CIM at the shut down reactor, fuel 
loading FA CIM is performed by operational monitoring in the refueling machine rod 
(RM FCIMS) and/or in  the FADS. FA detected as leaky by the RM FCIMS method 
are subject to mandatory monitoring using FADS in order to confirm the leak 
condition and determine the possibility of further FA operation. 
The fuel assembly failure criterion is the value set in the fuel supply 
documentation. 
[PAGE 230]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
228 
 For FA identified as leaky based on the results of monitoring in the RM 
FCIMS and in the FADS, the NPP management may decide to inspect and/or repair 
them at the FA T&RR. 
5.8.3.20 The following shall be operable when the reactor core is fully 
unloaded: 
- FAK10 FP cooling system channel; 
- channel of PEB service water system of essential loads fully corresponding to 
operable channel of FP cooling system; 
- MCR and ECR devices, alarm and automation circuits of protections and 
interlocks of these systems. 
5.8.3.21 Do the following upon completion of refueling operations: 
1)  check the correctness of core loading in accordance with the approved 
map of the next fuel loading using a RM television camera; 
2)  check the elevation location of FA heads.  Mut ual height positioning of 
FA heads of the same operation year shall not differ by more than 5 mm; 
3)  use the television camera and refueling machine to inspect the core and 
make sure that there are no foreign items and damages, loading and location of FA,  
CPS AR are correct;  
4)  install the gates between the RPIT and FP on the standard places, seal 
them.

6 Nuclear fuel handling 
6.1 General provisions 
Nuclear fuel (NF) storage and handling system complex is a set of systems, 
devices, components intended for nuc lear fuel storage, loading, unloading, 
transportation and monitoring. 
The complex comprises the following systems for performing all operations 
with nuclear fuel within the power plant: 
- new fuel storage system; 
- refueling system; 
- system of fuel cladding integrity monitoring at shut down reactor; 
- spent fuel storage system; 
- system of in-plant movement of nuclear fuel. 
Radiation safety during NF handling, including FNF, shall be ensured in 
accordance with the requirements of the Rooppur NPP Regulation for radia tion 
monitoring. 
6.2 Incoming inspection of FA 
6.2.1 Depreservation and incoming inspection of FA and CPS AR (check of 
data sheets, marking, appearance) are performed in accordance with the manufacturer 
instruction.  
6.2.2 Accounting for FA, control if their location, quantity and movement are 
performed in the fresh fuel storage facility (FFSF).  
6.2.3 Each FA is marked with designation of FA number and its enrichment. 
FA identification in FFSF is performed visually. 
6.2.4 If during the incoming inspection any defect of FA (CPS AR) is  
detected, then the issue of acceptance of fuel for operation or its rejection is decided 
by the commission comprising representatives of the manufacturer and NPP.  
6.2.5 Defective fresh FA can be stored in the FFSF in packaging sets. 
6.2.6 Accounting is performed by factory numbers on FA 
6.2.7 At Rooppur NPP one hundred percent accounting of nuclear fuel and 
its movement within NPP shall be provided. 
6.3 Fresh fuel storage in the FFSF 
6.3.1 Transport and handling operations performed in the fresh fuel storage 
facility comprise: 
 acceptance and storage of fresh nuclear fuel; 
 visual inspection of FA before loading into the reactor; 
 sending fresh nuclear fuel prepared for loading into the reactor to the 
reactor building. 
6.3.2 Fresh FA, CPS AR are delivered to NPP in packaging sets. 
6.3.3 FA are supp lied in transport packaging sets with capacity of two FA. 
FA can be complete with CPS AR. 
[PAGE 232]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
230 
6.3.4 CPS AR can be delivered to NPP separately from FA in packaging  sets 
for CPS AR with capacity of six bundles. 
6.3.5 The frequency of fresh fuel delivery to NPP is determine d by the 
operating organization (NPP administration) given the NPP demand in fuel of the 
required enrichment and quantity. 
6.3.6 When performing transport and handling operations with fuel in the 
FFSF, the following conditions are met to monitor the movement and  location of 
fresh FA and CPS AR: 
 all transport and handling operations with fuel in the FFSF are regulated 
by the program and working schedule of FA movement, which are prepared in 
accordance with the core loading maps, casks, FP racks; 
 each separate transport and handling operation related to the movement of 
fresh FA and CPS AR is recorded in the working schedule by persons monitoring the 
movement of FA and CPS AR; 
 all works on the movement of fresh FA are performed in the FFSF under 
the monitoring of the  supervising physicist (or supervisor for the movement of 
nuclear fuel outside the reactor) acting in accordance with the “Regulation on 
supervising physicist” and the “Regulation on the supervisor for the movement of 
nuclear fuel outside the reactor”; 
 responsible managers of FA, CPS AR movement works at NPP are 
determined, responsible fuel keepers at NPP are appointed by order of the Director. 
6.3.7 The design capacity of the common -plant storage of new fuel is 
established based on the requirements to ensure the  fulfillment of the following 
conditions: 
- the storage facility has equipment necessary for FA placement for refueling 
of two reactors with 20% margin at 12 -month fuel cycle. The number of cells in the 
equipment for FA placement is (42 2) + (42 2x0.2) = 100 .8 pcs., based on the 
required need for 42 pcs. of reloaded FA; 
- in the storage facility there is a place for arrangement of packaging sets 
with FA necessary for complete loading of the reactor with 10% margin - 163+163 
0.1 = 179 pcs. with FA into 90 packaging sets; 
- equipment for placing sealed casks in the amount of 10% of the number of 
FA of the core of one reactor - at least 163*0.1 = 16 pcs. of sealed casks, which is 
confirmed by the experience of NPP operation with VVER; 
6.3.8 Fresh FA storage standards: 
- fresh FA are placed in 90 packaging sets (capacity of one PS is two FA, 
distance between FA axes is 550 mm) in groups, no more than 16 packages in a 
group, distance between groups is not less than 2.5 meters; 
- in racks, fresh FA are placed with a spacing of 300 mm along the triangular 
grid, the clear distance between racks is at least 1 m; 
- in casks, fresh FA are placed with a spacing of 400 mm along the triangular 
grid; 
[PAGE 233]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
231 
- clear distance between casks is at least 1 m. 
6.3.9 The FFSF is equipped with two cranes with a lif ting capacity of 50/5 
tons (in the transport corridor and the fresh fuel storage room) designed for fresh fuel 
refueling. Crane lifting capacity is selected based on weight of loaded transport cask. 
6.3.10 The total capacity of the fresh fuel storage facility is 314 FA (134 FA in 
two racks and 180 FA in 90 packaging sets) and 54 FA can also be placed in two 
transport casks. 
6.3.11 The maximum possible capacity of the transport cask (27 FA) was 
selected given the limitations on nuclear safety and the size of the containme nt lock 
to reduce the reactor refueling time. 
6.3.12 Handling of fresh (non -radiated) NF in the FFSF is provided by the 
following systems and components: 
 nuclear fuel storage and handling equipment; 
 ventilation system maintaining air temperature not lower than  
10 ºС above zero and relative humidity not higher than 80%. FFSF provides constant 
monitoring of air temperature and humidity. 
 radiation monitoring system in accordance with Rooppur NPP 
“Regulation for radiation monitoring”;  
 in terms of fire safety, implem entation of organizational and technical 
measures; 
 a security alarm system that prevents access to the FFSF premises of 
persons who do not have permission to work with fresh fuel; 
 operating and emergency lightning system. 
6.4 Movement of transport cask with FA from the FFSF to reactor building 
6.4.1 Only serviceable standard devices and mechanisms that have passed 
periodic examination, testing and final inspection before the operations shall be used 
when performing transport and handling operations to move the loaded transport cask 
with FA from the FFSF to the reactor building and the empty transport cask from the 
reactor building to the FFSF. 
6.4.2 When performing transport and handling operations, avoid: 
1)  ingress of foreign items into casks and FA; 
2)  transportation of loaded cask with FA above the safe height of 9 m; 
3)  cask overturning during transportation; 
4)  transportation of loads over loaded FA casks in the FFSF and reactor 
building. 
6.4.3 Transportation of the loaded transport cask with FA and the empty 
transport cask through the Rooppur NPP territory shall be performed on an in -plant 
platform moved by a road train.  
6.4.4 Load lifting cranes used during transport and handling operations have 
lapping speeds of movement and lifting (lowering). 
[PAGE 234]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
232 
6.4.5 Special structures of load -gripping devices and special grippers are 
used when performing lifting and transport operations, which prevent disengagement 
and fall of the transported cargo. 
6.4.6 When lifting the shipping cask, a shock absorber is installed on the 
transport portal site. 
6.4.7 The fo llowing systems and equipment shall be inspected and their 
readiness for operation shall be confirmed before starting works: 
1) special bridge electric crane with load lifting capacity of 50/5 t span  
15.5 m; 
2) special bridge electric crane with lifting capacity of 50/5 t span 10.5 m; 
3) tilter; 
4) FA rack; 
5) FA grip; 
6) grip for CPS AR; 
7) frame; 
8) sealed cask grip; 
9) transport cask; 
10) Cross-beam for covers; 
11) 50 t rail trolley; 
12) case for casks; 
13) a pulling device for a transport packaging set; 
14) fresh fuel storage facility transport lock equipment; 
15) road train (road tractor and heavy truck semitrailer); 
16) packaging set; 
17) readiness of personnel for incoming inspection and transport and 
handling operations is confirmed. 
6.5 Removal of aged spent nuclear fuel 
6.5.1 SFA held for at least three years in th e fuel pool are removed from the 
reactor building in a transport packaging set (TPS). The maximum design power 
value of residual power flux of one FA used in the 12 -month fuel cycle after three 
years of holding in the pool is 0.0031 MW. 
6.5.2 After completion of  operations for removal of aged fuel from the 
reactor building, spent fuel is unloaded from the reactor to the fuel pool and fuel is 
rearranged in the reactor. 
6.5.3 Spent nuclear fuel is held in the fuel pool to remove activity and 
residual heat from spent FA to the values permissible for their transportation.  
6.5.4 SNF is sent from the reactor building of the Unit in the following 
sequence: 
 horizontal cross-beam is delivered to the transport portal and is hung on 
the hook with l/c of 190 tons of the crane of the transport portal; 
[PAGE 235]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
233 
 empty TPS is delivered by road to the transport portal of the reactor 
building; 
 TPS for SNF is raised horizontally to the site of the transport portal of the 
reactor building using a horizontal cross-beam and installed on a lock trolley; 
 a protective sliding door gets opened; 
 the outer door of the transport lock gets opened; 
 lock trolley with TPS enters the transport lock; 
 the outer door of the lock gets closed and the inner door gets opened; 
 the lock trolley enters the central hall of the reactor building; 
 the container gets engaged with vertical cross-beam; 
 The TPS is tilted to a vertical position using simultaneous horizontal 
movement of the lock trolley and lifting of the container by a circular crane; 
 TPS is removed from the trolley and t ransported to the equipment 
decontamination cavity; 
 with the help of a nut wrench and a rod, the container cover is 
decompressed, removed and installed in a temporary storage place; 
 TPS is transported to FP container compartment and installed on a multi -
purpose socket; 
 vertical cross -beam is disengaged from TPS and transported to storage 
place; 
 SFA intended for removal are removed from the fuel pool rack using a 
refueling machine and one after another are loaded into the TPS; 
 the container is closed with a cover using a rod; 
 The TPS is lifted from the container compartment above the shock 
absorber installed under the multi -purpose seat by means of the vertical cross -beam 
while the water is drained from the container internal cavity; 
 TPS is transported to the  equipment decontamination cavity, where it is 
sealed, decontaminated and held to stable parameters; 
 The TPS is transported to the lock trolley using a vertical cross -beam 
hung on the yoke of the circular crane; 
 TPS is set to a horizontal position with the  help of simultaneous 
movement of the trolley and lowering of the crane yoke; 
 lock trolley with TPS via transport lock leaves the reactor hall to the site 
of transport portal to the area of portal crane operation. Trolley leaving the TPS from 
the central hall is performed in the order opposite to the entering; 
 TPS is installed in shock absorber lower part by horizontal cross -beam 
using portal crane; 
 shock absorber upper part is installed on shock absorber lower part by 
horizontal cross-beam and is fixed; 
 The TPS together with the shock absorber is lowered to under the 
platform of the transport portal using a horizontal cross-beam; 
[PAGE 236]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
234 
 shock absorber is removed from TPS; 
 TPS is installed on the trailer of the road train and transported outside the 
NPP. 
6.5.5 All TPS with aged spent FA are loaded and removed in the same way. 
6.6 Refueling of nuclear fuel in the reactor core 
6.6.1 Operations on refueling of nuclear fuel in the reactor core provide for 
replacement of spent fuel assemblies and CPS AR with fresh ones, as well as 
rearrangement of FA and CPS AR rods inside the core. 
6.6.2 The reactor refueling is performed using a refueling machine under a 
protective layer of water in accordance with a special map. 
6.6.3 Reactor refueling procedure: 
1) Spent FA is removed from reactor core by refueling  machine. After the 
FA is lifted to transport position by the fuel cladding integrity monitoring system on 
the shut down reactor in the refueling machine operating rod (RM FCIMS) over a 
pre-selected FP or reactor cell, operations shall be performed to obta in preliminary 
data on the tightness of FA fuel elements in order to subsequently check the detected 
FA with leaky fuel elements in the casks of defective fuel assembly detection system 
(FADS); 
2) After leak test, FA is removed from the FADS cask and, depending on the 
test results, is installed either in the rack cell or in the sealed cask; 
3) Sealed casks are delivered from the FFSF to the reactor building and 
installed in the fuel pool until the first reactor refueling. Unsealed FA that have 
reached the failure criterion are stored in sealed casks during the Unit service life; 
4) Operations on replacement of CPS AR rods are performed similarly to FA 
replacement operations, except for CPS AR leak test operation; 
5) CPS AR are removed from the reactor building in the CPS AR container; 
6) The refueling machine simultaneously performs operations with only one 
FA or with one CPS AR, or with FA complete with CPS AR. 
6.7 Reactor loading with fresh fuel 
6.7.1 Fresh nuclear fuel prepared for loading into the reactor in the fresh fuel 
storage facility and installed in the transport cask is supplied to the reactor building in 
the following order: 
 fresh FA (CPS AR) loaded into the transport cask are delivered on the 
trailer of the road train for transportation of the transport cask to the trans port portal 
of the reactor building; 
 components for fastening the cask on the trailer are removed; 
 shock absorber is put on the cask; 
 the cask together with the shock absorber with the help of the transport 
portal crane is lifted to the transport portal si te (to the elevation plus 26,300 m). The 
total lifting height of the cask is 26,800 m; 
[PAGE 237]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
235 
 the shock absorber is removed from the cask using the cross -beam of the 
vertical transport portal; 
 cask is installed on lock trolley; 
 the safety door of the transport lock vestibule gets opened; 
 the external door of the transport lock of the reactor building gets opened; 
 lock trolley with cask moves inside that transport lock; 
 the external lock door gets closed and the internal door gets opened; 
 the lock trolley enters the central hall of the reactor building; 
 the cask is transported by a vertical cross -beam by an electric circular 
bridge crane to the container compartment of the fuel pool and installed in a multi -
purpose socket, under which a shock absorber is mounted; 
 fresh FA or CPS AR are loaded from the cask into the fuel pool rack or 
installed immediately into the reactor. 
6.7.2 Operations for new fuel loading, spent fuel unloading and fuel 
rearrangement inside the core are performed in accordance with the nuclear fuel 
refueling map, working program and working schedule under the constant monitoring 
by the supervising physicist. 
6.7.3 Operations are performed using the refueling machine (MP) in the 
following sequence:  
 bring the RM to the specified coordinate of FA removed from th e reactor 
core, make sure that the RM reaches the specified coordinate exactly; 
 check compliance of FA marking with the working schedule and loading 
map; 
 engage the RM rod with the FA head; 
 transport FA by RM to transport position in the FP, reach the spec ified 
coordinate of FP rack cell, in which the removed FA shall be installed;  
 check the accuracy of reaching the specified coordinate and lower FA into 
FP rack cell; 
 disengage from FA by RM rod; 
 lift the operating rod of RM and use the television camera t o make sure 
that there is no FA on the rod. 
6.7.4 Rearrangement of CPS AR in the reactor and unloading of CPS AR 
from the reactor to the FP shall be performed by CPS AR grip according to the RM 
operation instruction, the working schedule and the reactor refueling map. 
6.7.5 After complete loading of the reactor core, it is necessary to check the 
location of FA heads by height and inspect the location of FA heads in plan view. FA 
identification for compliance with the refueling program is performed using the 
television camera located on the refueling machine by marking on FA. 
6.8 At-reactor storage of SNF 
6.8.1 The SNF storage system is designed to reduce SFA activity and 
residual power flux to permissible values for transportation. 
[PAGE 238]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
236 
6.8.2 Functions of the SNF at-reactor storage system: 
 location of SNF unloaded from the reactor during refueling; 
 location of emergency unloading of core fuel; 
 holding (storage) of spent fuel; 
 residual heat removal from SNF; 
 providing biological protection of personnel against fuel stored in the fuel 
pool. 
6.8.3 Depending on the test results, SFA can be installed either in FP rack 
cell or in a sealed cask, or in the FA test and repair rack. 
6.8.4 Spent CPS AR unloaded from the reactor are installed in spent FA in 
the FP rack, or in the container for their export to SRWS. 
6.8.5 The fencing structures of the fuel pool (FP) are designed to retain active 
fission products emitted in various operation modes of the NPP, as well as to 
attenuate ionizing radiation. 
6.8.6 It is possible to cool the fuel pool water to remove residual heat from 
spent fuel assemblies installed in the fuel pool. 
6.8.7 During scheduled refueling and unloading of the entire core, the water 
temperature in the pool is maintained at no more than 600C (rated value is 450C).  
6.8.8 The pool is filled with an aqueous solution of boric acid with a 
concentration of at least 16 g/dm3 to ensure nuclear safety during fuel storage. 
6.8.9 The pool water serves to remove residual heat from spent FA. FP water 
circulates through the cooling system and the related fuel pool water purification 
system. FP makeup is provided to maintain the specified level of FP water (the same 
level during storage and refueling - elevation plus 25.450 m). 
6.8.10 All pipelines entering or leaving the FP fuel compartments are 
connected from the top of the pool so that their breaks do not lead to a decrease in the 
level below the level required in the fuel storage mode. 
6.8.11 Pressure pipelines passing under the water layer to the very bottom of 
the compartment are equipped with a device for passive breakdown of the bellows, 
which may occur when these pipelines break. These devices are hydraulic locks with 
a hole in the upper point connecting the hydraulic lock to the atmosphere of the 
containment. 
6.8.12 The reactor building fuel pool capacity is accepted based on the 
conditions of placement of s pent fuel assemblies (together with CPS AR) 
accumulated over 10 years of power generation and the possibility of unloading all 
reactor core assemblies into the pool at any time of operation. 
6.8.13 Sealed casks with spent leaking FA installed in them shall be sto red in 
FP racks until the Unit is taken out of operation. 
6.8.14 Design capacity of fuel pool racks at 12 -month fuel cycle is 420 + 163 
= 583 FA, including: 
 420 FA - replacement of 42 FA every 12 months accumulated over 10 
years of power generation; 
[PAGE 239]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
237 
 163 FA - emergency core unloading. 
6.8.15 Maximum (structurally obtained) capacity of compressed fuel storage 
racks is 756 cells, including: 
 cells for FA, 732 pcs.; 
 cells for sealed casks, 24 pcs. 
6.8.16 The upper elevation of the pool plus 26,300 m is determined by the 
reactor design and the value of the protective water level (about 3 meters) above the 
active part of the spent assembly when it is carried in the refueling channel. 
6.8.17 The fuel pool consists of one compartment designed directly for SFA 
storage and a container compartment - the loading area of the SFA transport container 
and unloading the transport cask with fresh FA. 
6.8.18 Container compartment is connected to fuel pool by refueling channel. 
Through the channel, fresh assemblies are reloaded from the cask to the reactor, spent 
aged FA are reloaded from the rack cells to the transport packaging set (TPS). 
6.8.19 The container compartment is equipped with a shock absorber and a 
multi-purpose socket for installation of a transport cask (for fresh fuel) and TPS (for 
spent fuel) in it. 
6.8.20 Allocation of TPS with spent fuel and transport cask with fresh fuel to a 
separate room (container compartment) eliminates the need to move the specified 
loads above fuel compartments. 
[PAGE 240]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
238 
7 Unit control in case of normal operation disturbances 
7.1 Defence in depth organization and technical measures 
7.1.1 Safety during NPP operation is based on the concept of defence in 
depth. Defence in depth is implemented using sequential physical barriers that 
prevent the spread of radioactive materials: fuel matrix, fuel shell, primary c ircuit 
boundaries, containment. Physical barriers, in turn, are protected by five levels of 
technical and organizational measures. 
Disturbances of normal operation of the Unit are prevented at level 1. This is 
also achieved by controlling “small deviations ” from normal operation using the 
“response to signal” procedures that determine the personnel actions when the alarm 
actuates at MCR panels in cases where the state of the Unit operating at power is 
stable. Personnel actions under the “response to signal”  procedures are intended to 
prevent disturbance in the operation of equipment or systems from developing into 
failures that require unloading of the Unit. 
Level 2 prevents design -basis accidents. This is achieved by control of Unit 
normal operation disturb ances in the “operation with deviations” state that lead to 
reactor power decrease, but without actuation of reactor emergency protection or 
safety systems, using the procedures included in the Unit Instruction for elimination 
of anticipated operational occurrences ( IMDBA). 
Beyond-design-basis accidents are prevented by safety systems at level 3. This 
is achieved by control of Unit normal operation disturbances: 
- in the “pre -accident situation” state caused by disturbance of  safe operation 
limits or conditions that lead to RP changeover to a safe state in accordance with the 
requirements of Section 7 of the technical specification; 
- in the “accident” state with the use of event -oriented procedures, which are 
part of the instructions for accidents mitigat ion (IAM), that determine personnel 
actions during the implementation of initiating events from the list of design -basis-
accidents with actuation of reactor emergency protection or safety systems. 
Severe beyond -design-basis accidents are prevented at Level  4. This is 
achieved by control of beyond -design-basis accidents using the procedures for 
monitoring and restoration of critical safety functions included in the beyond -design-
basis accidents management guideline (BDBAMG) using design-basis equipment not 
in design-basis modes, non-design-basis equipment. 
The consequences of core damage for personnel and the public are reduced at 
Level 5. This is achieved by control of severe beyond -design-basis accidents using 
the procedures included in the manual for management of severe beyond-design-basis 
accidents (MMSBDBA), as well as by the implementation of measures from 
personnel and population protection plans. 
7.1.2 The Unit monitoring and control system performs the following 
function of the “operator’s assistant” to pr ovide the operating personnel with the 
information required to make a decision on control actions: the safety parameters 
display system (SPDS) identifies disturbances of critical safety functions, presents the 
[PAGE 241]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
239 
necessary information for making decisions and  performing actions under the 
procedures included in the BDBAMG. 
7.1.3 The functional and group process control system (FGPC) of the Unit 
shall ensure the implementation of the main strategies and “standard action blocks” 
contained in the IMDBA, IAM and BDBAMG i n order to implement the control 
emergency response actions. 
7.1.4 NPP SS is a person directly responsible for the initial assessment of the 
event significant for the safety and reliability of the Rooppur NPP (hereinafter 
referred to as the event), including a p erson who makes a decision on the 
implementation of the “Preliminary action plan of personnel protection in case of 
accidents at the Rooppur NPP” in the absence of a director or its deputy. 
7.1.5 The RP operator (LERC) is entitled and shall stop the reactor 
independently in cases stipulated by the technical specification, as well as if further 
work threatens the NPP safety. 
7.1.6 In case of occurrence of conditions dangerous to life and health of 
people in separate rooms of the Unit, the USS shall organize evacuation o f personnel 
from these rooms and ensure that measures preventing access of persons to these 
rooms are taken by the personnel subordinate to it. 
7.1.7 NPP SS shall report all events in the Unit operation. Messages shall be 
made based on the lists of organizations  and employees depending on the nature of 
the event. 
7.1.8 Collection, processing, analysis, storage of information on failures of 
safety related system components and incorrect personnel actions shall be provided 
during operation at the Rooppur NPP. 
7.1.9 The events that occurred in the operation of the Rooppur NPP shall be 
investigated by commissions in accordance with the current regulatory documents. 
7.1.10 Prior to the formation of the commission to investigate the event in the 
NPP operation, the NPP administration shall  take measures to preserve the situation 
at the event site as it was during the event, stop all works on the systems 
(components) where the event occurred, if this does not pose a danger to human life 
and does not cause further development of the emergency situation. 
7.2 Personnel actions in case of deviations from normal operation 
7.2.1 The operating personnel actions to monitor the automatic control of the 
main process parameters, to signal the achievement of the upper limit values by 
monitored parameters, to determine and eliminate the cause of deviation from normal 
operation are an integral part of the normal operation conditions, the conditions to 
prevent the “small deviations” from normal operation of the main equipment from 
developing into disturbances of normal operation of the Unit, to prevent the actuation 
of protections initiating Unit unloading. 
7.2.2 Approximate list of “small deviations” from normal operation of the 
main equipment (design modes of category 1), which can occur with a frequency of 
more than 10-1 reactor·year: 
[PAGE 242]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
240 
- ALT actuation, shutdown of operating, actuation of standby equipment; 
- decrease of service water flow rate from PE system pumps; 
- decrease of service water flow rate to 11KAA10AC001 (12KAA20AC001) 
heat exchanger; 
- decrease of component cooling system water flow rate; 
- increase of component cooling system water activity; 
- temperature increase downstream the component cooling system heat 
exchanger; 
- balance between makeup and blowdown; 
- increase of cooling air temperature at CPS drives inlet; 
- level increase in SG emergency cooldown heat exchanger (process 
condenser); 
- level decrease in JND emergency boron injection system tank 1; 
- level increase in the LPH; 
- level increase in the HPH; 
- ground on DCB; 
- ground at 0.4 kV KRU; 
- RMS preventive alarm actuation; 
- actuation of generalized fault alarm in the RMS. 
7.2.3 Requirements for response-to-signal procedures. 
The “response to signal” procedures shall contain: 
- information on the signal (sensor identification, the nominal value of the 
parameter and the value of the alarm actuation setpoints when the parameter deviates 
from the nominal value, in which interlocks is involved, method and location of the 
alarm, availability and method of determining similar information to confirm the 
reliability of what is happening, etc.); 
- information on the causes that could lead to a disturbance of normal operation 
of equipment and on possible consequences; 
- instructions on the operating personnel actions to eliminate the causes that led 
to the disturbance of normal operation of the equipment. 
All information on the deviation signal in the equipment operation and 
personnel actions to find and eliminate the cause of deviation is given in a formalized 
graphic form on one or two sheets and on the respective ULCS video frames to 
minimize the volume of procedures. 
7.2.4 Requirements for the organization of works on the “response to signal” 
procedures. 
The need to perform works on the “response to signal” procedures is 
determined by the CE (DCE(o)) or NPP SS in cases where a deviation in the 
equipment operation occurred at night or on holidays, and when its prompt 
elimination is necessary. 
Actions under the “response to signal” procedure are not emergency response 
and shall be performed as planned. 
[PAGE 243]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
241 
The main purpose of the “response to signal” procedures is to inform the 
operating personnel about the deviation that occurred, its cause and possible 
consequences. 
7.3 Unit control in the “operation with deviations” state 
7.3.1 Operation with deviations from normal operation is permitted operation 
of the Unit at the regulated power level in case of failures or taking the equipment 
(components) out of service for repair listed in Table 7.1 for a certain period. 
Unit changeover to the regulated state, including to a new state after the 
expiration of the permissible time and non -elimination of the causes of failure, is 
performed in the normal process sequence (except for the operation mode of PRLD, 
PP-1, APP protections). 
7.3.2 The operating personnel actions to monitor the operation of process 
protections of the main equipment of the Unit, limiters (PRLD, PP), to monitor the 
unloading and stabilization of the Unit at the new permitted power level are 
conditions of accident -free operation and are performed in order to prevent the 
actuation of emergency protection or safety systems and deviations development into 
pre-emergency situations and accidents. 
7.3.3 The list of deviations in the Unit operation caused by failures or taking 
the systems equipment (components) out of service for repair, which may le ad to RP 
unloading, is given in Table 7.1.
