7.3.4 List of initiating events with failure conditions (category 2 design 
modes) that may occur with a frequency of mo re than 10 -2 reactor·year, which are 
part of the Unit Instruction for elimination of anticipated operational occurrences 
(IMDBA): 
- disturbance in feedwater system that leads to feedwater temperature decrease; 
- disturbance in the feedwater system that leads to feedwater flow rate increase; 
- spontaneous opening of steam generator safety valve (SG SV), BRU -A relief 
valve (11LBA10AA201, 11LBA20AA201, 12LBA30AA201, 12LBA40AA201) or 
BRU-K turbine bypass valve (10MAN11,12,21,22,31,32,41,42AA201) with their 
subsequent unfitting; 
- increase of steam flow to the turbine (due to faulty operation or failure of 
steam pressure controller) (instantaneous increase of the turbine load by 10% above 
the nominal one); 
- Decrease in steam flow rate to the turbine (due to faul ty operation or failure 
of steam pressure controller); 
- closing of turbine stop valves or loss of external electric load; 
- loss of normal feedwater flow rate (except for feedwater pipeline break); 
- false closing of fast-acting shut-off valve (FASIV); 
- loss of vacuum in the condenser or other cases that lead to turbine shutdown; 
- loss of non-emergency AC power supply of auxiliary station equipment (NPP 
blackout); 
- disconnection of different number of RCPS; 
- modes of emergency frequency deviation in the mains; 
- uncontrolled extraction of CPS CR group at MCPL and at power; 
- operator error when suppressing xenon oscillations (CPS CR movement that 
causes the maximum possible power density field deformation) 
- incorrect loading and operation of FA in this position; 
- inadvertent dilution of boric acid in the primary circuit coolant; 
- CPS CR mismatch; 
- disturbance in the volume and chemical control system that leads to an 
increase in the primary circuit coolant inventory; 
- false injection into the pressu rizer from the volume and chemical control 
system; 
- breaks of I&CD lines or other lines containing primary circuit coolant outside 
the containment; 
- disturbance in heat removal from under the cladding; 
- damage to the fuel pool cooling system; 
- medium leak through equipment seals; 
- leak or damage of systems containing liquid radioactive media; 
- leak of medium from the container containing radioactive substances; 
- false actuation of accident management algorithm for primary -to-secondary 
leak; 
- false injection into pressurizer from RCPS head; 
[PAGE 263]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
261 
- spontaneous actuation of ECCS accumulator; 
- SG ECS false actuation; 
- PHRS false actuation; 
- CEDP switching-off; 
- HPH switching-off; 
- EWP switching-off; 
- false actuation of emergency boron injection system; 
- Uncontrolled withdrawal of the CPS CR group at a certain power level 
(assuming the most unfavorable reactivity conditions in the core and primary circuit), 
which causes the most severe consequences (initial power level between low power 
and full power); 
- sudden changeover to primary circuit makeup with water temperature of 60 
оС above zero 
- small leaks from the primary circuit compensated by the KBA makeup 
system. 
7.3.5 Requirements for the procedures included in the IMDBA [33]. 
1)    Initiating events of cat egory 2 design modes are considered in the 
instruction. 
2)  Each of the sections of the instruction is a separate procedure drawn up 
for a specific event. 
3)  The section provides a brief description of the considered event, signs of 
Unit state, automation actions, personnel actions. 
4)  The algorithm of personnel actions is given in step-by-step form. 
5)    Step -by-step personnel actions shall be based on the signs of the Unit 
state: 
- process parameters; 
- indication of alarm actuation and indication of equipment state. 
6)     The steps of personnel actions consist of monitoring the operation of 
automation, and in case of automation failure, performing the respective switchings, 
diagnosing the state of the Unit and RP changeover to a stable safe state. 
7.3.6 Computerized procedures shall meet the following general 
requirements: 
- for each step in the respective video format, the operator is provided with 
the information necessary for making a decision and access to the control necessary 
for performing the task formulated in the name of the step;  
- the video format of the procedure step contains only the information on the 
state of the unit, which is necessary to perform the current action; 
- parameters and state of the Unit presented as part of the procedure shal l be 
updated; 
- provide the operator with recommendations on the implementation of one of 
the possible alternative actions based on the assessment of information on the state of 
Unit equipment and systems; 
[PAGE 264]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
262 
- ensure verification of the operator’s decisions while maintaining the final 
control and the right to decide whether to continue the actions or not; 
- automatic navigation over a specific procedure (overcoming the shortcomings 
related to the page-by-page arrangement of traditional procedures on paper). 
7.3.7 Requirements to the organization of works under IMDBA [33] 
procedures: 
1)  the operating personnel shall determine the cause of the disturbance in 
the Unit operation by preventive and emergency alarm, by text information on the 
action of protections, which is displayed on the operational display automatically 
when the root cause signal is generated, by the message of MCS that performs the 
functions of “operator’s assistant”; 
2)  act under the relevant section of the instruction. At the instruction of 
USS, LERC and LETC perform the respective diagnostic or control actions, or give 
commands for switching at the equipment location or from local control boards. 
7.4 Unit control in “pre-accident situation” and “accident” 
7.4.1 The Unit is in the “pre-accident situation” state if: 
- any SOL for process parameters from Section 3.1.1 or parameter values for 
WC standards from Appendix D is disturbed, but no accident signs are detected; 
- any OL from Table 3.8 is disturbed (the permissible time for elimination of 
OL disturbance is exceeded). 
In these cases, the operating personnel shall stop (check the shutdown) the RP 
and change over the Unit to a safe state in accordance with the requirements of 
Section 7 of the technical specification. 
7.4.2 The operating personnel actions to monitor  the actuation of emergency 
protection and safety systems, to monitor the state of critical safety functions, 
personnel control actions to eliminate design -basis accidents, to manage beyond -
design-basis accidents are performed in order not to exceed the limits of fuel damage, 
to preserve the integrity of physical barriers. 
7.4.3 List of design-basis accidents (category 3 design modes) that can occur 
with frequency from 10 -2 to 10 -4 reactor/year, which are part of the instruction for 
accidents mitigation (IAM): 
- spectrum of steam pipeline breaks inside and outside the containment; 
- SG feedwater pipeline break; 
- spontaneous opening of pressurizer safety valve with subsequent unfitting; 
- small leaks with primary circuit coolant loss as a result of primary circuit  
pipelines break (Dn < 100 mm) uncompensated by the KBA makeup system; 
- break of the heat exchange tube of the steam generator with subsequent 
cooldown at a rate of 60 ºС/h; 
- compensated leak inside the containment; 
- accidents with loss of primary circuit coolant from the reactor during 
shutdown at unsealed reactor and under refueling conditions; 
[PAGE 265]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
263 
- leak in the fuel pool or pipeline break that lead to water level decrease in the 
pool. 
7.4.4 List of design-basis accidents (category 4 design modes), probability of 
occurrence of which is from 10 -4 to 10-6 reactor/year, included in th e instruction for 
accidents mitigation (IAM) 
- instantaneous jamming or break of shaft of one reactor coolant pump set; 
- ejection of control and protection system control rods in case of drive 
housing break; 
- connection of non-operating loop without preliminary power reduction; 
- large leaks of the primary circuit coolant as a result of break of the primary 
circuit pipelines with an equivalent diameter of more than 100 mm, including break 
of main circulation pipeline; 
- primary-to-secondary circuit leak w hen the steam generator header cover is 
detached; 
- drop of individual FA, casks, housings with FA during transport and 
handling operations; 
- falling of items that can change the location and disturb the integrity of FA 
and FE claddings (including into the reactor and fuel pool); 
- hangup of spent FA in the process of handling works; 
- failures of equipment in the set of nuclear fuel storage and handling systems 
including complete power supply interruption; 
- decrease of homogeneous absorber concentration in fuel pool water; 
- failure of packages attachment during nuclear fuel transportation; 
- falling of transport container with spent FA; 
- leak of pipelines in systems for transportation, storage and processing of 
radioactive waste containing radioactive gas. 
7.4.5 Requirements for the IAM procedures. 
7.4.5.1 The  IMDBA may comprise both event -oriented procedures for the 
mitigation of design -basis accidents ( IMDBA) and symptom -oriented procedures ( 
IMDBA), or both. 
7.4.5.2 The  IMDBA procedures are identical in form to the IMDB A 
procedures. 
7.4.5.3 Each event procedure included in the IMDBA has the name of the 
initiating event of the emergency mode, for the management of which the respective 
personnel actions are defined in the procedure. The number of procedures 
corresponds to the number of initiating events. 
7.4.5.4 The “event -oriented” and “symptom -oriented” terms refer to the 
principle of organizing emergency response control actions to mitigate accidents. 
7.4.5.5 A feature of the event approach is the organization of accident 
management based on the following assumptions: 
- automation devices operation complies with the design algorithm; 
- operating personnel unambiguously determine the initiating event, which is 
the cause of the accident; 
[PAGE 266]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
264 
- initiating event is one of a certain set of expected event s (list of design-basis 
accidents for the Unit); 
- operating personnel works according to the instruction that defines their 
actions for this particular emergency scenario. 
7.4.5.6 Disadvantages of event procedures: 
- there is no step-by-step algorithmic procedure that determines the personnel 
actions to diagnose the state of the Unit, to determine the initiating event that caused 
the accident, to select the necessary procedure for accident management; 
- all possible variants of accident scenarios with all possible  combinations of 
equipment failures are not taken into account; 
- focus the operator’s attention on specific parameters and control means 
related to a specific event, and do not direct the operator to a periodic assessment of 
the general state of the Unit; 
- priority of event procedures in case of overlay of initiating events is not 
determined (for example: what actions are performed first in case of primary circuit 
leak and secondary circuit leak); 
- each event procedure is an independent document. 
7.4.5.7 Operating personnel is instructed to determine the root cause of the 
initiating event and apply the respective event-oriented procedure from the IAMeo. 
7.4.5.8 If the IAM consists of two parts IAMeo and IAMso, the IAMeo is 
used first and the IAMso is used under the following conditions: 
- operating personnel could not determine the initiating event, could not 
determine which of the event procedures shall be used to manage the accident; 
- overlay of initiating events occurred and operating personnel cannot 
determine which of the event procedures shall be applied first; 
- application of event procedures does not lead to the expected result. 
7.4.5.9 Symptom-oriented procedures are interconnected and together form 
a single system arranged by a branching structure. Work with IAMso begi ns after EP 
actuation or safety systems actuation by entering the A -0 procedure. This procedure 
comprises monitoring the operation of automation and diagnosing the Unit state. The 
A-0 procedure contains instructions on the operator’s actions in case of acc idents 
with equipment failures in case of tight primary and secondary circuits, including the 
response to EP actuation, loss of all AC sources and cooldown conditions during 
natural circulation, as well as entry into the procedures of three other categories. 
The Category 1 procedure group comprises procedures designed for primary 
circuit leak accidents and based on relevant symptoms. Procedures of this category 
contain instructions on primary circuit cooldown and pressure reduction in it after 
primary circu it leak occurrence, on reduction and disconnection of primary circuit 
emergency makeup, changeover to long-term cooldown. 
The Category 2 procedure group covers the procedures related to the primary-
to-secondary circuit coolant loss, including leaks from se veral steam generators. 
These procedures contain instructions on isolation of damaged steam generators. 
[PAGE 267]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
265 
Category 3 comprises procedures related to primary -to-secondary leaks, 
including leaks in several steam generators or primary -to-secondary circuit leaks  in 
combination with primary or secondary circuit leaks. These procedures contain 
instructions on cooldown of the primary circuit and pressure reduction in it after 
primary-to-secondary leak, on reduction and disconnection of emergency makeup of 
the primary circuit. 
There are links between procedures that are transitioned under certain 
conditions. 
Within the framework of each symptom -oriented procedure, constant 
diagnostics of certain parameters of the Unit, as well as additional diagnostics of the 
state of the Unit with the changeover to another procedure, if the previous assessment 
of the situation was incorrect or an accident developed, are assumed. 
If there is an overlap of accidents and failures of equipment and systems, then 
the structure of procedures  and the structure of connections between them determine 
priorities in control actions. 
7.4.6 Rules for construction of emergency response procedures included in 
the IAM 
7.4.6.1 The emergency response procedure is a duly executed document 
containing instructions for seq uential, step -by-step performance of certain control 
actions. Accordingly, accident management is considered as sequential achievement 
of certain goals (sequential step -by-step solution of tasks) with a common ultimate 
goal of achieving a safe, controlled state of the Unit. 
7.4.6.2 The goal achieved at each step (task to be solved) is formulated in 
the step name and achieved by implementing a certain strategy or standard action 
block under certain conditions by standard diagnostic actions. 
7.4.6.3 Accident management is se quential implementation of certain 
strategies, “standard action block” with monitoring of: 
- conditions at the beginning of fulfillment and criteria for decision-making; 
- success of execution. 
7.4.6.4 Examples of “standard action blocks” are: 
- actions after EP a ctuation (CPS CR fall monitoring, anti -distillate 
measures); 
- actions after TG shutdown; 
- actions to create the minimum permissible concentration or standby 
concentration of boric acid in the primary circuit; 
- actions on search and isolation of damaged SG; 
- actions to fill SG by AFWP; 
- actions to control and maintain the NC; 
- actions to stabilize RP parameters; 
- actions to maintain RP parameters during cooldown - Nsg, Nprz, ΔTprz, 
ΔTsg; 
- RP cooldown actions using RCPS; 
- actions on RP cooldown in the mode of planned cooldown by JNA system; 
[PAGE 268]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
266 
- actions on RP cooldown in the mode of emergency cooldown by JNA 
system; 
- actions on RP cooldown through steam generator using passive heat removal 
system (PHRS); 
- actions for RP cooldown through the steam gener ator from emergency 
cooldown; 
- actions for putting the blowdown makeup system into operation. 
7.4.6.5 Some of the possible strategies are: 
- primary circuit borating; 
- primary circuit pressure reduction; 
- “discharge-makeup” over the primary circuit; 
- heat removal from the primary circuit to the final absorber; 
- heat removal from the primary circuit through steam generators using 
passive heat removal system (JNB50); 
- heat removal from the primary circuit through steam generators using SG 
emergency cooldown system (JNB10); 
- heat removal from the primary circuit through steam generators with steam 
discharge to atmosphere through BRU -A (11LBA10AA201, 11LBA20AA201, 
12LBA30AA201, 12LBA40AA201); 
- maintenance of primary circuit coolant inventory in SG; 
- passive makeup of SG with water from deaerators and turbine hall pipelines; 
- secondary circuit overpressure protection; 
- maintaining the primary circuit coolant inventory in the reactor; 
- protection of the primary circuit against overpressure and brittle destruction; 
- heat removal from the fuel pool; 
- limitation of pressure rise in the containment; 
- SG isolation in case of primary-to-secondary circuit leak; 
- removal of hydrogen from the containment. 
The strategies of personnel control actions do not significant ly depend on the 
initiating event and the previous course of the accident development and are 
determined by the state of the RP and the main equipment of the Unit. 
There are a limited number of options using different combinations of means 
provided by the NPP design to implement each personnel action strategy. 
7.4.6.6 “Standard action blocks”, actions to implement any strategy, 
diagnostic actions in different procedures shall not differ. These are bricks from 
which procedures are built. 
7.4.6.7 The procedure shall also con tain a logical scheme to clearly 
understand the meaning of actions performed under steps. In the scheme, the steps are 
represented as a chain of squares interconnected by arrows. The task to be solved at 
this step is indicated in the square. 
In the logic s cheme, the arrows clearly indicate the transitions from one step 
to another. 
[PAGE 269]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
267 
If different outcomes are possible after any step, then conditions for its 
execution are specified for each. 
7.4.6.8 If the actions performed under one procedure were interrupted, a 
transition was made and actions were performed under another procedure, then 
interrupted actions of all group of standard steps or strategy implementation are 
performed when returning back to the first procedure. 
Interrupting the execution of actions under one procedure, changeover and 
starting the execution of actions under another procedure are determined by changing 
the situation at the Unit and the need to perform actions with higher priority goals. 
7.4.6.9 Level of description detailing of steps is defined by optim al 
combination of the following requirements: 
- it shall not take much time to read steps, that is, the description of actions 
shall be concise, easy to read and understand; 
- the description of actions shall be specified so as to exclude possible 
personnel error, that is, so that the personnel clearly understands what needs to be 
done. 
7.4.6.10  If, in order to perform an indication of any step, it is necessary to 
take into account the possibility of different progress of the emergency process and it 
is also necess ary to take into account the possible states of the equipment, then this 
step (high level step) is divided into the required number of sub -steps (detailed 
instructions) considering all possible options. 
7.4.6.11 Each instruction ends with either changeover to other  instructions, if 
necessary, or bringing the Unit to a safe state. 
7.4.6.12 An FGC program shall be developed for each “standard action 
block” and actions for the implementation of any strategy. 
7.4.6.13 It is desirable to implement the “standard action block” and any 
strategy not with individual control means of safety panels, but by start -up of the 
respective FGC program. 
7.4.7 Requirements for the organization of works under the IAM 
7.4.7.1 NPP SS is the operational manager for emergency response. 
After arriving at the MCR, the NPP SS shall perform the following as the 
operational manager for emergency response: 
- monitor the accident mitigation process; 
- monitor that the personnel acts in accordance with the IAM; 
- give instructions to the USS on the application of the respective IAM 
sections, and, if necessary, on the necessary additional actions; 
- make a decision on changeover to the CSF restoration instruction or 
continue performing requirements of IAM procedures in case of unsatisfactory state 
of any CSF; 
- stop the actions under the IAM in the availability of an extreme or severe 
state of the CSF and give orders to fulfill the requirements of the MMBDBA to 
restore the relevant CSF; 
[PAGE 270]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
268 
- continue to perform actions under IAM after recovery of CSE state, which 
was in extreme or serious state. 
7.4.7.2 USS is the operational head for emergency response in the absence 
of NPP SS at MCR. USS shall: 
- determine the cause of the accident and report to NPP SS; 
- supervise the actions of MCR and Unit personnel; 
- read out actions under the respective IA M section and monitor their 
implementation; 
- monitor the accident mitigation process. 
7.4.7.3 LERC and LETC shall follow the USS instructions, report to it on 
the actions performed. 
7.4.7.4 The RSSS shall monitor the CSF state in the absence of a shift 
technical adviser at the MCR, report to the USS on the need to use the respective 
IAM sections. 
7.4.7.5 A specialist from the list approved by the Chief Engineer, who will 
perform the functions of the shift technical adviser, shall be delivered to the MCR 
within 30-40 minutes from the moment of EP actuation. Upon arrival at the MCR, the 
shift technical advisor shall: 
1) monitor the CSF state; 
2) report to the operational manager on the need to apply the respective 
IAM sections; 
3)   monitor that the personnel acts in accordance with the IAM; 
4)   monitor the course of accident mitigation. 
7.5 Unit control in conditions of beyond-design-basis accidents 
7.5.1 In case of non -design-basis accident development, the operating 
personnel actions are determined by the “Beyond-design-basis accidents management 
guideline” (BDBAMG). 
7.5.2 Any technical means available in operable state intended for normal 
operation and for ensuring safety in case of design -basis accidents are used in order 
to manage the beyond-design-basis accident. 
7.5.3 It is necessary to strive to perform the following safety functions to 
prevent severe core damage during an accident: 
- reactor shutdown and its maintenance in sub-critical state; 
- removal of residual heat from the reactor core and provision of sufficient 
water inventory in the primary circuit; 
- retention of radioactive substances within the established limits. 
The criterion for the success of the operator’s actions may be the achievement 
at a given time of the required values of supplied water flow rate, the water level in 
the reactor, the temperature of the primary circuit coolant at the core outlet. If it is 
impossible to provide the required flow rate of cooling water, water supply to the 
core shall be provided with any available flow rate in order to slow down the process 
of its drainage and delay the transition to the moment when damage and destruction 
[PAGE 271]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
269 
of fuel elements begins. The time gain thus obtained shall be used for further attempts 
to restore systems capable of providing sufficient core cooling, as well as for 
arranging alternative sources of cooling water. 
7.5.4 If it was not possible to provide cooling of  the core and its damage 
occurred, then it is necessary to take measures to cool the damaged core in the reactor 
vessel and delay the moment of melting of the reactor vessel. In addition, it is 
necessary to take measures to reduce the pressure in the react or vessel. To achieve 
these objectives, it is necessary to use all available means to reduce pressure in the 
primary circuit and supply boric acid solution to the reactor and primary circuit. In 
this case, it is necessary to take measures to reduce the con sequences (steam 
explosion, thermal and hydraulic shocks, etc.) of the possible restoration of water 
supply to the reactor. 
7.5.5 List of BDBA (without fuel melting) included in the BDBAMG: 
- failure of all AC power sources for 24 hours and up to 72 hours; 
- stop of fuel pool cooling for 8 and 24 hours; 
- spectrum of breaks of steam pipelines inside and outside the containment up 
to the maximum diameter of the steam pipeline with break of one tube in the steam 
generator; 
- complete termination of feedwater supply; 
- accidents with primary circuit coolant loss in case of large leak with ECCS 
active part failure; 
- accidents with primary circuit coolant loss in case of small leaks with ECCS 
active part failure; 
- long-term (up to 24 h) termination of heat removal by  planned emergency 
cooldown systems with reactor cover removed and/or sealed reactor; 
- primary circuit coolant leak from the primary circuit to the secondary one in 
case of multiple destruction of SG tubes, or leakage through the primary circuit 
header of the steam generator with equivalent diameter Dn 100 mm; 
- accidents of ATWS type (with failure of emergency protection): 
a) loss of non-emergency AC power supply of auxiliary stationary equipment 
(NPP blackout); 
b) false closing of FASIV; 
c) uncontrolled removal of one or a group of controls at MCPL and at power; 
d) inadvertent dilution of boric acid in the primary circuit coolant; 
e) opening of SG safety valve, BRU -A relief valve (11LBA10AA201, 
11LBA20AA201, 12LBA30AA201, 12LBA40AA201) or BRU -K turbine by pass valve 
(10MAN11,12,21,22,31,32,41,42AA201) with their subsequent unfitting; 
f) loss of normal feedwater flow rate (except for feedwater pipeline break). 
7.5.6 Requirements for the procedures included in the BDBAMG. 
7.5.6.1 The implementation of the following main (c ritical) safety functions 
(CSF) is the condition for safety of protective barriers: 
- CSF-1 “Reactor core subcriticality”; 
- CSF-2 “Nuclear fuel cooling”; 
[PAGE 272]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
270 
- CSF-3 “Heat removal from the primary circuit to secondary one”; 
- CSF-4 “Primary circuit integrity”; 
- CSF-5 “Containment integrity”; 
- CSF-6 “Primary circuit coolant inventory”. 
7.5.6.2 The BDBAMG comprises CSF state trees, as well as CSF 
monitoring and restoration procedures. 
7.5.6.3 Knowledge of the previous emergency process that caused the CSF 
disturbance is not r equired. The general purpose of control actions under the 
BDBAMG is to restore the CSF at any BDBA. 
7.5.6.4 The structure of CSF state trees determines priorities and goals of the 
personnel control actions. 
7.5.7 The rules for constructing emergency procedures included in the 
BDBAMG are similar to the IAM. 
7.5.8 The requirements for the organization of work under the BDBAMG are 
similar to the IAM. 
7.5.9 Diversity (additional) protection is created as part of the CPS -ESFAS 
system to overcome common cause failures in the actuating par t of CPS-ESFAS due 
to the lack of diversity in the means and software. 
7.5.10 The technical means used in the development of the actuating part of 
the subsystem of diverse (additional) protection are based on the automation tools 
unit (ATU) to prevent common caus e failures (generality of the process platform, 
operating system, application software): 
1)  not using SW during operation (reception, processing and generation of 
protection commands); 
2)  using SW for implementation of process alarm tasks, self -diagnostics 
and interaction with other APCS systems, which differ from the means used in the 
actuating parts of the EP-ESFIP system. 
7.5.11 In addition to diversity (additional) protection, a signal on detection of 
failures in TXS SW is provided, which is aimed at reducin g the probability of 
deviation from normal operation without informing the operating personnel. 
7.5.12 The optimal way to overcome the consequences of a common cause 
failure of EP -ESFAS, as well as to fulfill the requirements for the reliability of EP 
and ESFAS f unctions for various design -basis initiating events, is to use alternative 
means of monitoring and control, and automatic subsystem of diverse (additional) 
protection for individual functions and subsequent actions of personnel. This 
subsystem shall provid e the Unit changeover to a controlled and safe state and shall 
be implemented on technical means based on the ATU and different from the means 
on which the EP-ESFIP subsystem is built. 
7.5.13 The subsystem of diverse (additional) protection ensures the fulfillment 
of the respective criteria for beyond -design-basis accidents in case of occurrence of 
some design initiating events of modes of Category 2, 3, 4 in combination with 
postulated common cause failure of EP -ESFAS due to alternative implementation of 
fundamental safety functions: 
[PAGE 273]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
271 
- reactor shutdown and its maintenance in sub-critical state; 
- heat removal from the reactor core; 
- isolation of radioactive fission products. 
7.5.14 Diverse (additional) protection, in case of postulated failure of the 
actuating part of t he EP -ESFAS subsystem, provides the implementation of the 
following basic safety functions in case of occurrence of design initiating events of 
Category 2, 3, 4 modes: 
- emergency shutdown of the reactor and its maintenance in sub-critical state; 
- emergency heat removal from the reactor; 
- retention of radioactive substances within the established limits. 
7.5.15 In view of the above, diversity (additional) protection provides: 
- CPS CR drop; 
- putting PHRS into operation; 
- isolation of containment and SG. 
7.5.16 The fo llowing is accepted in case of common cause failure of EP 
equipment and ESFAS start-up: 
- the common cause failure of the actuating part of the main CSyS is 
considered, which leads to the failure of emergency protection (EP) commands 
generation and automat ic start -up of safety systems, failure of safety system group 
start-up buttons, failure to present information and alarm generated in the scope of 
CSyS actuating part; 
- the design provides for the implementation of a part of the UU NOCS (APP, 
PP-1, P-2) functions on computerized automation equipment similar to those used in 
the actuating part of the main CSyS, therefore their failure is considered when 
substantiating the effectiveness of diverse (additional) protection; 
- common cause failure of the main C SyS actuating part is not accompanied 
by a change in the signals at the output of the CSyS actuating part and/or the 
generation of false signals; 
- is not considered simultaneously with the common cause failure of the CSyS 
actuating part and the failure of  the technical means of the ESFAS actuating part, 
which have control methods alternative to the CSyS actuating part, such as the 
opening/closing of the PRZ POSV and the SG POSV (11LBA10,20,30,40AA901, 
12LBA10,20,30,40AA902) by the spring, opening of the PH RS air gates when they 
are de-energized, etc.; 
- failure of EP -ESFIP actuating part does not affect individual control of 
safety system valves and mechanisms, and presentation of information on the state of 
valves and mechanisms; 
- failure of EP -ESFIP actu ating part does not affect presentation of analog 
information and signaling, which is not generated in the scope of EP-ESFIP actuating 
part, information from the ESFAS actuating part on position of control objects and 
information from ICIS and ULCS is available; 
- operating personnel actions may be taken into account at design 
substantiation of diverse (additional) protection 30 min after accident identification. 
[PAGE 274]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001

272 
Accounting for actions at an earlier stage is possible when performing an appropriate 
substantiation. 
7.5.17 Design substantiation of diverse (additional) protection and efficiency 
of personnel actions is performed sequentially for design -basis events of Categories 
2, 3 and 4 with overlay of CSyS actuating part common cause failure. The CCF 
overlay on the design initiating event is considered as a beyond-design-basis accident 
in accordance with its definition from the OPB-88/97. 
7.5.18 Diverse (additional) protection is created in the form of two sets of the 
same type located in the CSyS channels. Each subsystem s et consists of three 
measuring and logical channels that collect and logically process the signals of 
primary measuring transducers and generate commands, and that are implemented to 
ensure the principle of diversity on non -programmable means. The design p rovides 
for 3 cabinets of diverse (additional) protection. Each is an independent channel of 
diversity (additional) protection. 
7.5.19 The need for two sets of diverse (additional) protection is due to: 
- the need to control safety systems equipment; 
- ensuring i mplementation of functions of diverse (additional) protection 
during repair or testing of the second set; 
- necessity to put into operation at least 3 PHRS, which are arranged in pairs 
in two CSyS channels. 
7.5.20 The commands of diverse (additional) protection are equal to priority in 
relation to the tasks of shutdown of the EP reactor. In relation to safety system start -
up commands, the diverse (additional) protection commands have priority lower than 
the commands of the PP -ESFIP actuating part, but higher than the commands of NO 
PPI and RemC. There are no opposite commands that require priority in diversity 
(additional) protection. 
7.5.21 The CPS EES AC and DC “= 110 V” power supply is removed by 
additional switching devices to drop the CPS CR under the action of diver se 
(additional) protection. Switches with two trip solenoids are used. 
7.5.22 Signals to de -energize CPS drives shall be generated at the system 
output within 0.3 s after formation of the root cause of actuation regardless of its 
availability. Algorithms of start -up of equipment of process safety systems shall 
provide generation of memory of start -up commands before their execution and ban 
of operator’s intervention within 30 minutes for supply of opposite commands. 
Output signals, duplicating EP, from the equipme nt of the actuating part in the form 
of high level signals (220 V) are supplied to the power supply switches of CPS CR 
drives. 
7.5.23 In the process of automatic execution of actions according to the 
specified algorithm, the RP is changed over to a sub -critical s tate, residual heat 
removal and other necessary actions are performed. LERC cannot interfere with the 
operation of automation for 30 minutes (except for the possibility of sending remote 
control commands that duplicate the CSyS commands), but after this ti me the 
[PAGE 275]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001

operator has the opportunity to control the equipment in accordance with the 
instructions for mitigation of accidents (IAM, BDBAMG). 
7.6 Personnel actions in conditions of severe beyond-design-basis accidents 
7.6.1 The operating personnel actions to mitigate the consequences of severe 
beyond-design-basis accidents, to protect personnel and the population are 
determined by the “Manual for management of severe beyond -design-basis 
accidents” (MMSBDBA) and are a condition for preventing personnel and population 
overexposure above the design limits. Changeover from the BDBAMG to the 
MMSBDBA is performed if it is not possible to raise the reactor level at least to the 
upper generatrix of reactor nozzles (point 3) and temperature at the reactor core exit 
is MORE THAN 650 ºС above zero and continues to grow by 1JAA23JZ031, 
2JAA23JZ079, 1JAA33JZ099, 2JAA23JZ153 CLMS NFME ICDA indications. 
7.6.2 List of BDBA with severe core damage (SCD) during reactor power 
operation: 
- large leaks of the primary circuit (279<Dn≤850) with fail ure of boron 
solution supply to RCC from two HA 1 and failure of boron solution supply from 
three EPCS pumps; 
- large leaks of the primary circuit (150 <Dn≤850) with EPCS failure and 
failure of three HA 1 or two HA2; 
- large and small leaks from the primary circuit with non-isolation of nitrogen 
supply from one of four HA 1; 
- range of accidents with primary circuit coolant loss in case of break of 
primary circuit pipelines with a diameter up to Dn 850 with a complete loss of AC 
sources; 
- small leaks from the primary circuit with EPCS failure and failure of three 
or four HA 2; 
- small primary -to-secondary circuit leaks with non -isolation of the 
emergency SG from the environment with failure to perform BDBA control 
measures. 
7.6.3 List of BDBA with SCD in standby modes. 
Fall of the following items on the reactor vessel during THO related to reactor 
assembly and disassembly: 
- upper unit (UU) together with cross-beam; 
- protective pipe unit (PTU) together with PTU transportation platform and 
cross-beam; 
- PTU transportation platforms. 
7.6.4 List of BDBA during nuclear fuel storage and transportation: 
- falling of heavy objects into the fuel pool; 
- fall of an uncompressed container with spent nuclear fuel into the container 
compartment of the fuel pool; 
- uncompensated leak of fuel pool lining, including complete dehydration; 
- occurrence of a chain reaction for nuclear fuel storage and handling systems. 
[PAGE 276]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
274 
7.6.5 Requirements for procedures included in the MMSBDBA. 
7.6.5.1 In contrast to the procedures included in the IMDBA, BDBAMG, the 
MMSBDBA comprises procedures not mandatory for implementation, but only 
recommended for use. 
7.6.5.2 MMSBDBA comprises the following parts: 
- two procedures for MCR operating personnel (SAG -MCR-1 - for initial 
actions, SAG -MCR-2 - for actions after the accident manag ement group starts 
working); 
- diagnostic block diagram (eight procedures); 
- severe hazard tree (four procedures); 
- graphic calculation tools; 
- long-term control procedure; 
- procedure for taking the MMSBDBA out of operation. 
7.6.5.3 The diagnostic flow diagram is used to determine how controlled the 
NPP state is and to diagnose in advance possible hazards to fission product barriers. 
The diagnostic block diagram deals with equipment failures that led to severe 
accident and important control actions aimed at rec overy of failed equipment. 
Equipment inoperability is the main contributor to core damage. Therefore, measures 
to restore failed equipment are the most important element of severe accident 
management. 
7.6.5.4 The severe hazard tree is a means of identifying immedi ate and 
serious hazards to fission product barriers. The following mechanisms of containment 
depressurization are included in the severe hazard tree: hydrogen combustion, 
containment depressurization at high pressure, containment depressurization at 
negative pressure. In addition, any large total release of fission products is included in 
the severe hazard tree, even if it is caused by other mechanisms. Large emissions 
require immediate actions to protect personnel and population from airborne fission 
products. 
7.6.5.5 Possible severe accident management strategies: 
- supply water to the reactor vessel and primary circuit; 
- reduce primary circuit pressure by its depressurization; 
- perform injection into the reactor vessel; 
- restart RCPS; 
- reduce pressure in steam generators; 
- supply water to steam generators; 
- perform injection into the containment; 
- start cooling fans; 
- perform injection to under the second containment cladding; 
- containment inertization with steam. 
7.6.6 Requirements for the organization of work under the MMSBDBA. 
7.6.6.1 In accordance with NP -005-2005, the MMSBDBA uses the 
personnel responsible for preparing recommendations on emergency response to 
change over the emergency Unit to a controlled stable state, for developing an 
[PAGE 277]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
275 
accident management strateg y, ensuring the operability of the computerized 
automation system and means of communication of the internal and external 
emergency centers of the NPP. 
7.6.6.2 In the event of a severe accident, the MCR personnel shall perform 
initial actions in accordance with th e special MMSBDBA procedure (SAG -MCR-1). 
Then the accident management group (AMG) start working in a shielded control 
room. DCE or another specialist from the list approved by the NPP CE may be the 
AMG head. After notification of the start of AMG work, the  MCR personnel shall 
transfer the accident management to the AMG and proceed to the SAG -MCR-2 
instruction, while monitoring the parameters that characterize the NPP state. 
7.6.6.3 The AMG monitors the parameters of the severe hazard tree and the 
parameters of the diagnostic block diagram, makes a recommendation for the use of 
any strategies from the instructions of the diagnostic block diagram and the severe 
hazard tree. Specific actions are entrusted to the MCR operating personnel after the 
decision is approved on the recommendation of the AMG. 
7.6.6.4 The diagnostic flow diagram is the main means used by the AMG to 
determine a suitable strategy for managing a severe accident. The AMG analyzes the 
positive and negative consequences of implementing various severe accident 
management strategies and makes a recommendation on which of the possible 
strategies is most desirable. 
7.6.6.5 If the setpoint for the parameters of containment integrity severe 
hazard tree is reached, then any actions under the diagnostic block diagram are 
postponed and the strategy provided by the severe hazard tree immediately begins. 
7.6.6.6 The final part of the diagnostic block diagram checks whether it is 
possible to exit the MMSBDBA. 
7.6.6.7 If a controlled stable state is reached, the AMG makes 
recommendations on limitati ons and warnings for the long -term recovery process 
based on the procedure for taking the MMSBDBA out of operation.

9 Organization of operation 
9.1 General provisions 
9.1.1 The organizational activity of operating organization is to perform on 
its own or with the involvement of other organizations activities for the location, 
design, construction, operation and decommissioning of NPPs, as well as activities 
for the handling of nuclear materials and radioactive substances under under the 
licenses of the state supervisory authorities of the PRB (BAERA). 
9.1.2 The operating organization performs it s control functions at the site to 
ensure safe and reliable operation of Rooppur NPP. The operating organization has 
the powers, financial, material, intellectual, labor and legal resources sufficient to 
perform its functions. 
9.1.3 The operating organization is  fully responsible for the safety of the 
Rooppur NPP in accordance with the laws on nuclear safety of the People’s Republic 
of Bangladesh. 
9.1.4 The operating organization is responsible for: 
 distribution of responsibility and transfer of authority within the op erating 
organization; 
 creation and monitoring of successful implementation of control programs 
that meet the requirements of personnel training; 
 performance of quality assurance program at the Rooppur NPP. 
9.1.5 The structure of the operating organization is det ermined by its Charter 
on the basis of SAR. 
9.1.6 Organizational structure and responsibility, powers, duties and 
functional roles of all employees and subdivisions, as well as the procedure for their 
internal and external interaction shall be formed for the Rooppur NPP. 
9.1.7 Duties of the General Director as the head of the NPP owner 
organization - ensuring the safety and quality of Rooppur NPP at all stages of the life 
cycle. 
9.2 Responsibility of NPP administrative management 
9.2.1 The activities of the NPP administrative ma nagement are aimed at 
ensuring the safety and quality of the NPP operation and consist in managing the 
activities of structural subdivisions and organizing administrative monitoring over 
their activities. 
9.2.2 The administrative management of NPP comprises: 
 NPP Director; 
 area-specific Deputy Directors (Chief Engineer, Chief Inspector, Chief 
Accountant, Deputy Director for Economics and Finance, Deputy Director for 
Regime and Physical Protection, Deputy Director for Personnel Management, Deputy 
Director for Capit al Construction - Head of CCD, Deputy Director for General 
Issues). 
 Deputy Directors of NPP by the areas of production activity. 
[PAGE 282]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP 
Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
280 
 Heads of structural subdivisions subordinate to Deputy Directors for 
production activities. 
9.2.3 The Director shall be liable in acc ordance with its job description, 
including responsibility for: 
 ensuring nuclear, radiation, fire, technical and environmental safety and 
physical protection at all stages of the NPP life cycle, safe and reliable operation of 
equipment, buildings, structur es, devices of NPP control systems at the stages of 
arrangement, design, construction, putting into operation, operation, taking out of 
operation of a nuclear facility, as well as safe handling of nuclear materials and 
radioactive substances, radioactive and industrial waste at NPP; 
 production as well as financial and economic results of NPP activities; 
 arrangement of the NPP civil defense activities; 
 performance of work on prevention and elimination of consequences of 
emergency situations within the sanita ry protection area of the NPP, putting into 
effect and implementation of the action plan for the personnel protection in the event 
of an accident at the NPP; 
 NPP financial security; 
 ensuring NPP operation quality at all stages of the life cycle; 
 organization of work and creation of conditions for the protection of state 
secrets. 
9.2.4 Personnel directly subordinate to NPP Director: 
 Chief Engineer; 
 Deputy Director for Regime and Physical Protection; 
 Deputy Director for Personnel Management; 
 Deputy Director for Economics and Finance; 
 Chief Accountant; 
 Deputy Chief Accountant; 
 Deputy Director for Capital Construction - Head of Capital Construction 
Department; 
 Deputy Director for General Issues; 
 Chief Inspector; 
 Head of Mobilization Training, Civil Defense and Emergen cy Centers 
Department; 
 Head of the Legal Department. 
9.2.5 NPP structural subdivisions are subordinate to Deputy Directors in the 
areas of their activities (works). 
9.2.6 The Chief Engineer performs operational control of NPP through its 
deputies in areas of activity in accordance with the adopted structure of 
administrative and technical management of NPP. 
9.2.7 The Chief Engineer performs operational control of Rooppur NPP 
through its deputies by areas of activity. 
9.2.8 The following employees are subordinate to the Chief Engineer: 
[PAGE 283]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP 
Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
281 
 Deputy Chief Engineer for Operation; 
 Deputy Chief Engineer for APCS and EEE; 
 Deputy Chief Engineer for Repair; 
 Deputy Chief Engineer for Safety and Reliability; 
 Deputy Chief Engineer for Chemical Technologies and RAW Handling; 
 Deputy Chief Engineer for Engineering Support and Modernization: 
 Deputy Chief Engineer for Personnel Training - Head of PTC: 
9.2.9 The main task of the Chief Engineer is to ensure efficient production of 
electricity with unconditional observance of nuclear, radiation, environmental and  
industrial safety in the processes of electric power generation, operational control and 
maintenance of equipment, systems and facilities of Rooppur NPP, their inspections 
and tests, M&R, reconstruction, modernization and technical re-equipment. 
9.2.10 The Chief Engineer is responsible for: 
 failure to perform or improper performance of the duties assigned to it; 
 incomplete or improper use of the rights granted to it; 
 failure to comply with nuclear, radiation, fire, industrial safety, 
environmental protection, lab or protection in accordance with the applicable codes 
and standards in the field of atomic energy use of the People’s Republic of 
Bangladesh; 
 non-compliance of the general technical level of NPP operation with the 
requirements of legislative, regulatory and legal acts applied at NPP; 
 violation of the requirements of legislative, regulatory and legal acts, 
federal codes and standards in the field of atomic energy use of the People’s Republic 
of Bangladesh; 
 untimely fulfillment of the requirements, decisions,  prescriptions and other 
mandatory documents of the state administration, regulation and supervision of the 
PRB (BAERA) for NPP safety assurance; 
 failure to fulfill the plans of organizational and technical measures for 
production and technical activities of NPP; 
 failure to fulfill the dispatch schedules of load bearing; 
 failure to work with personnel of subordinate subdivisions in accordance 
with the requirements of the rules for organization of work with personnel; 
 failure to comply with orders and other guiding documents used at NPP; 
 failure to comply with labor protection rules and instructions, assigned 
labor protection duties; 
 failure to provide safe working conditions in the assigned areas of work 
and cases of industrial injuries, violation of labor l aws and other regulatory legal acts 
on labor protection; 
 repeated events and incorrect actions of personnel, deficiencies of 
organizational discipline; 
[PAGE 284]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP 
Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
282 
 improper organization of works on operation and prevention of deficiencies 
in management. 
9.2.11 The structural  subdivisions of NPP, headed by the heads of the 
subdivisions, are subordinate to Deputy Chief Engineers in the areas of their 
activities. 
9.2.12 The heads of NPP subdivisions have the powers, functional and general 
job duties, rights and responsibilities establi shed in their job descriptions to 
implement the tasks assigned to the structural subdivisions headed by them in 
accordance with the regulations on subdivisions. 
9.2.13 NPP subdivisions administrative management personnel directly in 
charge of NPP safe operation are responsible for: 
 failure to perform or improper performance of duties in accordance with 
the job description; 
 failure to comply with instructions, orders, directives at NPP, directives and 
tasks of higher management; 
 incomplete or improper use of the rights and obligations granted; 
 failure to comply with the activities of subordinate subdivisions with the 
requirements of the legislation, codes and standards governing these activities in the 
People’s Republic of Bangladesh; 
 violation of official duties by  it personally and personnel of subordinate 
subdivisions, internal regulations, regime requirements; 
 non-compliance with fire safety measures, fire safety obligations; 
 failure to comply with labor protection rules and instructions, assigned 
labor protection duties; 
 failure to provide safe working conditions in the assigned areas of work 
and cases of industrial injuries, violation of labor laws, other regulatory legal acts of 
the People’s Republic of Bangladesh on labor protection; 
 incorrect or untimely decision taken, violations of the organization of work 
of the NPP subdivision, threat to the safety of NPP and contracting organizations 
personnel; 
 incorrect or untimely decision, inadequate monitoring of the 
implementation of regulatory documents (acts, instr uctions) by subordinate 
subdivisions, the consequences of which may lead to a violation of the organization 
of work of NPP subdivisions, deterioration of the technical and economic indicators 
of NPP, threat to the safety of NPP employees and contracting organizations; 
 failure to comply with nuclear safety obligations; 
 poor-quality selection, untimely and poor -quality training and continuing 
training of personnel of subordinate subdivisions. 
9.3 Personnel responsibility 
[PAGE 285]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP 
Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
283 
9.3.1 The main operating organization subdivisio ns comprise specialized 
structural subdivisions. The structure of subdivisions, distribution of duties and tasks 
between subdivisions shall be approved by the operating organization head. 
9.3.2 The distribution of duties and responsibilities is contained in the 
Regulations on Rooppur NPP subdivisions, which describe the structures of 
subdivisions, and in the job descriptions of personnel, as well as in organizational and 
administrative documents. 
9.3.3 Operational control of NPP operation is directly performed by 
operating personnel, the shift of which comprises: 
 leading operating personnel in shift (NPP SS, USS); 
 MCR operating personnel; 
 operating personnel of subdivisions who serve production sections and 
perform operation switching in accordance with the duty schedule. 
9.3.4 Operation of the Unit equipment is performed by the personnel of 
subdivisions by assignment under the supervision of shift supervisors (SS) by 
permission (directive) of an employee in whose operational supervision (control) it is 
located. The general ma nagement of the NPP, the Unit operation is performed, 
respectively, by the nuclear power plant shift supervisor (NPP SS) and the shift 
supervisor of the unit (USS). 
9.3.5 The delimitation of functions, responsibilities for the maintenance of 
systems, equipment a nd premises, the procedure for operations, the frequency of 
monitoring parameters during the operation of individual systems and equipment in 
the process of maintaining the specified mode of Unit operation are determined by 
the relevant job descriptions, p roduction instructions and regulations of the Rooppur 
NPP. 
9.3.6 An order for any planned change in the Unit power, as well as for its 
start-up and shutdown, is given by the NPP SS after receiving the appropriate 
permission from the dispatching services. 
9.3.7 Operational control of common-station systems connected to the Unit is 
performed by the NPP SS. 
9.3.8 Communication with duty dispatchers of dispatching services is 
performed by the NPP SS. 
9.3.9 All switchings in the main electric connection diagram of Rooppur 
NPP, which ca n affect the operation mode of Units, are performed with the 
permission of NPP SS with mandatory prior notification of USS. 
Taking out of service for repair of electrical equipment of the main electric 
connection diagram of Rooppur NPP, which is included i n the List of equipment, 
RPA and EPA devices, LFC, dispatching and process control means is performed 
according to the Rooppur NPP request authorized by the dispatching department of 
the appropriate power system, or according to the request of the dispatch ing 
department of the power system agreed by the NPP Chief Engineer. 
9.3.10 The following shall be developed and approved at the Unit by the NPP 
CE: 
[PAGE 286]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP 
Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
284 
1) list of systems and equipment, switching on which is performed only under 
switching forms with mandatory indicatio n of the sequence of operations and safety 
measures; 
2) list of premises in case of fire in which the Unit shall be immediately shut 
down; 
3) list of locked, sealed premises, channels, tunnels; 
4) list of locked, sealed valves with indication of their position in v arious 
states of RP NO; 
5) list of closed, sealed cabinets. 
All equipment and premises shall be locked or sealed in accordance with the 
lists approved by NPP CE before the start of reactor bringing to the “reaching 
MCPL” state. 
9.3.11 The requirements for operabilit y checks of safety related systems 
(components) (SRS) are established in the “Regulations on checks and tests of 
systems and equipment of Rooppur NPP Unit 1” (RCT) and shall be fulfilled in all 
states of normal operation of the Unit. 
A schedule of checks a nd tests of the Unit SRS equipment shall be developed 
and approved by the NPP CE in accordance with the specified regulations (RCT).  
The schedule shall be located at the workplaces of NPP SS and USS. There 
shall be approved schedules for checks and tests of this equipment at the workplaces 
of personnel who operate certain types of equipment. 
9.3.12 Equipment PPI checks are performed with the permission of the 
operating personnel in charge of the equipment (NPP SS, USS, shops SS). Works on 
PPI check are performed by RS, TS, CS, TICS, ES, VS, RWHS, RSD shift personnel 
under the supervision of operating personnel who controls the equipment with results 
recording in the PPI check logbook and operational logbooks of SS shops. After 
check is complete: 
- protection and i nterlock equipment with devices for putting them into 
operation or for changing setpoints (or cabinets in which they are located), except for 
TM with continuous remote access control and recording devices, shall be sealed. It 
is allowed to remove seals onl y for the shop personnel who service this equipment, 
with the permission of NPP SS, to take the protections, interlocks out of operation or 
change the setpoints; 
- process protections of the Unit shall be put into operation. Devices for 
protections actuati on, if any, and setpoints change (or cabinets in which they are 
located), as well as devices included in protection, shall be closed and sealed; 
- putting the process protections into operation after installation or 
reconstruction shall be performed only by order of NPP CE. 
Operability check of equipment, process protections, interlocks and alarms 
shall be formalized under the established procedure at the MCR as the equipment and 
systems are put into operation, to standby. 
[PAGE 287]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP 
Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
285 
9.3.13 Rooppur NPP shall draw up and appr ove a schedule of workplaces 
walkdown by administrative management. The walkdown results shall be analyzed 
by the Rooppur NPP management. 
9.3.14 The heads of Rooppur NPP shops shall provide recording of data on 
operation modes of subordinate equipment (loading cy cles), data on the value of 
residual equipment life, test reports (including start -up and adjustment period), data 
on repair and modernization, certificates of applied materials. 
During operation, it is necessary to monitor the exhausted life of the equipment 
for which the strength and loading cycles were substantiated. Monitoring is 
performed by recording the actual number of modes, equipment parameters (pressure, 
levels, temperature, state of valves) with subsequent design analysis of damage and 
operating time by cycles according to the duly agreed method. Analysis and 
accounting of exhausted life shall be implemented on computer means with results 
documentation by the PTD and submission to organizations concerned annually. 
9.3.15 Rooms where safety system equipm ent is located shall be closed for 
access by non-operating personnel. 
9.3.16 In all Unit NO states, the operating personnel shall: 
monitor operation limits and conditions for systems and equipment;  
 monitor compliance with safe operation limits and conditions;  
 monitor the concentration of boric acid in the primary circuit, FP, safety 
system tanks, (HA ECCS of stages 1, 2) and maintain it in the range of permissible 
values;  
 monitor the implementation of measures to exclude the spontaneous supply 
of distillate water to the reactor, as well as to the FP with a boric acid concentration 
of less than 16 g/dm3;  
 monitor the quality of working media in the primary and secondary circuits;  
 check equipment and systems in accordance with schedules.  
9.3.17 Repair, maintenance (except for external inspection), checks and tests 
of equipment and systems, the state of which determines the conditions of safe 
operation of the Unit, shall be performed with the registration of a permit for these 
works in accordance with the procedure established at the Rooppur NPP. 
9.4 Requirements to the number and composition of personnel 
9.4.1 Safety culture shall formed and maintained by all employees and 
organizations that deal with placement, construction, operation and taking out of 
operation of N PP, design, engineering and manufacture of their systems and 
components. 
9.4.2 The operating organization shall ensure selection, preparation, 
admission to unsupervised work and maintenance of personnel qualification. 
9.4.3 Requirements for qualification, knowledge an d skills of employees of 
the operating organization shall be established in the regulations on subdivisions and 
job descriptions for various categories of employees. 
[PAGE 288]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP 
Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
286 
9.4.4 When establishing the requirements for personnel qualification, it shall 
be taken into account that: 
 when designing, constructing, commissioning and operating NPP, as well 
as manufacturing equipment, a complex technology is used, which is 
constantly being improved and changed; 
 ensuring NPP life at all stages of its life cycle is a complex organ izational 
problem; 
 in case of transient processes at NPP, as well as during the occurrence of a 
crisis situation, appropriate conclusions of specialists may be promptly 
required, which shall be provided by the relevant departments of the operating 
organization. 
9.4.5 It is necessary that the qualification, training and experience of all 
personnel of the operating organization correspond to their duties and work 
performed. 
9.4.6 The management of the operating organization and leading specialists 
shall have appropriate education and experience in practical work in subordinate or 
similar organizations in the field of their work. 
9.4.7 The management and leading specialists of the operating organization 
shall be licensed before admission to unsupervised work. 
9.4.8 Job descriptions sh all be developed for all personnel, specifically 
defining for each position: 
 rights and obligations; 
 tasks; 
 interaction within the organization and with third parties; 
 education requirements; 
 previous work experience requirements; 
 amount of knowledge; 
 procedure for testing knowledge and admission to unsupervised work, 
frequency of testing knowledge. 
9.4.9 Training programs shall be developed to ensure the required 
competence of the personnel when staffing the operating organization. Particular 
attention shall be paid to the training of managers and specialists involved in solving 
the issue of NPP safety and obliged to organize work to overcome crisis situations at 
NPP in case of accidents. 
9.4.10 The requirements for the number and composition of personnel for the 
Rooppur NPP Unit workplaces given the reserve personnel providing leave, 
temporary disability (sick leave), involvement in additional work to support 
operation, confirmation of qualifications (preparation and passing of exams, etc.) are 
indicated in Table 9.1.

9.5 Personnel interaction procedure 
9.5.1 Personnel interaction is based on the functional delineation of 
responsibilities of managers from the NPP administrative management by areas of 
activity in accordance with the Rooppur NPP operation management structure. 
9.5.2 The Rooppur NPP organizational structure is based on the principle of 
functional delineation of powers and responsibilities of NPP adm inistrative 
management and tasks performed between NPP structural subdivisions in the areas of 
their activities (works). 
9.5.3 Operation management activities shall provide for interaction of 
Rooppur NPP management, managing operating personnel and operating per sonnel 
of shifts, operation, repair and support services of NPP. 
9.5.4 Prompt operation comprises activities performed directly by operating 
personnel, managing operation personnel and in interaction of operating personnel 
with personnel of other NPP subdivisions. 
9.5.5 Interaction of personnel at the Rooppur NPP is performed both within 
the organization and with third-party organizations. 
9.5.6 The procedure of interaction and subordination of personnel in 
accordance with the approved organizational structure of Rooppur NPP  management 
shall be described in the personnel job descriptions and regulations on the 
subdivision. 
9.6 Organizational issues of operation in various states 
9.6.1 Organizational issues in the “shutdown for repair” state 
9.6.1.1 A schedule approved by the operating organiza tion and working 
programs for the work shall be drawn up in advance before planned preventive 
[PAGE 292]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP 
Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
290 
maintenance at the Unit. These programs shall be agreed under the procedure 
established at the Rooppur NPP. The complete monitoring of repair work 
performance shall be provided under the guidance of NPP CE. 
9.6.1.2 Personnel access to the containment shall be provided in accordance 
with the requirements of the “Instruction for personnel admission to containment for 
work, examination and inspection during Unit power operation”. 
9.6.1.3 Personnel admission for work on the decompressed primary circuit 
and reactor shall be performed in accordance with the procedure established at the 
Rooppur NPP with the implementation of measures to prevent foreign items from 
entering the decompressed primary circuit, reactor, RFP and FP. 
9.6.1.4 The open cavities of the primary circuit shall be reliably closed for 
the time of break in works. 
9.6.1.5 Before refueling the reactor, the main joint shall be decompressed 
and the reactor disassembled with the organization o f the repair area in accordance 
with the “clean area” policy. 
9.6.1.6 During reactor assembly and disassembly with the upper unit 
removed, measures shall be taken to prevent foreign items entering the reactor, 
namely: 
- it is prohibited to transport equipment above the reactor that is not involved in 
the process operations for reactor assembly and disassembly; 
- when transporting the reactor core barrel to and from the RVI pool, it is 
prohibited for the personnel to stay in the steam generators compartment and RCPS; 
- works on the housing flange and transportation of large -sized equipment 
above the reactor shall be performed with a standard process cover installed on the 
MRJ; 
- accounting of tools and devices involved in the reactor works shall be 
performed; 
- reliable fixing and absence of foreign items on large -sized equipment 
transported above the reactor shall be checked. 
9.6.1.7 The following level of representation of administrative, technical, 
operating and repair personnel is established for repair of the Unit equipm ent during 
the shutdown period: 
- the manufacturer and responsible work manager, shop-owner SS are involved 
in checking the operability of auxiliary equipment of the Unit (NPP) after the current, 
medium repairs or overhaul. 
Acceptance of auxiliary equipmen t after any type of repair is performed by a 
commission chaired by an engineering and technical employee appointed by the head 
(deputy head) of the shop by equipment belonging; 
- the work performer and responsible work manager, head (deputy head) of the 
shop-owner, shop -owner SS are involved in checking of FWP, RCPS, TG, safety 
systems, equipment of the main electric circuit after current, medium repairs or 
overhaul, as well as after unscheduled emergency repair, as well as in hydraulic tests 
of the primary circuit. 
[PAGE 293]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP 
Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
291 
Acceptance of the specified equipment from any type of repair is performed by 
a commission chaired by the shop manager (by belonging). 
9.6.2 Organizational issues in the “refueling” state 
9.6.2.1 Before the start of reactor refueling, the operating personnel a t the 
MCR and the CH workplace (refueling machine control panel) shall have all 
documentation related to refueling, including: working programs and schedule of 
refueling, maps of placement of fresh and spent FA, programs of FA movement in FP 
and RFP (if necessary), route maps of cargo movement in the CH (above reactor and 
FP) during refueling. 
Note - works on the first loading of the reactor core at the stages of the first approach of 
criticality shall be performed according to the program specially develop ed for this purpose “The 
first loading of the reactor core. Test program and procedure”. 
9.6.2.2 All works on the movement of fresh and spent fuel shall be 
performed according to the programs approved by the NPP CE. If necessary, the 
programs indicate additional safety measures not stipulated by this specification. 
9.6.2.3 All transport and handling operations during refueling of nuclear fuel 
shall be performed according to special instructions in compliance with the rules of 
nuclear, radiation safety and labor protection. 
For the production of transport and handling operations, it is allowed to use 
only serviceable standard devices and mechanisms that have passed periodic 
inspection and final inspection before the performance of operations. Load lifting 
devices used during  operations shall be inspected in accordance with the current 
rules. Lifting and transport devices designed for work with highly active equipment 
shall have serviceable monitoring devices for vertical and horizontal movement, as 
well as lifting and lowerin g loads; lifting and turning limiters of lifting devices shall 
be serviceable. Electric motors of transport and handling equipment mechanisms 
shall have reliable power supply with backup during transportation of spent FA. 
9.6.2.4 In accordance with the transport a nd handling diagram approved by 
the NPP CE. Movement of loads and equipment above the reactor and FP not 
involved in refueling is prohibited. 
9.6.3 Organizational issues in the “cold” state 
9.6.3.1 RP changeover from the “shutdown for repair” state to the “cold” 
state i s performed after the records are made by the heads of the equipment 
subdivision-owners, DCE (r), DCE (o) on the completion of repair works on the RP 
equipment, performance in full of checks during the PPM and in the “shutdown for 
repair” state and NPP CE permission to start operations to change over the RP to the 
“cold” state drawn up in the technical orders logbook of the Unit at the USS 
workplace (hereinafter referred to as the technical orders logbook of the Unit). 
Readiness for checking the tightness o f the primary circuit with a pressure of 
3.2 MPa and the secondary circuit with a pressure of 1.96 MPa is documented by the 
relevant reports and permits of the DCE (o) in the technical orders logbook of the 
Unit. 
[PAGE 294]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP 
Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
292 
9.6.3.2 The heads of equipment subdivision -owners s hall make records on 
changes in the circuits and design of equipment adopted under the established 
procedure in the technical orders logbook of the Unit. Operation documentation at 
operating personnel workplaces shall be corrected in accordance with these changes 
and the operating personnel shall be familiar with them. 
9.6.3.3 Admission of personnel to perform work on elimination of defects, 
performance of inspections, taking the equipment out of service for repair is provided 
in accordance with the procedure estab lished at the Rooppur NPP given the state of 
systems and equipment of the Unit. 
9.6.4 Organizational issues during Unit start-up 
9.6.4.1 Acceptance of the Unit from medium repair and overhaul is 
performed by a commission comprising administrative and technical personnel  of the 
Rooppur NPP chaired by the NPP CE, including the managers of repair works 
appointed by the relevant orders. Acceptance of the Unit after overhaul and medium 
repair shall be performed according to the program “Working program for bringing 
the reactor plant to design power. Sequence of operations for preparation for RP start-
up after refueling with subsequent Unit bringing to design power”. 
9.6.4.2 Start-up of the Unit after scheduled repair is performed with the 
permission of the operating organization. The basis for obtaining such permission is 
the statement of the NPP SS (or its substitute person) confirming the readiness of the 
Unit for start -up. The request shall indicate the start -up date, the start -up time of 
reaching reactor power MCPL. The above statement shall confirm: 
- serviceability and readiness of the Unit equipment, including safety systems 
for actuation in accordance with the requirements of the technical specification; 
- full completion of planned repair works, as well as modernization and 
technical re-equipment of the Unit equipment and systems; 
- compliance of scope and quality of works performed with the requirements of 
effective regulatory documents. 
The statement on the readiness of the Unit for start -up shall be prepared in 
accordance with the requirements established by the Atomic Energy Commission of 
the People’s Republic of Bangladesh (ВАЕС). 
ATTENTION! 
Communication with duty dispatchers of dispatching services during checks and tests is 
provided by the dispatching service of Rooppur NPP. 
The NPP personnel shall not have the right, without the permission of NPP SS, RDM, ODM 
dispatcher, to switch off, on, test and change the setpoints of the system automation, as well as the 
dispatching and process control means under the supervision or control of the respective dispatcher 
(power plant shift supervisor). 
9.6.4.3 The start-up of the Unit after refueling, repair or reconstruction, as 
well as after any downtime, except for a short time (less than three days), shall be 
performed in accordance with the schedule developed for this particular start -up. The 
schedule shall define the list of tests performed during this start-up. 
[PAGE 295]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP 
Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
293 
9.6.4.4 Readiness of the equipment, documentation and personnel of the 
Unit for start -up is confirmed by records in the technical orders logbook of the Unit 
by the heads of shops and subdivisions that perform operation, repair and monitoring 
of the state of equipment and systems, DCE (r), DCE (o). 
9.6.4.5 After preparing a report of Unit acceptance after repair, a permit for 
the Unit start-up shall be drawn up in the technical orders logbook of the Unit signed 
by the NPP CE or DCE (o) indicating the maximum permitted level of reactor power 
and agreed with the head of the BAERA inspection at the Rooppur NPP. 
9.6.4.6 During the start-up of the Unit, the Chief Engineer appoints the DCE 
(o) as the technical manager of the start-up. 
9.6.4.7 The USS reports to the NPP SS on the received permission to start 
the Unit and, with the permission of NPP SS, gives a written order (drawn up in the 
LETC and LERC operational logbook). 
9.6.4.8 The technical manager of start -up shall draw up tasks for the 
operating personnel in the shift tasks logbook of the Unit for: 
- RP heat-up to hydraulic test temperature; 
- checking of the primary and secondary circuits for tightness (strength); 
- RP heat-up to nominal parameters; 
- inspections and tests in the “hot” state of the Unit. 
9.6.4.9 The tightness of the containment shall be provided after switching on 
RCPS and inspecting the equipment until the t emperature of the primary circuit 
coolant of 150 ºС above zero is reached, while: 
- process rooms of the primary circuit were checked according to the approved 
list for the absence of people, combustible and explosive objects. These rooms shall 
be closed and sealed upon completion of the inspection; 
- all doors of locks are closed and sealed for personnel passage to containment 
rooms, locks opening (closing) interlocks are put into operation; 
- check results are recorded in the RS SS, USS operational logs. 
9.6.4.10 The readiness of equipment, documentation and personnel of the 
Unit to reach MCPL is confirmed by records in the technical orders logbook of the 
Unit by the heads of equipment and systems subdivision -owners, DCE (r), DCE (o). 
Permission to start operations  to change over the Unit to the “reaching MCPL” state 
is given by NPP SS or DCE (o). 
9.6.4.11 Bringing the reactor to MCPL from the sub -critical state after 
refueling of the reactor, as well as after any shutdown of the reactor shall be 
performed in the presence of  the NSRD engineer -physicist. Calculation of start -up 
concentration after refueling is given using the “Album of neutron -physical 
characteristics” with a record in the Unit technical orders logbook. 
9.6.4.12 The technical manager of start -up shall draw up tasks for  the 
operating personnel to bring the Unit to MCPL and to perform measurements of 
neutron-physical characteristics (after PPM with nuclear fuel refueling) in the shift 
tasks logbook of the Unit. 
[PAGE 296]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP 
Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001
