294 
9.6.4.13 NPP SS shall draw up a written order for bringing the RP to M CPL 
in the USS operational logbook and USS - in the LERC and LETC operational 
logbooks. 
9.6.4.14 Operations to reach the critical state shall be performed only by 
commands of NPP SS or USS. 
9.6.4.15 The technical manager of start-up, NPP SS, RS SS shall be present at 
the Un it MCR at any reactor bringing to power from the sub -critical state. RS SS 
shall monitor LERC actions before switching to automatic mode of reactor power 
maintenance. 
9.6.4.16 The start-up of the Unit after an unscheduled shutdown is performed 
in accordance with Item 9.2.7 of this specification. 
9.6.4.17 Bringing the reactor to a critical state is a nuclear -hazardous work 
and shall be performed according to the program “Working program for bringing the 
reactor plant to design power. Sequence of operations for preparation for  RP start-up 
after refueling with subsequent Unit bringing to design power”. 
9.6.5 Organizational issues in the “power operation” state 
9.6.5.1 After the Unit downtime for more than 10 days, the heads of the RS, 
TS, TICS, ES, CS, VS, NSRD, RSD heads, NPP CE deputies for  operation, safety 
and repair shall confirm the readiness of the systems for Unit connection to the mains 
and load buildup with records in the technical orders logbook of the Unit. 
9.6.5.2 NPP SS permission with indication of permitted level of thermal 
power of re actor plant shall be obtained for Unit power buildup. Permission to raise 
power shall be recorded in the LERC and USS operational logbooks. 
9.6.5.3 The technical manager of start -up, NPP SS, shift supervisors of RS, 
TS, TICS, ES shall be present at the Unit MCR wh en the turbine generator is 
connected to the mains. 
9.6.5.4 Permission of RDM, ODM dispatching services shall be obtained for 
generator connection in the mains. NPP SS receives permission from the dispatching 
services. 
9.6.5.5 Physical, dynamic and thermal -hydraulic tests  at the Unit shall be 
performed under the permitted requests and according to the programs duly agreed 
and approved by the NPP CE. Work under the programs is performed by shop 
personnel by the USS command under the technical supervision of a person 
appointed by the NPP CE. 
9.6.5.6 All operations that require constant monitoring by operating 
personnel shall be stopped during the shift turnover at the Unit. 
9.6.5.7 Any planned change in the power of the Unit shall be made by 
written permission of the NPP SS in the USS operat ional logbook after receiving 
permission from the RDM, ODM dispatching services and the operating 
organization. Power change operations shall be performed under the supervision of 
USS. 
9.6.5.8 Tests and checks of safety related systems and components shall be 
performed according to instructions, programs and schedules approved by NPP CE. 
[PAGE 297]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP 
Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
295 
9.6.5.9 Setpoints of protections, interlocks and alarms shall always be set in 
accordance with the setpoint chart. Devices with setpoints shall be sealed, the 
availability of seals is chec ked by the TICS operating personnel. It is prohibited to 
perform any repair and adjustment works in the circuits of actuated protections. 
9.6.5.10 TICS personnel shall provide the following during operation of ICIS 
equipment: 
1) maintaining an archive of measured and calculated parameters; 
2) maintenance of metrological characteristics of the protection function by 
local parameters implemented in the ICIS CAS-P; 
3) taking printouts (once a shift) of temperature sensor signals in RP loops and 
at FA output, as well as  DCD signals with analysis of their operability. Analysis of 
sensors operability and reliability of information shall be performed by personnel 
using data from internal instrumentation system records; 
4) taking printouts (once a shift) of the main controll ed parameters with 
assessment of margin up to the established limits. 
9.6.5.11 Boundary valves on the air removal pipeline from the RCPS 
independent circuit shall be open only by the USS order. 
9.6.5.12 Personnel admission to the containment at a pressure in the RCC 
above atmospheric, if necessary, shall be performed with locking in accordance with 
a special instruction. 
9.6.5.13 Taking normal operation systems, devices or equipment out of 
service for repair that results in the operation without redundancy for the period of 
repair is allowed only with the written permission of NPP CE. 
9.6.6 Organizational issues during Unit shutdown 
9.6.6.1 Unit shutdown can be short -term (up to 3 days), up to 15 days and 
long-term (more than 15 days). Depending on the final state, the shutdown is 
performed with ch angeover to the “hot” state or to the “cold” state for repair work, 
refueling of reactor fuel with partial or complete unloading of it from the core. 
9.6.6.2 Permission for the planned shutdown of the Unit is given by the NPP 
CE with a record in the technical orders logbook of the Unit. 
9.6.6.3 Operations for planned unloading of the Unit and its shutdown are 
performed by the operating personnel by the NPP SS written order with a record in 
the USS operational logbook after receiving the appropriate permission of the RDM, 
ODM dispatching services and the USS written order in the LERC and LETC 
operational logbooks. 
9.6.6.4 Before the cooldown, before the planned shutdown of the Unit, 
inspection of the primary and secondary circuits equipment shall be performed in-situ 
at nominal parameters in order to: 
- check the absence of leaks and steaming, the state of thermal insulation; 
- check the state of indicators of thermal movements, freedom of thermal 
movements of pipelines and equipment; 
- check the operability and absence of foreign items in supports of equipment 
and pipelines. 
[PAGE 298]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP 
Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
296 
9.6.6.5 Organizational measures shall be taken during Unit shutdown: 
- planned shutdown of the Unit shall be performed according to the program 
(procedure) of the Unit shutdown approved by the NPP CE; 
- completion of all  works performed according to special programs shall be 
recorded under the procedure established at the Rooppur NPP; 
- all operations that require constant monitoring by operating personnel shall be 
stopped for the time of shift turnover; 
- repair, mainten ance, checks and tests of systems and components shall be 
performed with registration of a permit under the procedure established at the 
Rooppur NPP. 
9.6.6.6 Preservation treatment of the condensate and feedwater path (CFWP) 
and SG shall be performed in accordance  with the requirements of Appendix D 
during the Unit shutdown. 
A specific preservation mode of each SG is developed in accordance with the 
process flow diagram during the PPM and depending on the shutdown duration. 
9.6.7 Organizational issues during start-up after unscheduled shutdown 
9.6.7.1 Start-up of the Unit after any unscheduled shutdown is performed 
only with the permission of the operating organization. The permit is issued on the 
basis of the NPP SS (or its substitute person) application on the Unit readiness fo r 
start-up, indicating the start -up date; start -up operation start time and start time of 
reaching reactor MCPL. The application shall contain: 
- certificate on detected causes of disturbances in Rooppur NPP operation and 
measures taken to eliminate them; 
- conclusion on compliance of safety system state, including CPS, with the 
specification requirements. 
9.6.7.2 Start-up after unscheduled shutdown shall be performed in 
accordance with the start-up procedure (program) approved by the NPP CE. 
The start-up procedure (program) shall unambiguously define the list of tests 
performed during this start-up and the number of test programs under which they are 
to be performed. 
If necessary, additional works shall be included in the start -up procedure 
(program): 
1) if there i s a leak of equipment or pipeline during repair, the electric 
resistance of all electric motors, cables, PRZ TEH and other electrical equipment that 
have fallen into the moisture action area shall be measured after its elimination, as 
well as the serviceability (reliability of sensor indications) of I&CD shall be checked; 
2) if repair works using welding were performed on the equipment of the 
primary (or secondary) circuit, then after the repair it is necessary to perform 
unscheduled hydraulic tests of the primary circuit with a pressure of 24.5 MPa (or a 
pressure of 11.5 MPa for the secondary circuit equipment). Hydraulic tests of 
repaired pipelines may be replaced with 100% inspection of new welds and repair 
sites using ultrasonic flaw detection or radiogr aphic method, and surface flaw 
detection methods; 
[PAGE 299]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP 
Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
297 
3) the equipment shall be checked in accordance with the requirements of the 
“Regulations for inspections and tests of systems and equipment of Rooppur NPP 
Unit No.1” before start -up after downtime to perfo rm unscheduled repair lasting 
more than 10 days, including: 
- serviceability of thermal insulation; 
- state of thermal displacement indicators; 
- serviceability and absence of foreign objects in RCPS, SG supports; 
- possibility of temperature movements of primary circuit equipment and 
pipelines without limitations; 
- compliance of indications from sensors measuring temperature movements of 
equipment and pipelines with actual temperature in the primary circuit; 
- position of valves on sampling lines from primary and secondary circuits; 
- position of boundary valves separating sections of pipelines with high and 
low medium pressure; 
- state of drains and air vent valves of systems and equipment; 
- I&CD state; 
- removal of temporary accessories for repair, including plugs. 
9.6.7.3 After an unscheduled shutdown in the absence of damage to 
equipment and structures, the subsequent power level reaching is allowed after 
determining and eliminating the causes of the shutdown and with permission from 
BAERA and BAEC, the operating organization for start-up. 
9.6.7.4 The Unit start -up after an unscheduled shutdown is performed by a 
written order of the NPP CE in the technical orders logbook at the MCR after 
receiving permission from the RDM, ODM dispatching services with an indication of 
the maximum permitted reactor power level. 
9.6.7.5 During the start-up of the Unit, the Chief Engineer appoints the DCE 
(o) as the technical manager of the start-up. 
9.6.7.6 The USS reports to the NPP SS on the received permission to start 
the Unit and, with the permissio n of NPP SS, gives a written order (drawn up in the 
LETC and LERC operational logbook). 
9.6.7.7 The technical manager of start -up shall draw up tasks for the 
operating personnel in the shift tasks logbook of the Unit for: 
- heat-up up to hydraulic test temperature (if necessary); 
- checking the primary and secondary circuits for tightness (strength) (if 
necessary); 
- RP heat-up to nominal parameters; 
- inspections and tests in the “hot” state of the Unit. 
9.6.7.8 If damage to equipment or systems preventing its start -up wa s 
detected after the shutdown, in this case the start -up is allowed after investigating the 
cause of the shutdown under the established procedure and after the elimination of 
the detected defects and damages, with the permission of BAERA and BAEC. 
9.6.7.9 Start-up after unscheduled shutdown for equipment repair is allowed 
after: 
[PAGE 300]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP 
Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
298 
- finding out the cause and completion of the repair of the equipment taken out 
of service for repair, followed by checking its operability; 
- completion of readiness check before reaching MCPL given in Section 5.4; 
- issuing the start-up permit. 
9.6.7.10 It is allowed not to check the protections and interlocks in case of 
short-term shutdown (up to three days) and provided that no repair work was 
performed in the protection circuits or voltage was not removed from them. 
In case of shutdown lasting from three to seven days and under the same 
conditions, it is allowed not to check protections and interlocks, except for reactor 
EP, PP and protections that comprise safety systems, which are checked in fu ll after 
each shutdown. 
Checks of protections and interlocks shall be performed within the scope 
specified in the “Regulations for inspections and tests of systems and equipment of 
Rooppur NPP Unit No.1” in case of shutdown lasting more than 7 days. 
Depending on the specific conditions and parameters during the unscheduled 
shutdown for a period of 7 to 10 days, the required scope of checks of protections and 
interlocks can be determined in the start -up program developed and approved at the 
NPP based on the requirements of the regulations for checks of protections and 
interlocks. 
9.6.7.11 During a short-term shutdown due to erroneous actions of personnel 
or actuation of protections, it is prohibited to perform switching in process and 
electric circuits, which may lead  to a change in the pre -shutdown state of these 
systems, except for switching due to process necessity. Start -up is allowed after 
finding out the cause of the shutdown and eliminating the fault. 
9.6.7.12 During RP start -up after a short -term shutdown, the equipment  is 
subjected to regular checks, which has reached the deadlines for checks and tests of 
safety related systems and equipment in accordance with the schedule of checks and 
tests developed by the Rooppur NPP administration. 
9.7 Organization of radiation safety assurance 
9.7.1 Rooppur NPP administration ensures strict accounting of personnel 
exposure doses, development and implementation of measures to reduce irradiation 
of NPP personnel and personnel of other organizations involved in the maintenance. 
9.7.2 Rooppur NPP admi nistration ensures accounting and control of 
generation, use, processing, storage of radioactive substances and radioactive waste, 
movement and locations of dismantled radioactive equipment, contaminated tools 
and clothing. 
9.7.3 Radiation monitoring is performe d by the personnel of the radiation 
safety department (RSD) at the Rooppur NPP. It is allowed to perform certain types 
of radiation monitoring by personnel of other NPP subdivisions under the 
methodological guidance of the radiation safety service. 
[PAGE 301]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP 
Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
299 
9.7.4 The radiation monitoring system technical means provide the following 
at the Rooppur NPP: 
- process radiation monitoring (PRM); 
- dosimetric radiation monitoring (DRM); 
- premises and site radiation monitoring (PSRM); 
- radiation contamination confinement monitoring (RMC); 
- environment radiation monitoring (ERM); 
- accident radiation monitoring (ARM). 
9.7.5 Automated radiation monitoring system provides monitoring, 
registration, display, collection, processing and output of reporting information 
according to unified forms. 
Operational information on radiation parameters, according to which the limits 
of safe operation are established, is automatically transmitted to the MCR and ECR, 
as well as to the central (CRMP) and unit (RMB) radiation monitoring posts. 
9.7.6 The radiation monitoring system for parameters, according to which the 
limits of safe operation are established, uses the following technical means at the 
Rooppur NPP: 
- continuous monitoring based on stationary automated technical means; 
- operational monitoring based on wearable, mobile technical means; 
- laboratory analysis based on stationary laboratory equipment, sampling and 
preparation facilities for analyses; 
- individual dosimetric monitoring of personnel irradiation. 
In case of a radiation accident, emergency  sets of radiation reconnaissance and 
dosimetric monitoring devices are provided in accordance with the current range. 
9.7.7 Rooppur NPP provides monitoring of radioactive substances coming 
from liquid effluents into storage tanks. The quantity of radioactive su bstances is 
monitored in accordance with the radiation monitoring regulations in case of 
discharge of liquid effluents from the storage tank into the external environment. 
9.7.8 When planning radiation -hazardous works at the Rooppur NPP, 
external exposure doses are calculated based on the results of radiation monitoring of 
premises and equipment given previously performed similar works. 
9.7.9 At the Rooppur NPP, individual dosimetric monitoring (IDM) is 
performed by monitoring the doses of external and internal exposure of personnel. 
All personnel working in the controlled access area as well as in the common 
access area with ionizing radiation sources are subject to IDM. 
Accounting for the results of individual dosimetric monitoring provides receipt 
of information on r adiation doses during NPP power operation, during repairs and 
during radiation-hazardous works. 
The Rooppur NPP provides for an automated system for recording the results 
of individual dosimetric monitoring (AIDMS), which provides the registration of 
personnel exposure doses and allows planning personnel exposure based on the 
analysis results. 
[PAGE 302]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP 
Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
300 
9.7.10 Rooppur NPP personnel shall strictly observe the area regime 
established by regulatory documents. The procedure for crossing the established 
boundaries of the areas b y people and radioactive materials is specified in the 
relevant instructions approved by the Rooppur NPP administration. 
9.7.11 The administration systematically analyzes the results of medical and 
dosimetric monitoring of personnel, as well as radiation monitoring on the territory of 
Rooppur NPP and SA, to develop measures to reduce personnel exposure doses and 
reduce the impact of NPP on the environment. 
9.7.12 Data on external and internal exposure doses of Rooppur NPP 
personnel and seconded persons shall be stored on  reliable storage media in the RSD 
for at least 50 years from the date of employee’s dismissal. 
The annual effective and equivalent dose, effective dose for 5 consecutive 
years, as well as the total accumulated dose for the entire period of professional 
activity are accounted for when performing individual monitoring. 
9.7.13 The Rooppur NPP has developed special instructions that regulate the 
accounting and control of radioactive substances, radioactive waste and RSb in SNF, 
measures and means that provide effective control and accounting. 
9.7.14 Planned inventory is performed at the Rooppur NPP: 
- radioactive substances (RSb) and RSb in SNF - annually; 
- radioactive waste (RAW) - once every five years. 
Those responsible for accounting and control check the actual available amount 
of NM, RSb and RAW with determination of their quantity, composition, as well as 
their changes. 
9.7.15 Individual dosimetric monitoring (IDM) of personnel external exposure 
comprise the following types of monitoring: 
- routine; 
- operational; 
- emergency. 
Thermoluminescent dosimeters (TLD) are used as the main means of IDM for 
current and emergency monitoring of external exposure at Rooppur NPP. 
Operational means of individual dosimetric monitoring are issued to all 
personnel located in the controlled ac cess area to ensure operational monitoring of 
external exposure. 
Frequency of individual dosimeter measurements: 
- electronic direct indication - every shift, upon completion of works; 
- IDM main means (TLD): 
a) at least once a quarter; 
b) monthly - for women of reproductive age (up to 45 years); 
c) when receiving a dose exceeding the permitted for the work by operational 
monitoring means. 
Individual dosimetric monitoring of internal irradiation consists in 
determination of expected effective dose (EED) of internal irradiation based on 
results of monitoring of radionuclide intake to human body. 
[PAGE 303]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP 
Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
301 
Measurement of the content of radionuclides in the human body is performed 
using WBC plants. 
IDM of internal exposure of personnel is divided into information, curren t, 
operational and special (emergency) in terms of frequency. 
Information monitoring consists in conducting a survey at the WBC in order to 
determine the content of radionuclides in the employee’s lungs and is used for: 
- monitoring of all newly hired and dismissed personnel; 
- annual monitoring of all Group A personnel. 
The IDM current monitoring consists in systematic instrumental measurements 
to determine the EED caused by the intake of radionuclides into the body at unknown 
times (intervals) and is perf ormed based on the results of information monitoring at 
least once a quarter. 
Operational monitoring consists in measuring the content of radionuclides in 
the body or individual organs of a person in order to determine the increase in EED 
due to a single (short-term) intake of radionuclides into the body at a known moment 
in time when personnel perform radiation-hazardous work related to the possibility of 
increased intake of radioactive substances into the body, including work in the 
conditions of the planned increased exposure. 
Special (emergency) monitoring is performed in case of an accident. 
9.7.16 At the Rooppur NPP, radiation monitoring is performed on equipment, 
in premises and on the territory of the NPP using portable devices with frequency and 
volume in accordance with the Regulation for radiation monitoring. 
9.7.17 A regular check of the serviceability of radiation monitoring equipment 
is provided in accordance with the regulations at the Rooppur NPP. 
9.7.18 With the help of ARMS, the Rooppur NPP constantly monitors: 
- daily release of radioactive gases, 131I and aerosols into the atmosphere 
through ventilation stacks; 
- specific activity and radionuclide composition of NPP waste water; 
- indications of measuring channels for monitoring IRG volumetric activity and 
tightness of process equipment. 
9.7.19 The Rooppur NPP provides for technical and organizational measures 
to protect against the propagation of activity in the equipment of the secondary circuit 
in the mode of disturbance of steam generators piping tightness in case of primary-to-
secondary circuit leaks. 
9.8 Organization of nuclear-hazardous works 
9.8.1 The list of nuclear -hazardous works is developed at the NPP and 
approved by the NPP CE based on the design documentation, the design list of 
nuclear-hazardous works and operating experience.  
9.8.2 Nuclear-hazardous works are performed according to a special working 
program approved by the NPP Chief Engineer. Nuclear -hazardous activities shall be 
performed, as a rule, at a shutdown reactor. The sub -criticality of the shutdown 
[PAGE 304]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP 
Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
302 
reactor during nuclear-hazardous works shall be at least 0.02 for the state of the core 
with the maximum effective multiplication coefficient. 
9.8.3 Works that affect the NPP safety not stipulated by the technical 
specifications and operation instructions are performed according to programs agreed 
with the RP and NPP designers and approved by the operating organization. 
9.8.4 The working program shall contain:  
 list of nuclear-hazardous works;  
 purpose of nuclear-hazardous works; 
 technical and organizational measures for nuclear safety assurance; 
 criteria and check of correctness of nuclear-hazardous works completion; 
 instruction on the appointment of a responsible person for nuclear -
hazardous works; 
 safety measures shall be based on the safety analyses performed. 
9.8.5 The list of NH A is developed in a separate NPP document “List of 
nuclear-hazardous works at the reactor plant of Unit No. 1 of Rooppur NPP”. This 
list defines nuclear -hazardous works that shall be performed according to specially 
developed programs (instructions) duly approved. 
9.8.6 Each of the works included in the list of nuclear -hazardous works is 
performed in accordance with the requirements of the operation and technical 
documentation.  
9.8.7 For any RP state, it is prohibited to simultaneously perform two or 
more NHA that affect the reactivity or reliability of heat removal from FE.

1) 1) Variable power setpoint depending on the number of operating RCPS is generated as follows:  
when one of the four RCPS gets disabled, the variable setpoint decreases linearly from 107 to 74% Nnom at a rate of 0.5% Nnom/s;  
when one of the three RCPS gets disabled (two adjacent RCPS remain in operation), the variable setpoint linearly decreases from the current one to 
47% Nnom at a rate of 0.33% Nnom/s;  
2) when 3 or more RCPS get disabled, the variable setpoint linearly decreases from the current value to 5% Nnom at a rate of 0.33% Nnom/s.  
When the RCPS gets connected, the setpoint value as per Item 4 of this table is automatically restored to the value corresponding to the number of 
operating RCPS.

N o t e  2  
1) The value of inertia shall not be more than 1.0 s for signals as per Items 6 and 9 of this table in modes accompanied by a sharp pressure drop in the 
primary circuit (for example, primary circuit coolant leak).  
2) The error value of neutron power measurement using NFME (Items 2, 3, 4, 7, 23 of this table) is given relative to the calibration value obtained 
from MCDS (ICIS).  
3) The operational conditions of neutron flux monitoring equipment related to the occurrence of a fault in its measuring channels is given in Item 9.3.

1) 1) Variable power setpoint depending on the number of operating RCPS is generated as follows:  
- when one of the four RCPS gets disabled, the variable setpoint decreases linearly from 104 to 72% Nnom at a rate of 0.5% Nnom/s;  
- when one of the three RCPS gets disabled, the variable setpoint decreases linearly from the current one to 46% Nnom at a rate of 0.33% Nnom/s.  
2) When the RCPS gets connected, the variable setpoint value as per Item 9 of this table is automatically restored to the value corresponding to the 
number of operating RCPS. 
3) The error value of neutron power measurement using NFME (Items 9, 10, 11, 16, 18 of this table) is given relative to the calibration value obtained 
from MCDS (ICIS).

Appendix C  
(mandatory) 
Limitations on equipment loading conditions 
С.1 In the process of RP operation, the number of equipment loading cycles in 
normal operation, in case of disturbances of normal operation (DNO), which is 
limited by the design, shall be recorded. The maximum permissible number of 
equipment loading cycles for the design modes of RP operation is given in Tables C.1 
- C.3 in accordance with the NPP design and is identical to the number of equipment 
loading cycles specified in the SAR. 
С.2 Monitoring of residual RP equipment lifetime during the Unit operation  is 
performed using the “ARLMS” MCDS subsystem, which keeps records of the 
damage rate of individual RP equipment assemblies. 
When the subsystem determines the exhaustion of the residual life for any of the 
individual RP assemblies, an operational decision  shall be made with the 
participation of representatives of RP Chief Designer on the conditions for further 
Unit operation. 
Initiating event that requires subsystem taking out of operation for repair does 
not lead to disturbance of subsystem functions perf ormance after its operability 
recovery.

Notes to Tables С.1 - С.3 
1) The process proceeds according to the design project in all modes. 
2) The number of cycles decreases in proportion to the decrease in service life for equipmen t with 
a service life of less than 60 years. 
3) The cycles shown in the tables comprise the cycles that will be gained upon start -up and 
adjustment works. 
4) Number of cycles of assemblies set loading for service life shall not exceed values specified in 
Table 5.3 for this fuel cycle. It is prohibited to operate the reactor and FA complex, which have 
exhausted their life in terms of loading cycles. 
5) It is necessary to assess the accumulated damage and the residual life of the equipment in case 
of exceeding the num ber of modes stipulated in the substantiation of equipment or its components 
strength, or in the case of more stringent conditions of their progress, as well as in the case of non -
design modes. Operation can be continued if the operating organization has a  substantiating 
analysis agreed under the established procedure.

resistance) the minimum allowable temperature of hydraulic tests and tightness test of 
the equipment for rea ctor vessel, at which pressure rise in the equipment is allowed 
during hydraulic tests of the RP, is given in Table C.4 for reactor vessel and C.5 for 
other equipment.

Appendix D  
(mandatory) 
Water chemistry standards of the primary and secondary circuits 
D.1 The requirements for WC standards of the primary circuit of the NPP Unit 
are established in accordance with the “Standards of water chemistry of the primary 
circuit. 10JAA-MEC0028 523D2” developed by OKB GIDROPRESS for  RP V-523 
of Rooppur NPP.  
Appendix D shall be corrected based on the obtained results of analysis of pilot 
commercial operation for the primary circuit WC and brought into compliance with 
the requirements of the final version of 10JAA-MEC0028 523D2. 
D.1.1 General provisions 
D.1.1.1 A weakly alkaline reduction coordinated ammonia -potassium water 
chemistry mode with boric acid shall be used in the primary circuit during Unit 
power operation. 
D.1.1.2 Primary circuit water chemistry shall ensure the following functional 
requirements: 
- suppression of formation of oxidative products of radiolysis during power 
operation; 
- corrosion resistance of structural materials of equipment and pipelines during 
the design service life of the Unit; 
- minimization of deposits on surfaces of fuel elements of the reactor core and 
heat exchange surface of steam generators on the primary circuit side; 
- minimizing accumulation of activated corrosion products. 
D.1.1.3 Suppression of the formation of oxidative radiolysis products is  
provided by maintaining the hydrogen concentration within the acceptable range by 
continuous or periodic dosing of ammonia radiolytically decomposing to form 
hydrogen and nitrogen. 
Corrosion resistance of structural materials of equipment and pipelines du ring 
the design service life of the Unit is provided by maintaining corrosive impurities 
within the specified limits. 
To minimize the formation of activated corrosion products on the surfaces of 
pipelines and equipment of the primary circuit, also during t he period of power unit 
commissioning during “hot running -in” a preliminary passivation of the surfaces in 
contact with the primary circuit coolant is carried out.   
D.1.1.4 Reduction of the intensity of sediment growth processes on heat 
transfer surfaces and accumulation of activated corrosion products on the primary 
circuit equipment surfaces during power operation is provided by maintaining the 
total molar concentration of alkali metal ions (potassium, lithium and sodium) in 
accordance with the optimal c oordinated dependence of them on the current boric 
acid concentration. For this purpose it is also envisaged to dose a zinc acetate solution 
depleted in 64Zn isotope (less than 1 %) into the coolant of the primary circuit. 
[PAGE 340]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1  RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001  
Version 2  
Continuation of Appendix D 
338 
D.1.1.5 The primary circuit coola nt quality standards provide for the division 
of primary circuit coolant quality indicators into rated and diagnostic indicators. For 
each of the rated indicators there are ranges of permissible values, as well as levels of 
deviation of the values of the rated indicators from the range of permissible values.  
Reference levels are set for diagnostic indicators. 
D.1.1.6 Rated indicators are indicators of the primary circuit coolant quality, 
the maintenance of which in the range of permissible values ensures t he integrity of 
the core elements, designated service life of the primary circuit equipment and 
pipelines and satisfactory radiation situation at the unit, in accordance with the 
established requirements. 
D.1.1.7 Diagnostic indicators include quality indic ators of the primary circuit 
coolant, which provide information on the causes of changes in the rated indicators in 
case of deviation from the range of permissible values. Diagnostic parameters, with 
the exception of boric acid concentration, also comprise  quality indicators of makeup 
water, water of fuel pool and RVI inspection cavities, borated solutions of RP safety 
systems, as well as water quality indicators of auxiliary systems. 
The minimum permissible values of boric acid concentration in the water o f 
fuel pool and RVI inspection cavities, and in borated solution tanks of RP safety 
systems are established based on ensuring the required level of reactor sub -criticality. 
Personnel actions in case of decrease of boric acid concentration (and/or isotope 10B) 
in them below the minimum permissible values specified in this document are 
defined in accordance with Section 3 of TSSO. 
Deviations of diagnostic indicators from reference levels indicate disturbances 
in the operation of process systems for ensuring w ater chemistry, which may lead to 
unacceptable deviations of the rated indicators. 
D.1.1.8 A violation of the water chemistry is a deviation of the rated indicators 
of the coolant quality from the range of permissible values, not eliminated within the 
specified time. 
The countdown of the Unit operation time at the levels of actions given in this 
document begins from the moment of fixing the deviation of the rated indicators of 
the primary circuit coolant quality. 
If diagnostic indicators deviate from the re ference levels given in this 
document, which do not lead to deviation of the rated indicators, work shall be 
performed to find and eliminate the causes of deviation. The inability to eliminate the 
deviation of diagnostic parameters within 7 days is recorde d as a disturbance of the 
water chemistry. 
Countdown of the unit operation time with deviations of one or several rated 
indicators from the range of permissible values and/or in case of deviation of one or 
several diagnostic indicators starts from the moment of deviation recording. 
D.1.1.9 The values of the chemical quality indicators given in this document 
correspond to the results of measurements in samples under standard conditions: 
[PAGE 341]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1  RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001

- temperature - 25 °С above zero; 
- pressure - 0.1 MPa. 
Concentrations of components of aqueous solutions are assigned to 1 dm 3 of 
the sample. 
 D.1.1.10 Primary circuit chemical monitoring data specified in this document 
shall be recorded and stored at the Unit until it is taken out of operation. 
D.1.1.11 The quality of reagen ts and ionites used for water chemistry 
correction and purification of primary circuit media shall comply with the 
requirements of regulatory documentation. 
D.1.1.12 The scope and frequency of chemical monitoring of the  primary 
circuit process media are d etermined by the “Regulations for chemical monitoring of 
process media at the Rooppur NPP” with the help of the following systems for 
automated and laboratory monitoring of the primary circuit water chemistry: 
  KUA100 sampling system from laboratory monito ring equipment 
(including module for post-accident sampling); 
 KUA60 primary circuit automated chemical monitoring system; 
 KUE  sampling system from active water treatment plants. 
D.1.1.13 The following sampling points shall be provided for quality control of 
coolant, makeup water, auxiliary systems water and boric acid solutions of RP safety 
systems and monitoring of purification systems operation: 
 at the KBE50-60 low-temperature coolant purification system inlet; 
 from the reactor vessel and RCPL loops; 
 downstream the makeup pumps for quality control of primary circuit 
makeup water of KBA volume and chemical control system; 
 downstream the heat exchanger of the JNA reactor coolant circuit 
emergency and planned cooldown and fuel pool cooling system; 
 downstream MBF of the KBE50 -60 low -temperature coolant purification 
system; 
 downstream the Н -cation-exchange filter of the KBE50 -60 low -
temperature coolant purification system designed to remove excess alkalinity from 
the primary circuit coolant; 
 downstream the OH -anion-exchange filter of the KBE50 -60 low -
temperature coolant purification system designed to remove boric acid at the end of 
the cycle; 
 from the FAK10-20 fuel pool cooling system; 
 downstream filters of KBH fuel pool water purification system; 
 downstream filters of KBF coolant treatment system; 
 water medium from the lower part and steam medium from the upper part 
of JEF system (PRZ system); 
 from the accumulators of the JNG50-80 emergency core cooling system;

D.1.1.14 Zinc dosing in the primary circuit at th e Rooppur NPP Unit No. 1 
shall be performed according to a separate program agreed with the RSD inspection. 
Dosing of zinc solution at the Rooppur NPP can be performed only after 
performance of works on pilot commercial operation in order to justify safety  and 
efficiency of this technology. After safety justification, a special program of zinc 
dosing into the primary circuit coolant shall be developed.  The zinc dosing unit shall 
be preserved before completion of pilot commercial operation and development o f a 
special program. Organizational measures shall also be taken to prevent the supply of 
zinc compound solution to the coolant: 
 do not perform preparation of the process solution of the zinc compound in 
the 10KBD40BB001 tank; 
 disassemble the electric circ uits for control and feeding of KBD40BB001 
zinc compound solution tank mixer; 
 disassemble the electric circuits for control and feeding of KBD40AP001 
zinc compound solution dosing pump; 
 close all valves of the assembly.  
Lock closed position of valves. Dis assemble the electric circuits of control and 
power supply of 10KBD40AA001,003 electrically driven valves. 
D.1.2 Unit operation at power > 50% Nnom 
D.1.2.1 Standards of primary circuit coolant quality and levels of deviations of 
rated indicators during Unit power operation > 50 % of Nnom are given in Table D.1. 
D.1.2.2 The total molar concentration of alkali metal ions (potassium, lithium, 
sodium) in the primary circuit coolant shall be maintained depending on the current 
boric acid concentration within area A indicated in Figure D.1. 
D.1.2.3 The concentration of ammonia in the coolant shall be maintained at a 
level providing a hydrogen concentration in the range from 2.2 to 4.5 mg/dm3. 
The concentration of dissolved oxygen in the primary circuit coolant sha ll not 
exceed 0.005 mg/dm3. 
D.1.2.4 The KBE50 -60 primary circuit coolant low -temperature purification 
system filters shall operate continuously at the required flow rate. 
D.1.2.5 Diagnostic indicators of the quality of water of fuel pool and RVI 
inspection cavities shall correspond to the values given in Table D.4.

D.1.3.1 First deviation level. 
Deviation of one or several rated indicators specified i n Table D.1 within the 
first level of deviations during Unit power operation > 50% of Nnom, not eliminated 
within seven days, is recorded, according to Item D.1.1.8, as a disturbance of water 
chemistry with mandatory analysis of the causes of disturbance a nd issue of a report 
on the results of analysis of water chemistry disturbance causes. The report shall 
contain a program of corrective measures to eliminate the disturbance and 
recommendations to prevent recurrence in the future.  
If it is impossible to e liminate the causes of deviation of rated indicators of the 
primary circuit coolant within 7 days, it is necessary to reduce the unit capacity to ≤ 
30 % Nnom. 
The total duration of the Unit operation with deviation of the rated indicator by 
the total molar  concentration of alkali metal ions (Area B) shall not exceed 30 days 
per fuel cycle of the Unit operation. 
D.1.3.2 Second deviation level. 
Permissible Unit operation duration at power > 50% Nnom in case of deviation 
of one or several rated indicators given in Table D.1 within the second level shall not 
exceed 24 hours from the moment of deviation registration. 
If it is impossible to identify the causes and eliminate deviations of the rated 
indicators within 24 hours, change over the Unit to the “reactor at MCPL” state. 
The subsequent power increase of the Unit is possible only after elimination of 
the causes of deviation and restoration of indicators to the rated values according to 
the requirements of Table D.3. 
The duration of Unit operation with deviation of the rated indicator for chloride 
ion concentration shall not exceed five days per fuel cycle of Unit operation. 
D.1.3.3 Third deviation level. 
The Unit shall be changed over to the “cold” state in the normal process 
sequence when the primary circuit c oolant quality indicators reach the values of the 
third deviation level specified in Table D.1. 
D.1.3.4 If one or more diagnostic indicators of coolant quality deviate from the 
check levels specified in Table D.1, it is necessary to search for and elimina te the 
causes of deviation.  
The duration of the deviation of diagnostic indicators - no more than 7 days. 
If it is impossible to eliminate the causes of deviation of diagnostic parameters 
of the primary circuit coolant, it is necessary to reduce the unit capacity to ≤ 30 % 
Nnom.

D.1.7 Actions in case of deviation of rated and diagnostic indicators of primary 
circuit coolant quality when RP is in the “hot” state, in “reaching MCPL” state and at 
power < 30% Nnom

“reaching MCPL” state and at power < 30 % Nnom in case of deviation of one or 
several rated indicators given in Table D.3 within the first level shall not exceed 24 
hours from the moment of deviation registration.

indicators within 24 hours, change over the Unit to the “cold” state.

of the coolant within 7 days, the unit shall be transferred to the “cold” state in the 
normal process sequence. 
D.1.8 Unit operation in the “cooldown ”, “cold”, “shutdown for repair”, 
“refueling” states 
D.1.8.1 A day before the start of RP cooldown, ammonia and hydrazine 
hydrate injection from the KBD reagent supply system to the primary circuit coolant, 
to the makeup water of the primary circuit is sto pped in order to reduce the hydrogen 
concentration in the coolant to a value not lower than 1.3 mg/dm 3. The reference 
level for the ammonia concentration in the primary circuit coolant is not set. 
The introduction of hydrazine hydrate into make -up water is  allowed only in 
case of exceeding the reference level of oxygen concentration in make -up water, in 
an amount ensuring no more than twice its excess in relation to the oxygen 
concentration. 
D.1.8.2 During RP cooldown the primary circuit coolant is cleaned by filters of 
the KBE50-60 low-temperature primary circuit coolant purification system until the 
forced circulation stops. 
D.1.8.3 During RP shutdown with subsequent decompression of the primary 
circuit equipment during cooldown, the primary circuit coolant is degassed due to the 
operation of the makeup water deaerator, water exchange and gas blow-offs. 
[PAGE 351]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1  RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001  
Version 2  
Continuation of Appendix D 
349 
Decompression of the primary circuit is allowed after reducing the 
concentration of dissolved hydrogen to 0.5 mg/dm3 or less. 
D.1.8.4 During the Unit cooldo wn, the dissolved hydrogen concentration and 
the dissolved oxygen concentration in the primary circuit coolant and makeup water 
shall be monitored at least once a shift until the dissolved hydrogen concentration in 
the primary circuit coolant is equal to 0 .5 mg/dm 3 or less. Reference levels of 
dissolved oxygen concentration in the primary circuit coolant are not established. 
If the concentration of dissolved hydrogen in the primary circuit coolant 
increases more than 0.5 mg/dm 3, additional degassing of the primary circuit coolant 
shall be performed due to the actuation of the makeup deaerator in the steam mode 
with a simultaneous increase in the primary circuit blowdown. 
Perform monitoring of hydrogen concentration in the steam phase from the 
upper PRZ part with frequency of at least once a shift when performing Unit 
cooldown after reaching the value of dissolved hydrogen concentration in the primary 
circuit coolant less than or equal to 0.5  mg/dm3 and when the Unit is in the 
“cooldown” state. Reference level of hydrogen concentration is 2% (volumetric). 
The concentration of dissolved hydrogen and the concentration of dissolved 
oxygen in the primary circuit coolant shall be monitored at least once a shift when the 
Unit is in the “cold” state. Reference levels of dissolved oxygen concentration in the 
primary circuit coolant are not established. 
If it is impossible to take a sample of the primary circuit coolant from the 
reactor vessel, the sample shall be taken from the head of the JNA system pumps. 
D.1.8.5 In t he “cold” state of the Unit, the concentration of boric acid in the 
primary circuit coolant shall be at least the steady-state concentration and provide the 
reactor sub-criticality of at least 2% (excluding CPS CR submerged into the core).  
The concentration of boric acid shall be in the range of 16-20 g/dm3 in the Unit 
“refueling” and “shutdown for repair” states or when performing nuclear -hazardous 
works. 
D.1.8.6 Diagnostic indicators of coolant quality in the “cold” state and in the 
“shutdown for repair”  state, water of fuel pool and RVI inspection cavities in the 
“refueling” state (as well as fuel pool water in all other states of the Unit) shall meet 
the requirements specified in Table D.4.

D.1.9 Unit start -up from th e “cold” state after “refueling” or “shutdown for 
repair” states 
D.1.9.1 Initial filling of the primary circuit before core loading after process 
operations related to full core unloading or repair works is performed by boric acid 
solution with quality specified in Table D.5.1.

D.1.9.2 After the start of forced circulation into the primary circuit coolant at a 
coolant temperature of 60 -80 ºС above zero, a potassium hydroxide solution shall be 
injected from the KBD system until the potassium ion concentration in the primary 
circuit coolant is within the range of 15-20 mg/dm3. Stop dosing potassium hydroxide 
when the concentration of potassium ions in the primary circuit coolant reaches this 
range. 
D.1.9.3 After heat-up of the primary circuit coolant to 80-90 ºС above zero, the 
oxygen concentration is reduced due to  the injection of hydrazine hydrate into the 
primary circuit from the KBD chemical reagents supply to primary circuit coolant 
[PAGE 353]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1  RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001  
Version 2  
Continuation of Appendix D 
351 
system in an amount providing two to three times its excess in relation to the oxygen 
concentration. 
The injection of hydrazine hy drate shall be continued until the oxygen 
concentration in the coolant decreases to the values   regulated in Table D.3. 
D.1.9.4  The primary circuit coolant temperature increase more than 120 °С 
above zero is allowed after the concentration of dissolved  oxygen in the coolant 
decreases to 0.02 mg/dm3 and below. 
The oxygen concentration in the coolant shall not exceed 0.02 mg/dm 3 when 
the temperature of the primary circuit coolant reaches 150 °C above zero.  
If the above value is exceeded, the temperature in the primary circuit shall be 
stabilized and the hydrazine hydrate injection shall be continued in a stoichiometric 
ratio to the actual oxygen concentration until the oxygen content in the coolant 
decreases not more than 0.02 mg/dm3. 
D.1.9.5 During Unit heat-up, the concentration of dissolved hydrogen and the 
concentration of dissolved oxygen in the primary circuit coolant and makeup water 
shall be checked at least once a shift. Reference levels of dissolved hydrogen 
concentration in the primary circuit coolant and in makeup water are not established. 
During Unit heat -up, the hydrogen concentration in the vapor phase from the 
upper part of the PRZ shall be checked at least once a shift. Reference level of 
hydrogen concentration is 2% (volumetric). If it is  impossible to take a sample of the 
primary circuit coolant from the reactor vessel, the sample shall be taken from the 
head of the JNA system pumps. When testing the containment, it is necessary to 
monitor the concentration of dissolved hydrogen in the pr imary circuit coolant and 
hydrogen in the vapor phase from the upper part of the PRZ with a frequency of at 
least once a shift. 
D.1.9.6 Saturation of MBF anion -exchange bed of the KBE50 -60 low -
temperature primary circuit coolant purification system with bo ric acid is performed 
immediately before the primary circuit water exchange due to its absorption from the 
primary circuit coolant. 
D.1.9.7 The primary circuit coolant quality standards shall comply with the 
requirements of Table D.3 when the Unit is brought to the “reaching MCPL” state. 
D.1.9.8 Cation -exchange bed of the operating MBF is changed over to the 
ammonia-potassium form by dosing ammonia and potassium hydroxide solution 
(КОН) from the KBD chemical reagents supply to primary circuit coolant system of 
the Rooppur NPP. 
D.1.9.9 Dosing of zinc acetate solution depleted by 4Zn isotope (less than 1%) 
to the coolant is performed from the KBD system after RP reaches the “reactor at 
MCPL” state. 
D.1.9.10 Filters of the KBE primary circuit coolant purification system shall 
operate with continuous flow rate.

For preparation of boric acid solutions for filling the primary circuit, fuel pools, 
safety system tanks and for refueling, boric acid may be used, the quality of which 
shall meet the following requirements: 
- Boric acid mass fraction - not less than 99.9%. 
- Mass fraction of sulphates - not more than 0.0005%. 
- Mass fraction of chlorides - not more than 0.0001%. 
- Mass fraction of iron - not more than 0.0002%. 
- Mass fraction of heavy metals (Pb) - not more than 0.0005%. 
- Atomic fraction of 10В isotope in boron isotope mixture in boric acid - at least 
19.6%. 
Mass fraction of silicic acid dioxide (in terms of Si032) - not more than 0.001

emergency core cooling system, in the s econd stage accumulators of the JNG10 -40 
passive core flooding system, in the boron solution storage tanks of the FAL system, 
in the tanks of purified boron concentrate of the KBC40-60 system and in the tanks of 
the JND emergency boron injection system, in  the tanks of the FAK10 -20 fuel pool 
cooling system reagents solution inventory shall be performed before Unit start -up 
after PPM, as well as after filling and additional filling. 
Continuous monitoring of the 10В content in the primary circuit coolant (reactor 
and pressurizer) is provided using automatic analyzers. 
D.2  The requirements for WC standards of the secondary circuit of the NPP 
Unit are established in accordance with the “Standards of water chemistry o f the 
secondary circuit. 10JAA-MEC0029 523D3” developed by OKB GIDROPRESS for 
RP V-523 of Rooppur NPP. 
Appendix D shall be corrected based on the obtained results of analysis of pilot 
commercial operation for the secondary circuit WC and brought into compliance with 
the requirements of the final version of 10JAA-MEC0028 523D3. 
D.2.1 General provisions 
D.2.1.1 The requirements to the quality of the secondary circuit working 
medium are established: 
- when putting the Unit into operation; 
- during start-up after shutdown and during Unit operation at power levels Nnom 
≤ 50%; 
- at Unit operation at power levels Nnom > 50%. 
D.2.1.2 Secondary circuit water chemistry shall provide: 
reduction of erosion -corrosion processes of equipment and pipelines of the 
secondary circuit; 
- Reducing the rate of corrosion product deposits formation on the heat -
exchange surfaces of SG and secondary circuit equipment; 
[PAGE 358]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1  RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001  
Version 2  
Continuation of Appendix D 
356 
- limiting the concentration of corrosion products and corrosive -active 
impurities in the make-up water of SG; 
- minimum achievable volume of discharges with concentration of impurities 
contained in them not exceeding the maximum permissible concentration for water 
bodies. 
Alkaline ethanolamine reducing WC with correction treatment of feedwater 
and condensate with ethanol amine, ammonia and hydrazine hydrate is provided for 
the secondary circuit. 
D.2.1.3 Quality indicators of the working medium are divided into rated and 
diagnostic. Ranges of permissible values, as well as deviations from ranges of 
permissible values are es tablished for rated indicators. Reference levels are set for 
diagnostic indicators. 
D.2.1.3.1  The rated indicators comprise the indicators, compliance with 
which ensures the minimum corrosion rates of structural materials when putting the 
Unit into operation and during commercial operation, the minimum contamination of 
SG heat exchange surfaces, the turbine flow path and the secondary circuit 
equipment, and the maintenance of which in permissible values ensures the design 
life of safe and reliable operation of the secondary circuit equipment. 
D.2.1.3.2  Diagnostic indicators comprise indicators that additionally inform 
the NPP personnel about the effectiveness of measures to ensure the cleanliness of 
the internal surfaces of the secondary circuit equipment  and pipelines during start-up 
and adjustment operations, about the correctness of water chemistry and operation of 
process systems for ensuring water chemistry and about the reasons for changes in 
the rated indicators or deterioration of WC. 
D.2.1.3.3  Deviations of rated indicators are divided into levels. The range of 
deviations of indicators from the established values, the state and permissible 
operation time of the Unit are established for each level. 
Counting of Unit operation time with deviations of  rated indicators of steam 
generator working medium quality (feedwater and blowdown water) starts from the 
moment of deviation registration. 
Deviations of diagnostic parameters of SG feedwater quality (increase of iron 
concentration and decrease of pH valu e) lead to increase of rate of formation of 
corrosion product deposits on SG heat exchange surfaces, which in turn intensifies 
corrosion processes of heat exchange pipes metal. 
In case of deviations of rated and diagnostic indicators of feedwater, blowdown 
water and SG steam quality, the causes of deviations shall be found and eliminated. 
Deviation of diagnostic indicators from the reference levels does not impose 
limitations on the state of Unit operation. 
D.2.1.4  Disturbances of water chemistry are: 
- achievement of limit values by one or more rated indicators of SG feedwater 
or blowdown water quality that correspond to the second deviation level at the 
[PAGE 359]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1  RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001  
Version 2  
Continuation of Appendix D 
357 
“Power start -up” stage and when the Unit operates at power levels ≤ 50% Nnom 
given in Tables D.14 and D.15, and the third deviation level at the “Pilot commercial 
operation” stage and when the Unit operates at power levels > 50% Nnom given in 
Tables D.17 and D.18; 
- deviations of rated SG feedwater or blowdown water quality indicators from 
permissible value s not eliminated within the time established by deviation levels, 
given in Tables D.14 and D.15, as well as Tables D.17 and D.18, and non -fulfillment 
of measures to switch to the appropriate levels of action given in this document;  
- deviations of SG feed water quality diagnostic parameters (iron concentration 
and pH value) from controlled levels, not eliminated within 15 days, starting from the 
moment of their detection. 
Data on the value and duration of water chemistry disturbances shall be 
recorded and stored during the SG service life. 
D.2.1.5 The main sources of working medium contamination are:  
- cooling water inflows through leaks of hydraulic part of turbine condensers, 
boilers of heating network, etc.; 
- corrosion of structural materials of the secondary circuit equipment; 
- air suction through leaks of vacuum part of condensate path; 
- additional water downstream the water treatment system; 
- condensate of drain tanks; 
- ion exchange materials and products of their destruction falling into 
feedwater from precoat ion exchange filters of the turbine condensate purification 
system and filters of the SG blowdown water purification system; 
- regeneration solutions and washing water of ion exchange plants in case of 
poor-quality washing of resins after regeneration; 
- leakage of turbine oil through leaks of lubrication system. 
D.2.1.6 The values of the indicators given in this document correspond to the 
results of measurements or recalculation for the standard conditions of the analyzed 
water samples: 
- temperature - 25 °С above zero; 
- pressure - 0.1 MPa. 
D.2.1.7 The quality of reagents and ionites used for WC correction and 
purification of secondary circuit media shall comply with the requirements of 
regulatory documentation. 
D.2.1.8 Scope and frequency o f chemical monitoring of process media of the 
secondary circuit are determined by the “Regulations for chemical monitoring of 
process media at the Rooppur NPP”.

D.2.4 Actions in case of deviation of rated quality indicators of working 
medium during Unit operation at power levels ≤50%Nnom 
D.2.4.1 First level of action. 
Permissible operation duration of the Unit during power ascension ≤50% 
Nnom in case of deviation of rated SG feedwater and/or blowdown water quality 
indicators within the first deviation level given in Tables D.14, D.15 shall not e xceed 
7 days from the moment of deviation detection. 
If it is impossible to identify the causes and eliminate the deviations of rated 
indicators within 7 days, change over the Unit to the “reactor at MCPL” state in the 
normal process sequence. 
The subsequent power buildup of the Unit is possible after elimination of the 
causes of deviation and restoration of the rated parameters of steam generator 
feedwater or blowdown water quality to the permissible values given in Tables D.13. 
D.2.4.2 Second level of action. 
When the steam generator feedwater and blowdown water quality indicators 
reach the values of the second level of deviations specified in Tables D.14, D.15, the 
Unit shall be changed over to the “hot” state in the normal process sequence. 
If it is impo ssible to identify the causes and eliminate deviations of rated 
parameters within 24 hours, change over the Unit to the “cold” state in the normal 
process sequence. 
Subsequent heat -up and power buildup of the Unit is possible only after 
elimination of causes of deviation of rated SG feedwater and blowdown water quality 
values. 
D.2.5 Actions in case of deviation of rated quality indicators of working 
medium during Unit operation at power levels > 50% N nom D. 
2.5.1 First level of action. 
Permissible operatio n time of the Unit at power > 50% Nnom in case of 
deviation of rated steam generator feedwater or blowdown water quality indicators 
within the first deviation level given in Tables D.14, D.15 shall not exceed 7 days 
from the moment of deviation detection. 
If it is impossible to identify the causes and eliminate the deviations of rated 
parameters within 7 days, reduce the power level of the Unit to a value of not more 
than 50% Nnom in the normal process sequence. 
The subsequent power buildup of the Unit more  than 50% Nnom is possible 
after elimination of the causes of deviation and restoration of the rated indicators to 
the permissible values specified in Tables D.17 and D.18. 
D.2.5.2 Second level of action. 
[PAGE 369]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur 
NPP Unit 1  RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001  
Version 2 
Continuation of Appendix D 
367 
Permissible operation duration of the Unit at power   > 50% Nnom in case of 
deviation of rated indicators within the second deviation level given in Tables D.17 
and D.18 shall not exceed 24 h from the moment of deviation detection. 
If it is impossible to identify the causes and eliminate the deviations of r ated 
indicators within 24 h, change over the Unit to the “reactor at MCPL” state in the 
normal process sequence. 
The subsequent power buildup of the Unit is possible only after elimination of 
the causes of deviation and restoration of rated indicators to p ermissible values given 
in Table D.13. 
D.2.5.3 Third level of action. 
When the quality indicators of steam generator feedwater and blowdown water 
reach the values of the third deviation level given in Tables D.17 and D.18, the Unit 
shall be changed over to the “hot” state in the normal process sequence. 
If it is impossible to identify the causes and eliminate deviations of rated 
parameters within 24 hours, change over the Unit to the “cold” state in the normal 
process sequence. 
Subsequent heat -up and power buildup of the Unit is possible only after 
elimination of causes of deviation of rated SG feedwater and blowdown water quality 
values. 
D.2.6 Requirements for water chemistry maintenance systems and methods 
D.2.6.1 Water chemistry maintenance systems comprise: 
 GCF influent water ion-exchange cleaning system; 
 10LCP10 demineralized water system; 
 turbine condenser system; 
 LAA feedwater accumulation and deaeration system; 
 LDF turbine condensate deferrization and demineralization system (UPD); 
 LDB self-contained demineralization plant system; 
 secondary circuit working fluid correction treatment system (10LFN); 
 CFWP pre-start washing system; 
 10LCQ10 SG blowdown and drains system; 
 LCQ50 SG blowdown water purification system; 
 LFG SG chemical washing system over the secondary circuit; 
monitoring of secondary circuit WC indicators is provided by automated 
chemical monitoring systems and laboratory monitoring of samples. The following 
systems of automated and laboratory quality control of the secondary circuit working 
medium are provided for this purpose: 
1) QUH secondary circuit manual sampling system of LDF turbine 
condensate deferrization and demineralization system (UPD); 
2) QUA automated chemical feedwater monitoring system; 
3) QUB automated chemical steam monitoring system; 
[PAGE 370]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur 
NPP Unit 1  RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001  
Version 2 
Continuation of Appendix D 
368 
4) QUC automated chemical monitoring system of condensate systems; 
5) QUG automated chemical monitoring system of LDF turbine 
condensate deferrization and demineralization system (UPD); 
6) QUK SG blowdown water automated chemical monitoring system.  
D.2.6.2 Methods of maintaining water chemistry comprise: 
 - use of demineralized water turbine of required quality when filling the 
secondary circuit, SG and making up the condensers; 
 correction treatment of the secondary circuit working medium; 
 providing tightness of vacuum part of turbine condensers by air and 
hydraulic part by cooling water; 
 feedwater deaeration;  
 treatment of secondary circuit working medium before Unit shutdown for 
preservation of secondary circuit equipment for shutdown period; 
 purification of tur bine condensate on mechanical and ion -exchange filters 
of the turbine condensate deferrization and demineralization system; 
 removal of SG blowdown water from the “salt” compartment, nozzles of 
the housing lower generatrix and “pockets” of SG coolant headers; 
 purification of SG blowdown water on ion -exchange filters of the 
purification system; 
 chemical quality control of the secondary circuit working medium; 
 cleaning of drain condensates; 
 SG chemical washing; 
 use of reagents and filtering materials of proper quality; 
 pre-start washing of condensate and feedwater path with demineralized 
water; 
 SG corrosion protection for the period of RP start -up, shutdown and 
parking. 
D.2.6.3 GCF influent water ion-exchange cleaning system 
Demineralized water obtained at the chemical water treatment plant is used for 
the initial filling of the primary and secondary circuits and makeup of the secondary 
circuit during operation. The plant comprises three legs (two operating, one standby), 
each of which consists of a mechanical f ilter, two stages of sorption filters, a reverse 
osmosis plant, a sodium cation-exchange filter, an electrodeionization plant.  
The quality of demineralized water at the GCF system output shall meet the 
following requirements: 
-  specific electric conductivity, μS/cm, not more than 0.15; 
- silicic acid concentration, mg/dm3, not more than 0.015; 
- total organic carbon concentration, mg/dm3, not more than 0.1. 
D.2.6.4 LCP10 demineralized water system

D.2.6.4.1 The LCP10 system provides demineralized water su pply for primary 
filling of primary and secondary circuit systems and secondary circuit makeup.  
D.2.6.4.2 The LCP10 demineralized water system provides storage of 
demineralized water required for NPP Unit operation in all operation modes. 
The 10LCP01BB001, 10LCP02BB001 demineralized water storage tanks shall 
be protected by carbon dioxide from air. 
D.2.6.4.3 Diagnostic quality indicators of demineralized water shall meet the 
following requirements: 
-  electric conductivity not more than 1.2 μS/cm; 
-  pH value from 5.5 to 8.0; 
-    chloride-ion concentration is not more than 0.005 mg/dm3; 
-    silicic acid concentration is not more than 0.015 mg/dm3; 
-    total organic carbon concentration is not more than 0.1 mg/dm3. 
D.2.6.4.4 The specific el ectric conductivity is not more than 1.2 μS/cm when 
filling the secondary circuit, performing washing and hydraulic tests of SG and other 
equipment, as well as makeup of the secondary circuit with a flow rate exceeding 1% 
of nominal RP steam capacity. 
D.2.6.5 The MAG turbine condenser system and LAA feedwater deaeration 
system 
D.2.6.5.1 The MAG and LAA systems provide oxygen concentration in turbine 
condensate not more than 0.02 mg/dm 3 and in feedwater not more than 0.005 
mg/dm3. 
D.2.6.6 LDF turbine condens ate deferrization and demineralization system 
(unit demineralization unit) 
D.2.6.6.1 Deferrization and demineralization system provides purification of 
turbine condensate from suspended and dissolved corrosion products and corrosive 
impurities to provide the required quality of SG feedwater and blowdown water. 
D.2.6.6.2 Deferrization and demineralization system comprises five cartridge 
filters (capacity of each is 950 m 3/h), five H -cation exchange filters and five MBF 
(capacity of the each is 900 m3/h).  
D.2.6.6.3 The UDP is fully or partially put into operation during Unit start -up 
after combining the feedwater and condensate paths to provide the quality of SG 
feedwater and blowdown water. The need for full or partial connection of the UDP is 
determined by the turbine condensate quality.  
During start -up and during Unit operation at power level 50% Nnom, the 
LDF system purifies 100% of turbine condensate flow rate on cartridge filters (two 
filters in operation, three on standby) and purifies 100% of turbine  condensate flow 
rate on H -cation exchange filters and MBF (two filters in operation, three on 
standby).  
[PAGE 372]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur 
NPP Unit 1  RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001  
Version 2 
Continuation of Appendix D 
370 
Cartridges with a maximum filtration rating of 90 μm shall be used in cartridge 
filters when performing pre-start washing of CFWP.  
When the unit is operating at power, cartridge filters should use cartridges with 
filtration rating of 10 or 40 microns (determined by the condition of the circuit WC as 
a whole and as per operating experience).  
D.2.6.6.4 During Unit operation at power > 50% Nnom, the LDF system 
purifies 100% of turbine condensate flow rate on cartridge filters (four filters in 
operation, one on standby) and purifies 100% of turbine condensate flow rate on H -
cation exchange filters and two MBF (four filters in operation, one on standby).  
When the unit is operating at power, cartridge filters should use cartridges with 
filtration rating of 10 or 40 microns (determined by the condition of the circuit WC as 
a whole and as per operating experience).  
H-cation exchange filters and MBF of the LDF turbine condensate purification 
system can be taken out of operation for regeneration when the Unit opera tes at 
power > 50% Nnom.  
Connection of H -cation exchange filters and MBF is performed in case of 
deviation of SG feedwater and blowdown water quality indicators from the rated 
values.  
D.2.6.6.5 H -cation exchange filters shall be loaded with strong acid c ation 
exchanger.  
MBF shall be loaded with a mixture of strongly acid cation exchanger and 
strongly basic anion exchanger in a ratio of 1:2. 
H-cation exchange filters can be taken out of operation for regeneration.  
MBF shall operate without regeneration.  
The value of electric conductivity downstream  Н-cation-exchange filter should 
not exceed 0.3 μS/cm. If the value of specific electric conductivity downstream  Н -
cation-exchange filter exceeds 0.3 μS/cm, the filter should be taken out for 
regeneration. 
The value of electric conductivity downstream MBF shall not exceed 0.2 
μS/cm.  
D.2.6.6.6 When the MBF is connected after downtime on standby, pre -start 
washing shall be performed to the value of specific electric conductivity at the MBF 
outlet not more than 0.2 μS/cm. 
Regeneration of ionic-exchange bed of mechanical filter and  cation -exchange 
bed of MBF is carried out with 4% sulfuric acid solution. Regeneration of the cation -
exchange bed of MBF is carried out with 4% caustic soda solution. 
D.2.6.7 LDB self-contained demineralization plant system 
D.2.6.7.1 The LDB self -contained demineralization plant system performs 
purification of DCT water.  
The following media are supplied to the DCT: water downstream the CFWP 
pre-start washing system, water after equipmen t assembly washing, unbalanced 
[PAGE 373]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur 
NPP Unit 1  RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001  
Version 2 
Continuation of Appendix D 
371 
waters of the second circuit, working medium of the secondary circuit when 
emptying and taking the Unit equipment out of service for repair, medium from the 
drain water tank of the turbine hall in case of non -compliance with the water 
chemistry requirements.  
D.2.6.7.2 The LDB self -contained demineralization plant system provides 
purification of various media in terms of mechanical impurities and ionic impurities 
in some cases with a significant content of ethanolamine and ammonia. 
D.2.6.7.3 The LDB system consists of series -connected mechanical (H­cation 
exchange) filter and MBF. 
Corrosion products in the form of dispersed and colloidal impurities are 
removed on the H -cation exchange filter. Cleaning from ion impurities is per formed 
at the MBF.  
D.2.6.7.4 The electric conductivity at the LDB system self -contained 
demineralization plant shall not exceed 0.3 μS/cm.  
The LDB system filters shall be taken out of operation for regeneration if the 
electric conductivity exceeds 0.3 μS/cm.  
D.2.6.7.5 The electric conductivity of H -cationized water sample of the drain 
tank of the turbine building drain system shall not exceed 1.5 μS/cm. 
Regeneration of ionic-exchange bed of mechanical filter and  cation -exchange 
bed of MBF is carried out with 4% sulfuric acid solution. Regeneration of the cation-
exchange bed of MBF is carried out with 4% caustic soda solution. 
D.2.6.8 Secondary circuit working fluid correction treatment system LFN 
D.2.6.8.1 Corrective treatment of working medium of the se condary circuit is 
performed by dosing ethanolamine, hydrazine hydrate and ammonia in order to 
reduce erosion and corrosion wear of the CFWP equipment and pipelines and steam 
path, create recovery properties of working medium and maintain pH value and 
concentration of dissolved oxygen in SG condensate and feedwater.  
D.2.6.8.2 Injection of ethanolamine, hydrazine hydrate and ammonia is 
performed by the secondary circuit WC correction system with the required 
concentration and flow rate that provide the regu lated pH value and concentration of 
ethanolamine, hydrazine and ammonia in SG feedwater in all Unit operation modes.  
Ethanolamine, hydrazine hydrate and ammonia shall be dosed into the suction 
header of the auxiliary feed pumps before connecting the turbine plant. 
After the turbine plant is connected, ethanolamine, hydrazine hydrate and 
ammonia shall be dosed into the suction header of the second stage condensate 
pumps. 
D.2.6.8.3 The LFN secondary circuit water chemistry correction system 
comprises: 
-   ethanolamine solution dosing assembly; 
-   hydrazine solution dosing assembly; 
-   ammonia solution dosing assembly.
