D.2.6.9  LCA90 condensate and feedwater path pre-start washing system 
D.2.6.9.1 LCA90 pre -start washing system is designed to remove sludge a nd 
corrosion products of structural materials from heat exchange equipment and 
pipelines of CFWP before water supply to SG during post-installation start-ups, start-
ups after repairs and shutdowns lasting more than three days. 
D.2.6.9.2 Preliminary flushin g of the feed path of the CDW is carried out at 
operation of AFWP through pipelines of additional recirculation of AFWP with the 
possibility of including two sections in the flushing path: 
- of pipelines between the HPH and the SG supply unit (with reverse  water 
supply); 
- of feed water pipelines (with water supply in working direction). 
Flushing water is heated to 100 °С above zero in the deaerator. 
When washing the feedwater path, water exchange is performed with the 
supply of chemically demineralized water to the deaerator and the removal of part of 
the water to the drain system of the turbine building through the turbine drainage 
expansion tank.  
D.2.6.9.4 CFWP washing is carried out by CDW at operation of CEDP -I, 
CEDP-II and FWP for recirculation throug h the circuit, including: condenser,  UDP 
bypass, LPH -1,2,3,4, deaerator, HPH, HPH bypass, flushing pipeline, condenser. 
Washing water shall be heated to 120 °С above zero in the deaerator. 
When the iron concentration in the circuit is stabilized, a partial water 
exchange should be carried ou t at the highest possible flow rate. When water 
temperature in the deaerator exceeds 90 °C, polluted water shall be discharged to the 
DCT through the drainage expander of the turbine hall.  
When the iron concentration is less than 0.3 mg/dm 3, the temperatu re in the 
washing circuit decreases to 40 °C above zero, the CFWP washing is continued with 
the connection of UDP system filters. The specific electric conductivity of H -
cationized feedwater sample is not more than 1.0 μS/cm, iron concentration - not 
more than 0.02 mg/dm3 are washing completion criterion. 
D.2.6.10 LCQ10-40 steam generator blowdown and drains system  
D.2.6.10.1 Continuous and periodic blowdown is performed by LCQ10 -40 to 
the LCQ50 SG blowdown water purification system to clean the blowdown w ater 
from soluble and insoluble impurities in order to maintain the quality of SG 
blowdown water.  
The LCQ10-40 SG blowdown and drains system is also designed for partial or 
complete SG drainage.  
Removal of blowdown water of each SG via continuous and per iodic 
blowdown lines is arranged in such a way that the effect of blowdown of individual 
SGs on each other as well as clogging of blowdown lines with sludge is excluded.  
D.2.6.10.2 Continuous blowdown of each SG by LCQ10 -40 is performed from 
the “salt” compartment of the cold end with a flow rate of up to 15 t/h and from the 
[PAGE 375]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur 
NPP Unit 1  RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001  
Version 2 
Continuation of Appendix D 
373 
blowdown lines from the lower generatrix of the SG housing and “pockets” of 
headers for heating up the blowdown lines with a flow rate of up to 5 t/h from each 
line.  
D.2.6.10.3 The fl ow rate of periodic blowdown from the “salt” compartment 
shall be up to 30 t/h, from the blowdown lines from the lower generatrix of SG 
housing through each or all Dn50 nozzles shall be up to 25 t/h, from the “pockets” of 
headers - up to 10 t/h through eac h Dn32 sleeve and up to 20 t/h through four Dn32 
sleeves.  
The total blowdown flow rate from each SG with simultaneous blowdown of 
all SG shall be up to 35 t/h. The SG blowdown system shall provide the total flowrate 
of blowdown water from four SG in the m ode of connection of periodic SG 
blowdown to 140 t/h.  
The flow rates of periodic SG blowdown from the blowdown lines from the 
lower generatrix of SG housing and “pockets” of headers, the frequency and duration 
of periodic blowdown actuation are determined  by the SG Operation manual and the 
SG Blowdown system operation regulations.  
D.2.6.10.4 When the quality of blowdown water from the “salt” compartments 
deviates from the rated values, the flow rate of blowdown from the “salt” SG 
compartments shall be increased to the maximum possible.  
Disconnection of continuous blowdown from the “salt” compartment of at least 
one SG due to a fault of the blowdown system is allowed for no more than 8 hours.  
If it is impossible to restore the SG blowdown system operabili ty, the Unit 
shall be changed over to the “cold” state in the normal process sequence. 
D.2.6.11 LCQ50 steam generator blowdown water purification system 
D.2.6.11.1 The LCQ50 steam generator blowdown water purification system 
provides SG blowdown water puri fication from suspended and dissolved corrosion 
products and corrosive impurities and its return to the secondary circuit. 
The entire flow of SG blowdown water before returning to the secondary 
circuit is purified on ion -exchange filters of the LCQ50 SG bl owdown water 
purification system.  
D.2.6.11.2 The LCQ50 system consists of two equivalent groups of equipment 
(operating and standby) connected to the combined blowdown line of four SG. 
In normal operation mode, one group is in operation and provides purge  water 
purification of four SGs with flow rate up to 140 m 3/h, the second group is on 
standby. 
Each group comprises H+ -cation exchange filter (mechanical filter) and MBF. 
H-cation exchange filters can be taken out of operation for regeneration. MBF is not  
regenerated. Regeneration of the ionic -exchange bed  of the H -cation exchange filter 
is carried out with 5% nitric acid solutions. 
The LCQ50 system operates over the header circuit: all filters get disabled for 
regeneration and connected to operation independently of each other.  
[PAGE 376]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur 
NPP Unit 1  RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001  
Version 2 
Continuation of Appendix D 
374 
D.2.6.11.3 The quality of purified SG blowdown water returned to the 
secondary circuit shall provide the working medium quality.  
The value of electric conductivity of purified SG blowdown water downstream 
LCQ50 shall not exceed 0.3 μS/cm and the pH value shall be at least 6.0. 
D.2.6.12. The LFG steam generator chemical washing system  
D.2.6.12.1 The LFG SG chemical washing system is designed for preparation 
and supply of washing solution to SG during SG washing.  
SG chemical washes are performed to remove product deposits  
corrosion from heat exchange surfaces and sludge from SG housing and 
blowdown lines.  
The need for chemical washing of the steam generator is determined by the 
actual degree of contamination of heat exchange pipe s determined in the previous 
PPM.  
D.2.6.12.2 Permissible value of specific contamination of heat exchange pipes 
of the steam generator shall not exceed 100 g/m 2 (thickness not more than 25 μm) in 
any controlled area.  
SG chemical washes are performed in accordance with the requirements of the 
SG Operation manual.  
D.2.6.13 Treatment of working medium before Unit shutdown for preservation 
of condensate and feedwater path for shutdown period  
D.2.6.13.1 In case of short-term Unit shutdowns for a period of up to 3 days or 
up to 15 days without decompression of equipment, treatment of working medium for 
preservation of CFWP may not be performed.  
D.2.6.13.2 When the Unit is shut down for a period exceeding the one given in 
Item D.2.6.13.1 for CFWP preservation, treatment of the working medium for 24 -48 
hours with ethanolamine and hydrazine hydrate with maintenance of ethanolamine 
concentration from 3.0 to 3.5 mg/dm 3 and hydrazine concentration of at least 0.01 
mg/dm3 in feedwater shall be performed by the LDN secondary circuit water 
chemistry correction system. Ethanolamine and hydrazine hydrate shall be supplied 
to the second stage condensate pump headers.  
D.2.6.13.3 Equipment and pipelines, which are not repaired, may be left filled 
with working medium containing ethanolamine and hydrazine hydrate after treatment 
according to Item D.2.6.13.2 during shutdown.  
After repair, the equipment shall be filled with demineralized water, the quality 
of which shall meet the requirements of Item D.2.6.13.3.  
D.2.6.13.4 It is allowed to increase the pH value in the SG blowdown water to 
9.9 during the working medium treatment with ethanolamine and hydrazine hydrate.

Algorithms for control of power and distribution of reactor power density 
 
F.1  Power density monitoring 
Core power density is characterized by scalar values and ar rays of numbers - 
distributions. Distributions are set in the core cells (j) or (i,j), where j is the FA 
number, i is the number of the elevation layer (from the core bottom). 
Power density parameters: 
N - current reactor power (provided by MCDS). 
Nnom - nominal reactor power (3200 MW). 
Nperm - reactor power, maximum permissible at the current state of 
equipment. 
Qlijk - maximum linear thermal load on fuel element with number k in the core 
cell (i,j), W/cm (provided by MCDS). 
Qlim perm - maximum permissible value of linear thermal load on fuel element 
in i -th elevation layer for three groups of fuel cells in FA - for central (m=1) and 
peripheral (m=2) FE and for GFE (m=3). 
Kvij - relative power density in the core cell (i,j) equal to the power density 
ratio in this cell to the average power (provided by MCDS). 
Kvij perm - maximum permissible value of Kvij at power Nperm (MCDS is 
provided for each cell of the core4). 
Kv = maxKvij - power density irregularity factor by core volume (provided by 
MCDS). 
Kqj - relative power of power density of jth FA equal to the ratio of its power 
to the average FA power (provided by MCDS). 
Kq=max Kqj - power density irregularity factor by FA (provided by MCDS). 
AO - instantaneous axial offset corresponding to the current xenon di stribution 
(provided by MCDS) 
, 
where NU and NL are the current power values of the upper and lower halves of 
the core, respectively;  
N=NU+NL. 
AO* - equilibrium axial offset corresponding to the equilibrium (stationary) 
distribution of xenon (provided by MCDS, see Item F.5.1).  
Limitation of integral power of core power density: 
NNperm. 
Limitation of relative power density at power NNperm:

Kqj and Kq parameters are informative. 
F.2  Control actions 
F.2.1 Control rod (CR) movement. 
F.2.1.1 CR can move at an operating speed of 2 cm/s, individually or as part of 
CR groups (Figure F.2), as well as fall under the impact of gravity. The minimum 
movement step of CR is 2 cm. When moving at operating speed, the limit upper and 
bottom CR p ositions are respectively on the upper (ULS) and bottom (BLS) limit 
switches, the lower limit position is on the lower abutment stop (LAS) when CR 
drop.  
F.2.1.2 Change of CR position in individual and group modes provides change 
of power and power density  distribution. CR extraction/submersion provides 
increase/decrease of reactor power and increase/decrease of power of FA in which 
CR move and their surrounding environment, as well as increase/decrease of local 
power density power of fuel element sections (FA/GFE) near the lower boundary of 
CR absorbing rods. 
F.2.1.3  The movement of the lower boundary of the CR absorbing rods in 
the direction of the middle of the core height reduces the offset value, the movement 
in the direction from the middle increases the offset value. 
F.2.1.4     CR position change in individual mode is performed by means of 
“INDIVIDUAL CONTROL” key 
F.2.1.5  CR groups position change is performed by operator manually 
using “GROUP CONTROL” key or automatically under APC -R control. The 
operator command is performed at simultaneous receipt of signals from operator and 
APC-R. 
F.2.1.6  Movement of one group without motion transfer and movement of 
groups with motion transfer are provided in manual and automatic modes. Motion 
transfer occurs at 50% or 100% of the core height (fuel column), respectively, when 
groups move up and down. 
F.2.1.7    Four “control” groups with the following numbers are used for 
control in normal operation: 9, 10, 11, 12. The standard sequence shall be maintained 
when control groups move: Н9≥Н10≥ Н11≥ Н12. 
F.2.1.8 It is allowed to reduce the reactor power by submerging the control 
groups without limiting their final position, after which groups 9, 10 and 11 shall be 
[PAGE 382]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur 
NPP Unit 1  RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001  
Version 2 
Continuation of Appendix F 
380 
removed to the ULS and group 12 shall be changed over to the per missible position 
interval within 12 hours. 
F.2.1.9  It is allowed to submerge control groups for no more than 12 
hours, subject to the following limitations, to suppress axial xenon oscillations when 
operating at a constant power level: Н10≥90%, H11≥80%, H12≥70%. 
F.2.1.10  Automatic reactor unloading by sequential submersion of groups 
with motion transfer is provided by PP-1 signal. 
2.1.11  One CR belonging to the control group may be submerged for no 
more than 6 hours to suppress or prevent xenon oscillations. 
F.2.1.12   Accelerated automatic reactor unloading due to the drop of the APP 
group is provided by APP signal. 
F.2.1.13   The reactor is shut down due to the drop of all groups by APP signal. 
F.2.1.14   Group and individual control system (GICS). 
F.2.1.14.1 GICS provides position indication and CR motion control by 
means of control rods and necessary indication means on the MCR operator control 
panel, as well as virtual means on the CPS EES/MCDS APC-R monitor. 
F.2.1.14.2 Indication of CR position. CR position, vertical distance from the 
lower boundary of the absorber to the bottom boundary of the core (fuel column) are 
provided in centimeters and as a percentage of the core height (Figure F.2). 
The control and selection unit (hereinafter referred to as CSB) is used to 
generate commands for automatic control of CR groups, CR selection and movement 
with the help of manual individual and group controls. General view of CSB unit is 
shown in Figure F.8. 
F.2.1.14.3 The CSB is a man-machine interface of CR control using physical 
buttons and keys to perform the following operations: 
 selection of CR group for manual control “GROUP SELECTION”; 
 selection of “MT” motion transfer mode from group to group; 
 confirmation of selection of CR group or “SET” mode with motion 
transfer from group to group; 
 selection of CR groups for automatic control by ARPC “ARPC GROUP 
SELECTION”; 
 ARPC “ARPC” operation start; 
 selection of mode of set neutron power maintenance (“N” mode); 
 selection of mode of MSH steam pressure maintenance (“T” mode); 
 selection of mode for steam pressure maintenance in MSH with wide dead 
band (“TPFC” mode); 
 control of CR groups movement “GROUP CONTROL”; 
 control of CR movement in individual mode “INDIVIDUAL CONTROL”

F.2.1.14.5 Selection of automatic group control mode 
1) ARPC actuation/disabling.  
2) When using the “ARPC” button, ARPC actuation permission conditions 
are checked, accompanied by uniform flashing of button light indication. Confirmed 
actuation of ARPC is acco mpanied by automatic setting of ARPC to “N” mode and 
actuation of “МТ” automatic group control with motion transfer, which will be 
indicated by constant illumination of respective “N” and “MT” buttons. If there is an 
ARPC actuation ban due to any unsatisfa ctory conditions for actuation, the “ARPC” 
button flashing stops in 3 seconds after pressing it. 
Automatic group control gets disabled by pressing the “ARPC” button again. 
After pressing, the light indication of the button signals that the automatic group 
control of uniform flashing is switched off for three seconds and then disabled. 
The “ARPC” button indication gets disabled automatically if ARPC gets 
disabled by APP or PP-1 signal. After stabilization of RP operation mode, ARPC gets 
started automatically in “N” mode with actuation of respective buttons indication. 
3) Selection of “ARPC MODES” APC operation mode. 
ARPC operation mode is changed by pressing one of “N”, “T” or “TPFC” 
operation mode buttons. By pressing the button, the conditions for enabling act uation 
of the selected mode are checked, accompanied by uniform flashing of the light 
indication of the newly selected mode and constant illumination of the previously 
selected modes. When confirming the conditions for changeover, the ARPC 
operation mode i s changed automatically, as evidenced by the constant illumination

of the respective button of the newly selected mode and the absence of indication of 
the previous mode. The flashing of the button light indication stops and the

F.2.1.14.6 Selection of CR group 
1) Manual group control modes. 
A group with the respective number is selected for control without motion 
transfer in the “GROUP SELECTION” area by pressing one of the bu ttons 1 to 12. 
Each pressing of the button in the row is accompanied by flashing light indication of 
the selected button. By pressing the “SET” button, the selection of the group for 
control without motion transfer is confirmed and the selected buttons beg in to be 
highlighted constantly. In this mode it is allowed to select only one CR group for 
control. 
By pressing the “MT” button in the row, with further confirmation by “SET” 
button, manual group control mode with motion transfer is set and “MT” button wi ll 
be illuminated constantly. 
In manual group control mode only one of two modes can be selected - either 
manual group control without motion transfer  (button with group number is pressed) 
or manual group control with motion transfer (“MT” button is press ed). The pressed 
and confirmed button is highlighted, while the previously highlighted button goes off. 
2) Automatic group control modes. 
A group with the respective number is selected for automatic group control 
without motion transfer in the “ARPC GROUP SEL ECTION” area by pressing one 
of the buttons 9 to 12. Each pressing of the button in the row is accompanied by 
flashing light indication of the selected button. By pressing the “SET” button the 
selection of CR group under ARPC control is confirmed and the selected buttons start 
to glow constantly. In this mode, it is allowed to select only one CR group for control 
from ARPC. 
By pressing the “MT” button in the row, with further confirmation by SET 
button, automatic group control mode with motion transfer is s et and the “MT” 
button will illuminate constantly. 
In automatic group control mode, only one of two modes can be selected - 
either automatic group control without motion transfer (button with group number is 
pressed) or automatic group control with motion transmission (“MT” button is 
pressed). The pressed and confirmed button is highlighted, while the previously 
highlighted button goes off.

SELECTION” selection buttons operation 
1) Button selection and change of an unconfirmed button.

Any pressing of CR group selection buttons on CSB unit is confirmed by

of initially selected buttons). At subsequent pressing of “SET” button in the 
respective part of CSB unit, the last selected button is confirmed with actuation of 
constant indication and indication of the previously selected button gets disabled. 
F.2.1.14.8 Controls 
1) INDIVIDUAL CONTROL key. 
It is a mechanical wrench for three positions with self-return to neutral position 
when the force is released (without fixing in limit positions). The key sets the 
command to move the CR selected for individual control down - “DOWN” or up - 
“UP”. 
2) GROUP CONTROL key. 
It is a mechanical wrench for three positions with self-return to neutral position 
when the force is released (without fixing in limit positions). The key sets a command 
to move down - “DOWN” or up - “UP” of CR groups with  or without motion 
transfer. 
F.2.1.14.11 Command priorities. 
GICS equipment implements the following priority of control commands (in 
descending order): 
- EP commands; 
- PP (APP, PP-1, PP-2) commands; 
- individual control commands; 
- manual group control commands; 
- automatic control commands. 
Besides, priority of control commands for CR downward movement over 
control commands for CR upward movement is implemented in each operation mode. 
F.2.2 Water exchange. 
[PAGE 386]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur 
NPP Unit 1  RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001  
Version 2 
Continuation of Appendix F 
384 
Decrease or increase of boric acid concentration  in the primary circuit coolant 
(water exchange) respectively by injection of boric acid distillate or concentrate 
provides respectively increase or decrease of reactor power with insignificant impact 
on power density distribution. The effectiveness of dis tillate injection is reduced to 
zero during the cycle (since it is directly dependent on the concentration of boric acid 
in the coolant). 
F.2.3 Overcompensation of control actions. 
If the reactor power is kept constant, the CR group movement shall be 
compensated by a change in the boric acid concentration or movement of another CR 
group. In the latter case, the groups shall move in opposite directions, while the 
distance of groups changes - the vertical distance between the lower boundary of CR 
absorber (in crease in the distance between two groups causes offset increase, 
decrease in distance - offset decrease). 
F.3. Operator information support. 
F.3.1 The operator uses special information support tools based on the data 
provided on the MCDS monitors on the c urrent state and history of the reactor. The 
RSim program is used as part of MCDS to provide the functions of design monitoring 
and prediction of the reactor state. The formats of information presentation on MCDS 
monitors oriented to the core power density control contain: 
- graphs of reactor power change, instantaneous and equilibrium offset values, 
predicted offset, CR group position, calculated and measured boric acid concentration 
in the coolant, predicted critical boric acid concentration in the coolant; 
- numerical current values of CR control groups position, average inlet 
temperature and coolant heating in the core, reactivity, Kv and Kq values; 
- profile of height power distribution of power density (Kvij values - average 
and maximum over the core, as well as for individual FAs), with a setpoint of 
scheduled limitation; 
- power density power distribution maps - Kqj and Kvij; 
- phase diagrams (Kq-power, Kv-power, offset-power, offset-offset); 
- text messages (tips, recommendations, warnings). 
F.3.2 Fo r the shutdown reactor, the operator is provided with analysis 
information obtained given the progress of xenon and samarium processes in the 
core: 
- current reactivity value (sub-criticality depth); 
- current value of critical concentration of boric acid; 
- current value of start-up boric acid concentration. 
F.3.3 Kv -power diagram is constructed in the axes of power (N) and Kvij 
(Figure F.4). Contain the current phase point, allowable and prohibited areas. A 
separate Kv power diagram is provided for each c ore cell (i,j). Maintaining the phase 
point in the allowable area corresponds to maintaining the permissible values of Kvij. 
F.3.4 Offset power phase diagram (Figure F.5) is constructed in the axes of 
power (N) and instantaneous offset (JSC). Contains opti mal paths, recommended 
[PAGE 387]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur 
NPP Unit 1  RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001  
Version 2 
Continuation of Appendix F 
385 
area, area of allowable power. Moving the phase point along the optimal path 
corresponds to the smallest changes in the local thermal load on fuel elements. 
Maintaining the phase point in the recommended area limits the change in the  local 
load within permissible limits. 
F.3.5 Offset -offset phase diagram (Figure F.6) is constructed in the axes of 
instantaneous (AO) and equilibrium (AO*) offset. The instantaneous offset 
corresponds to the current distribution of xenon concentration in the core. The 
equilibrium offset corresponds to the equilibrium distribution of xenon. The points on 
the diagonal of the diagram (AO=AO*) correspond to the steady states of the reactor. 
The recommended area corresponds to the recommended offset power diagr am area 
for the current power value. 
F.4. Xenon processes. 
F.4.1 Integral xenon processes. 
The change in reactor power causes a transient xenon process related to a 
change in the total number of 135Xe nuclei in the core and a respective reactivity 
change. The availability of an extremum is a characteristic feature of the reactivity 
change at a non -zero initial concentration of xenon. The following main stages of 
xenon transients are distinguished by the nature of the dominant effects: 
- xenon burnup - reactivity increase after power rise ( 135Xe concentration 
decreases due to neutron absorption); 
- poisoning - reactivity decrease immediately after power decrease or after 
power increase and reaching maximum reactivity during xenon burnup ( 35Xe 
concentration increases due to decay of 135I nuclei); 
- de-poisoning - reactivity increase after reaching a minimum during poisoning 
as a result of power decrease (decay of 135Xe nuclei). 
Change of 135Xe concentration is compensated by change of absorber content 
in the co re by water exchange and/or movement of CR groups in order to maintain 
constant power during xenon processes. 
F.4.2 Spatial xenon processes  
Xenon fluctuations of power flux distribution are due to periodic process of 
redistribution of 135Xe nuclei concent ration by core volume. Axial (height) and 
diametrical xenon oscillations are of practical importance for reactor operation. 
F.4.2.1 Axial xenon oscillations. 
F.4.2.1.1 Offset change at constant reactor power and absence of CR motion 
(offset drift) indicate s the availability of axial xenon oscillations. Free xenon 
oscillations (long offset drift) have the character of sinusoidal oscillations of the 
value of instantaneous offset AO relative to the point of the equilibrium offset AO* 
with a period T ~ 28 -30 hours. Free xenon fluctuations attenuate at the beginning of 
the cycle, divergent fluctuations can be observed at the end of the cycle . The offset 
increase/decrease step is called the “ascending”/“descending” phase of axial xenon 
oscillations. 
  
[PAGE 388]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur 
NPP Unit 1  RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001  
Version 2 
Continuation of Appendix F 
386 
F.4.2.1.2 The main causes of axial xenon oscillations: 
- Initial offset perturbation. A positive or negative offset increment (as a result 
of CR groups movement or power change) excites the upward or downward phase of 
the oscillations, respectively. The intensity of the oscillations is directly related to the 
offset increment and time. If an offset perturbation is introduced in the phase with 
existing oscillations, then this increases their intensity. 
Power decrease. Power decrease at constant CPS CR position causes i nitial 
offset increase and upward phase of oscillations. If offset increase is compensated by 
CPS CR group submersion, then initial phase of xenon oscillations is determined by 
initial shape of iodine height distribution. Immediately after power decrease, the 
process of iodine decay and xenon concentration increase dominates, so for the initial 
steady state with negative/positive offset value, power decrease excites the 
ascending/descending phase of xenon oscillations. In the initial availability of xenon 
oscillations, the power decrease leads to an increase in their intensity (maximum - at 
the inflection points of the offset time schedule (AO=AO*), minimum - at the 
extremum points). 
- Power increase. Power increase at constant CPS CR position causes initial  
offset decrease and downward phase of oscillations. Immediately after the increase in 
power, the xenon burnup process dominates, so the phase of xenon oscillations is 
determined by the initial offset change: negative or positive offset increment excites 
the descending or ascending phase of xenon oscillations, respectively. 
F.4.2.2 Diametral xenon oscillations. 
F.4.2.2.1 Asymmetric increase of Kqj in a separate FA group and decrease of 
Kqj in diametrically opposite part of the core at constant reactor power  and absence 
of CR motion indicates availability of diametrical xenon oscillations. 
F.4.2.2.2  Main causes of diametrical xenon oscillations: 
- asymmetric CR movement, in particular, the fall of one CR or the extraction 
of a previously fallen CR; 
- RCP shutdown or actuation. 
F.5. Control algorithms in normal operation conditions. 
F.5.1 Maintaining a constant power level. 
F.5.1.1 In a state with stationary xenon, fuel burnup is automatically 
compensated by the extraction of group 12 under the control of APC -R. The group is 
periodically returned to its initial position in the permissible range (Figure F.3) due to 
distillate injection. It is recommended to maintain the design position of group 12 
90% for efficient use of fuel. 
F.5.1.2 Integral xenon transient p rocesses are compensated by water exchange 
and movement of control groups given the need to control the power density 
distribution. 
F.5.1.3 Offset is maintained within the recommended area of offset power 
diagram, if necessary, xenon oscillations are suppressed (Item 5.3.3). 
[PAGE 389]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur 
NPP Unit 1  RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001  
Version 2 
Continuation of Appendix F 
387 
F.5.2 Power change. 
F.5.2.1 Power change planning. The final state of the reactor is predicted, the 
final position of group 12 is selected, the final steady offset value is determined 
within the recommended area using the RSim program. It is recommended to select 
the endpoint on the offset power diagram near the optimal phase path passing through 
the starting point. 
F.5.2.2 Power change modes. 
F.5.2.2.1 Turbine power change. 
The TG controller (“PO” mode) automatically changes the TG elec tric power 
at a given speed to a set value and the APC -R (“T” mode), while controlling the 
movement of groups, automatically changes the reactor power, while maintaining 
constant steam pressure. 
F.5.2.2.2   Reactor power change. 
Manual mode. When APC -R is off, reactor power is changed due to: water 
exchange, movement of groups, xenon processes. In this case, the TG controller 
(“OR” mode) accordingly changes the electric power, while maintaining a constant 
steam pressure. 
Automatic mode. APC -P in “N” mode du e to the movement of groups 
automatically changes the reactor power at a given speed to a set value. In this case, 
the TG controller (“OR” mode) accordingly changes the electric power, while 
maintaining a constant steam pressure. 
F.5.2.3 Changeover to reduced power level. 
F.5.2.3.1  Reactor power is reduced in manual or automatic mode due to 
submersion of control groups and/or injection of concentrate, as well as due to xenon 
poisoning. 
F.5.2.3.2    Power reduction rate is limited (Table 5.3). 
F.5.2.3.3  In case of power decrease, the offset -power diagram phase point 
going beyond the recommended area is allowed for not more than 12 hours. 
F.5.2.3.4  After reaching the set power level, groups are extracted in the 
standard sequence at the poisoning stage (Item F.2.1.7) using the APC-R. The groups 
movement is corrected by switching APC -R to control the selected group, as well as 
using the “GROUP CONTROL” key and water exchange while suppressing xenon 
offset oscillations and ensuring the return of the offset powe r diagram phase point to 
the recommended area. The offset is stabilized at the set final value at the de -
poisoning stage. 
F.5.2.4 Changeover to increased power level. 
F.5.2.4.1 Power increase is performed by extraction of groups (manual or 
automatic mode) or injection of distillate (manual mode) and group 12 is extracted to 
position not higher than 95%. The reactor can also be loaded due to the processes of 
xenon burnup and decomposition. 
[PAGE 390]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur 
NPP Unit 1  RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001  
Version 2 
Continuation of Appendix F 
388 
F.5.2.4.2 It is prohibited to extract groups or individual CRs simult aneously 
with distillate injection at power increase in manual mode. 
F.5.2.4.3   Power increase rate is limited (Table 5.4). 
F.5.2.4.4  If the current offset power diagram point was originally in the 
recommended area, it shall remain within the recommended  area during the power 
increase. If the current point was originally outside the recommended area, it shall be 
moved to the recommended area during the power increase from the initial value to 
the 0.8ΔN level (where ΔN is the power change). 
F.5.2.4.5  After reaching the set power level, offset is s tabilized within the 
recommended area of the offset power diagram using xenon oscillation suppression 
algorithms, if necessary (Item 5.3.3). 
F.5.2.5 Short-term power decrease. 
F.5.2.5.1 Power decrease/increase is performed according to Items F.5.2.3, 
F.5.2.4. 
F.5.2.5.2 The following is generally recommended to prevent xenon 
oscillations: after power decrease, quickly extract control groups 9, 10 and 11 and 
transfer group 12 to the position providing the initial offset value; further 
compensation of xenon pr ocesses and increase of power shall be performed due to 
water exchange, movement of group 12 while maintaining initial offset value. 
F.5.2.5.3 When the power is reduced for less than 12 hours, it is allowed to 
keep the groups in the position reached by the m during unloading in order to ensure 
the power increase due to the extraction of the groups. This technique is 
recommended for use in conditions of reduced water exchange efficiency at the end 
of the cycle. 
F.5.2.5.4 In the process of short -term reactor u nloading from nominal power 
Nnom to power N within the range of 75 -90% for not more than 5 hours, an 
algorithm of spatial localization of xenon processes can be used, which ensures 
decrease of water exchange intensity and prevention of xenon oscillations. Power 
reduction is performed by submersion of control groups 11 and 12 into upper half of 
core so that power of lower half is maintained. For this purpose, the offset shall be 
reduced from the initial AOin value to the value  
 
АОlow=100+(AOin-100)Nnom/N. 
 
At reduced power poisoning is compensated by extraction of groups, offset 
value if possible close to AOlow is maintained by change of distance of groups. If 
necessary, distillate or concentrate is added. 
F.5.2.5.5   Power raise  is performed by extraction of groups: group 11 is 
extracted completely, group 12 - to the position not higher than the maximum 
permissible. If the extraction of groups did not provide a power rise of up to 100%, 
further power increase is performed by the xenon burnup process or distillate 
injection. The initial offset value AOin is maintained when operating at 100% power. 
[PAGE 391]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur 
NPP Unit 1  RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001  
Version 2 
Continuation of Appendix F 
389 
F.5.2.5.6  Optimal control with in relation to change of local thermal load on 
fuel elements is provided if phase point of the offset po wer diagram returns to initial 
position. 
F.5.3 Power density distribution control. 
F.5.3.1 Warning and elimination of exceeding the maximum permissible values 
of Kvij, Qlijk parameters. 
Current values of Kvij and Qlijk parameters in each elevation layer ar e 
monitored using special formats of MCDS and RSim. The operator shall be provided 
with minimum margin values from the current values Kvij and Qlijk to the respective 
maximum permissible ones - Kvijperm and Qlimperm, with indication of FA number 
(i) and elevation layer number (j), where minimum is reached. The following actions 
shall be performed when the minimum margin is reduced to zero: 
- perform actions to reduce offset to prevent exceeding the limit values of Kvij 
and Qlijk in the upper half of the cor e (sub-items 2.1.3, 2.3). If the limit values are 
exceeded, then the power is reduced until the permissible values are reached 
(preferably by submerging the control groups to the upper half of the core); 
- perform actions to increase the offset to prevent exceeding the limit values of 
Kvij or Qlijk in the lower half of the core (sub -items  2.1.3, 2.3). If the limits are 
exceeded, the power is reduced to the allowable values (preferably by injecting 
concentrate). 
F.5.3.2 The minimum offset deviation from the value corresponding to the final 
steady state is provided to prevent axial xenon oscillations during reactor state 
change. 
F.5.3.3 Suppression of axial xenon oscillations. 
F.5.3.3.1   The degree of offset instability is estimated (the amplitude and 
phase of offset oscillations are determined), the possibility of phase point going 
beyond the recommended area of the offset power diagram or the possibility of 
exceeding the maximum permissible values of power density parameters is predicted 
with the help of the offset diagram and phase diagrams, and, if necessary, making the 
design forecast according to the RSim program. If necessary, xenon vibration 
suppression procedure is performed. 
F.5.3.3.2  General rule of vibration suppression. The control action shall  
change the offset in the direction opposite to its drift. Time delays are made between 
control actions to determine offset drift direction and speed. 
F.5.3.3.3   Group 12 is submerged by 2 -5%, then groups 11 and 10 are 
successively submerged to suppress the ascending phase of oscillations in the case of 
control groups position above 50%. Offset drift is checked before the start of 
submersion of each group. Described procedure of groups submersion is repeated 
until oscillation phase is changed. The vibratio n suppression is stopped when the 
groups reach the lower limit positions, then the exceedance of permissible values of  
Kvij and Qlijk is monitored before the oscillation phase changes. The submersion of 
[PAGE 392]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur 
NPP Unit 1  RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001  
Version 2 
Continuation of Appendix F 
390 
the groups is compensated by the injection of distil late (xenon burnup and de -
poisoning are also used if possible). Movement of groups is controlled by means of 
“Group control” key and switching of APC-R to control of selected group. 
F.5.3.3.4  The control groups are extracted from the core; groups 10 and 1 1 
are extracted up to ULS, group 12 - not more than 95% to suppress the downward 
phase of oscillations in the case of control groups position above 50%. The extraction 
of the groups is compensated by the injection of concentrate (poisoning is also used if 
possible). Movement of groups is controlled by means of “Group control” key and 
switching of APC-R to control of selected group. It is allowed to compensate for the 
extraction of groups by submersion of the central CR to positions below 50% 
(submersion of the central CR above 50% does not give the necessary effect). 
F.5.3.3.5  A distance change method is used to suppress the oscillations if 
the distance between the two control groups is more than 40%. In this case, one group 
is controlled using the “GROUP C ONTROL” key, the other is connected to the  
APC-R. 
F.5.3.3.6  The algorithm for changing the phase of oscillations accelerates 
the suppression of oscillations during the drift of the phase point on the offset -offset 
diagram in the direction - “from the dia gonal”. Control groups are moved by acting 
on the offset until the drift direction changes - “to the diagonal”. 
F.5.3.3.7  The algorithm for maintaining a constant offset ensures 
stabilization of the reactor state at the specified position of group 12. By moving the 
control groups, a constant offset (corresponding to the specified position of group 12) 
is maintained until the oscillations are completely eliminated. 
F.5.3.3.8  The algorithm of maintaining the equilibrium offset provides the 
fastest suppression of oscillations. Oscillations suppression is started at the moment 
when the phase point reaches the offset -offset diagram diagonal (AO =AO*). The 
current point on the diagonal of the offset diagram is maintained by moving the 
control groups until the oscillations are completely eliminated. 
F.5.3.4  Suppression of diametrical xenon oscillations. 
If the possibility of exceeding the maximum permissible values of Kvij and 
Qlijk parameters during diametrical xenon oscillations is predicted, submersion of 
one CR closest to the j -th FA and belonging to one of the control groups prevents 
exceeding the maximum permissible values of parameters and provides oscillations 
suppression. CR motion is compensated by control group movement or water 
exchange. Submerged CR can be in the core for no more than 6 hours. It is allowed to 
submerge CR if there are no CRs in the core that do not belong to control groups. 
F.6. Control algorithms in case of disturbance of normal operation. 
F.6.1  Power reduction in manual mode. If in case of disturbance of normal 
operation it is necessary to reduce the reactor power, then this is done in accordance 
with Item F.5.2.3. 
[PAGE 393]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur 
NPP Unit 1  RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001  
Version 2 
Continuation of Appendix F 
391 
F.6.2 PP-1 mode. Upon PP -1 signal, the reactor is automatically unloaded by 
injecting CR groups in the standard sequence . After cancellation of PP -1 mode use 
described in the subparagraph F.5.2, F.5.3 reactor control algorithms. 
F.6.3   APP mode. Upon the APP signal, the APC -R gets disabled and the 
power is reduced due to the drop of the APP group (six peripheral CRs from g roup 
7), at the same time the groups are submerged in PP -1 mode until the reactor is 
unloaded to the set power level. Then APC -R will be automatically started in “N” 
mode, which will form the “B” command (as a result of reactor xenon poisoning).  
If the “APC-R GROUPS SELECTION” key is in “SuS” position, then the APP 
group is extracted automatically. APC -R command is sent only to control groups 9 - 
12. After extraction of group 12 to the position of 90% (other groups are on ULS), 
normal movement mode is rest ored (Item F.2.1.14.9) and APP group extraction is 
started.  
The APP group shall be extracted from the core within 3 hours. Acceleration of 
this process can be provided by injecting BAS or submerging group 12 (the “APC -R 
GROUPS SELECTION” key is set to “12 ” or “SuS” position, the “GROUP 
SELECTION” key is set to “7” or “SuS” position, the “GROUP CONTROL” key 
sends the “B” command). 
The local power of power density in the lower half of the core increases during 
the extraction of the APP group. It is allowed t o extract the APP group by two 
subgroups of three CR in the individual control mode to prevent violation of 
limitations on local power.

Rooppur NPP 
Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
424 
Designations used in the Table:        
O  - equipment in operation - the equipment performs the design functions; 
O * - at primary circuit temperature more than 150 °С above zero; 
OS - equipment on standby (operable state) - equipment is ready for operation: electric circuit are lined up, PPI are checked and put 
into operation, cabinets are sealed, rooms are locked and access to them is limited. If the specification or operation instructions 
require the equipment to be in watchdog, then the equipment shall be ready for putting into operation in automatic mode;  
TO - taken out of operation (from standby); 
NR - not regulated (no requirements for operability and operation in terms of the Unit state). 
(1) - the minimum required number of operable system channels is indicated in parentheses; 
(1p) - the number of system pumps is indicated in parentheses (for example, the system and at the same time not less than one pump 
of this system shall be operable); 
SC - special conditions for the system in this state of the Unit given in the respective section of the specification or in the op eration 
instructions for this system or equipment; 
/ - (/) indicates the change in the state of the system or equipment in the process of Unit parameters change during operation in  
this mode or state.

Conditions for safe storage and transportation of nuclear fuel 
H.1 Conditions for safe storage of fresh FA in FFSF 
1) FA and CPS AR can be stored in the FFSF in TPS, racks or transport 
casks. 
2) TPS shall be stored sealed in horizontal position. Opening of TPS with 
FA cooled below 0°С shall be performed not earlier than 10 hours after their put ting 
into the FFSF. 
3) FA shall be stored in racks or transport casks in vertical position packed 
in polyethylene film. Racks and transport casks shall be covered with covers. 
4) The following air parameters shall be provided when working with FA 
and CPS AR, as well as when storing in racks and transport casks in the FFSF: 
- temperature - not lower than 10 °С above zero; 
- relative humidity - not more than 80%. 
5) Air temperature and humidity in the FFSF shall be checked daily on 
business days with results registration in a special logbook. 
6) The rack and transport cask shall be checked for cleanliness and absence 
of foreign items before installation of FA in them. 
7) Before installation of FA for storage in rack or transport cask, wipe it (in 
accessible places) with clean cotton napkin wetted in alcohol and pack it in 
polyethylene film covering, then install FA vertically in rack or transport cask with 
thrust on the shank. Wrap the free edge of polyethylene cover on the FA head and tie 
it with tape. 
8) It is allowed not to pack FA into polyethylene film covers, if the duration 
of FA sto rage in the rack or transport cask does not exceed three months, counting 
from the date of their incoming inspection. 
9) It is prohibited to perform construction and welding works at a distance 
closer than 3 meters from the products, use fire, smoke, store fo reign items that are 
not necessary for work in the FFSF premises, in the availability of fresh FA. 
H.2 Limits and conditions of safe transportation of fresh FA from the FFSF to 
reactor building 
1) Fresh FA are transported in transport cask with a capacity of 27 FA. 
2) Transport cask is closed with cover. 
3) Transport cask is moved from FFSF to reactor building with the road 
train (lifting capacity of 50t and weight of 60,000kg) equipped with special devices 
for installation and reliable attachment of the transport cask. 
4) Speed of fresh FA transportation from the FFSF to reactor building with 
the road train should not exceed 5 km/h. 
H.3 Spent FA storage conditions in the FP 
1) Working medium in the FP - demineralized water with boric acid content 
of 16 ÷ 20 g/dm3; 
[PAGE 428]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP 
Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
Continuation of Appendix H 
426 
2) Water level elevation in FP is 25.450 m ±100 mm; 
3) Water temperature in FP - not more than 60 °С above zero. 
H.4 Conditions for safe SNF transportation are ensured by using the dual -
purpose transport packaging set TUK -137T.E designed for transportation and long -
term storage of irradiated fuel assemblies (SFA). 
1) Capacity of TUK-137T.E . – 18 pcs. of SFA; 
2) The total power of residual power density of SFA loaded into the 
container - not more than 30 kW; 
H.5 Standards of fresh FA storage and transportation 
1) According to th e design project, the total capacity of the FFSF is 462 
FA, of which 201 FA in 3 racks, 180 FA in 90 TPS TK-S5 (TUK TKК-С5М)  and 81 
FA in three casks. 
2) 90 TPS TK-S5 (TUK TK-С5М) with FA (capacity of one packaging set 
- two FA, distance between FA axes - 550 mm) are located on the floor at el. + 0.500 
m and at elev. + 7.400 m in designated areas designated by marking, groups. There is 
no more than 16 packages in a group, the distance between groups is at least 2.5 
meters. It is allowed to install packages in  no more than 4 tiers in such a way that 
their fall is excluded.  
3) FA are located in racks in cells (borated hexagonal pipes) with 300 mm 
spacing along triangular grid. Number of FA in one rack - 67 pcs. The distance 
between racks is 1 m. 
4) FA in transport ca sks are arranged with spacing of 400 mm along 
triangular grid. Quantity of FA in the cask is 27 pcs. The cask can be used for 
transportation and storage of CPS AR with preliminary installation of the frame. 
5) When refueling the reactor core, it is allowed to  place fresh FA in the 
fuel pool rack cells of Rooppur NPP Unit 1. 
6) Speeds of lifting and moving TPS with NF shall not exceed 8 m/min, 
while initial (strictly vertical rise to a height of 0.5 m) and final (strictly vertical 
lowering from a height of 0.5 m) speeds shall not exceed 4.25 m/min. Install TPS 
with NF on the tilter and in storage places at a finishing vertical speed of 0.6 m/min. 
7) All movements of FA and CPS AR during transport and handling 
operations in the FFSF shall be performed in vertical posit ion with speeds not 
exceeding: 
- in horizontal direction - 12.0 m/min; 
- in vertical direction - 6.0 m/min. 
8) Movement of FA and CPS AR near the equipment shall be performed at 
a speed not exceeding: 
- in horizontal direction - 4.0 m/min; 
- in vertical direction - 0.6 m/min. 
9) Vertical movement of FA and CPS AR inside the packaging set and 
process equipment shall be performed at a speed of not more than 0.6 m/min, while 
the person responsible for carrying out transport and handling operations with fresh 
[PAGE 429]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP 
Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
Continuation of Appendix H 
427 
fuel in  the FFSF shall be in close proximity to the moved FA and monitor the 
freedom of their movement during the entire period of this operation. 
10) It is prohibited to move FA in horizontal direction with their 
simultaneous lifting or lowering. 
11) Installation of the  transport cask with NF into the socket with the road 
train shall be performed at a finishing speed of not more than 0.6 m/min. 
H.6 Standards of SNF storage and transportation in the FP 
1) The design capacity of the FP of Rooppur NPP Unit No. 1 is adopted 
based on the conditions of placement of spent fuel assemblies in it (together with 
CPS AR) for at least 10 years and the possibility of unloading all reactor core 
assemblies into the pool at any time of operation. Sealed casks with spent leaking FA 
installed in them shall be stored in FP racks until the Unit is taken out of operation. 
2) Maximum actual capacity of compressed fuel storage racks of FP of 
Rooppur NPP Unit 1 is 756 cells, including: 
- 732 cells for FA; 
- 24 cells for sealed casks. 
3) FA are located in c ells (borated hexagonal pipes) of FP racks with 
spacing of 300 mm. Unsealed or defective SFA are placed in sealed casks with 
spacing of 400 mm. Racks consist of 12 separate sections. Each section has 2 cells for 
sealed casks and 61 cells for FA. 
4) The storag e pool also comprises a container compartment located 
nearby, which is connected to the FP by a refueling channel. The container 
compartment is equipped with a multi -purpose socket for installation of a transport 
cask in it with a capacity of 27 fresh FA ( CPS AR) or TUK TK -137TE designed for 
loading 18 SFA into it for subsequent shipment from the NPP territory. 
5) All movements of FA and CPS AR during transport and handling 
operations in the FP shall be performed RM with observance of the following speeds: 
- horizontal - 21 m/min; 
- vertical - 12.5 m/min. 
Main vertical speed of FA movement: 
- in the reactor core - not more than 4.0 m/min; 
- in transport casks, fuel pool racks, FADS casks, sealed casks, TUK TK -
137ТЕ - not more than 6.0 m/min. 
Final speed of FA movement - not more than 0.6 m/min.

Terms and definitions 
Term Definition 
Accident NPP anticipated operational occurrence with release of 
radioactive substances and (or) ionizing radiation beyond the 
limits provided by the NPP design documentation for normal 
operation in amounts exceeding the established safe operation 
limits, the accident is characterized by the initiating event, 
pathways and consequences 
Disturbance of normal 
operation 
disturbance in NPP operation, in which a deviation from the 
established operation limits and (or) conditions occurred. At the 
same time, other NPP design-basis limits and (or) conditions, 
including safe operation limits and (or) conditions, may also be 
violated 
Basic Unit operation mode NPP mode in the power system at a power level of 80-100% of 
the nominal one with permissible deviations of the current 
frequency in the power system from the nominal value and 
without involving in operational frequency control 
Check system (component) operation monitoring in order to establish 
their operable or inoperable state and identify faults 
Check completion success 
criteria 
set of signs based on which the system (component) operability is 
confirmed 
CPS CR design positions CPS CR design positions that provide effective emergency 
protection and optimal power density field, at which the 
maximum permissible values of reactor thermal power and power 
density irregularity factors are not exceeded by the core volume in 
all reactor operation modes 
CPS CR jamming CPS CR state in which any of the following conditions are met: 
- CPS CR does not move down to BLS when the drive is de-
energized or by EP signal (by APP signal for CPS CR of group 
used for APP); 
- CPS CR does not drop to BLS when the drive is de-energized, 
but drops down to BLS by CK; 
- CPS CR does not move by CK or by signals of PP-1, PRLD, 
APC-R to BLS due to loss of control for any reason 
Document development Collection of data that is necessary for the development of the 
document, development of revisions, coordination with 
stakeholders, approval from the responsible person, sending the 
document to the archive, monitoring of document submission to 
stakeholders and responsible parties 
Document of direct action it means the need to perform all actions prescribed by the 
document and the mandatory implementation of prescribed 
instructions 
Efficiency of emergency 
protection 
negative reactivity injected into the reactor during the drop of all 
CPS CR groups included in the emergency protection, sufficient 
to change over the reactor to the sub-critical state and maintain 
the sub-critical state of the reactor in case of normal operation 
disturbances, including design-basis accidents. 
[PAGE 442]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP 
Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
440 
Term Definition 
Emergency protection - safety function, which consists in rapid reactor changeover to 
the sub-critical state and in maintaining it in the sub-critical state; 
- set of safety systems that performs the emergency protection 
function 
Emergency shutdown spontaneous shutdown under a preliminary submitted request 
caused by the actuation of EP, process protection or personnel 
actions, including erroneous ones  
Emergency switchings switchings in systems (components) when eliminating normal 
operation disturbances, emergency situations and accidents 
performed by operating personnel 
Energy power level reactor plant power level sufficient to connect the turbine 
generator to the mains 
Equipment loading cycle a single change in the parameters of the working medium by 
absolute value (or at a speed exceeding the permissible one) that 
reduces the equipment lifetime. The list of cycles that reduce the 
lifetime is established by the engineering (design) documentation 
Event deviation of the diagnostic parameter from the standard regardless 
of the real state of the diagnosed item 
False actuation of EP or 
PP&I 
actuation caused by failure of components or their circuits when 
the appropriate parameters do not reach their setpoint values 
Familiarization with 
document 
familiarizing with the document by the personnel who shall know 
and use the document in the work in due time. Familiarization 
shall be formalized in the document copy kept at the workplace 
and/or in the Technical documentation familiarization logbook 
under the established procedure established. Familiarization with 
document shall be confirmed by signature 
Fault changes in the parameters and characteristics of equipment 
(components) operation, which lead to a disturbance (deviation) 
in the performance of the specified function of equipment 
(components) 
First approach of criticality the stage of putting the NPP Unit into operation, including the 
reactor loading with nuclear fuel, reaching the critical state of the 
reactor and performing the necessary tests and measurements at 
the power level, at which heat removal from the reactor is 
performed due to natural heat loss (dissipation) 
Maintenance a set of operations to maintain the item (systems and components) 
operability when used as intended in standby mode, during 
storage and transportation 
Nominal (allowed) power 
level (Nnom) 
value established by the design project  
Non-operability state recorded at the MCR (ECR) due to a failure in the system 
equipment in the signal path 
Normal operation NPP operation within the design operation limits and conditions 
Nuclear accident accident related to fuel elements damage exceeding the specified 
limits of safe operation or accident without fuel elements damage 
caused by: 
- disturbance of monitoring and control of fission chain

Term Definition 
reaction; 
- occurrence of criticality during refueling, transportation and 
storage of nuclear fuel; 
Nuclear-hazardous work works with safety related NPP systems or components (including 
tests, taking out of service for repair and putting into operation) 
not stipulated by the Technical specification of NPP Unit 
operation and operation instructions, as well as other works 
included in the list of nuclear-hazardous activities by the 
operating organization based on the operating experience, 
including following the results of investigation of NPP 
disturbances, given the design and engineering documentation, 
due to the need to establish special requirements for such works 
not contained in the Technical specification of NPP Unit 
operation and operation instructions. Nuclear-hazardous work 
comprises only such work, failed procedure of which can lead to a 
nuclear accident 
Operating conditions conditions stipulated by design concerning the number, 
characteristics, state of operability and technical maintenance of 
safety-related systems (components) needed for operation without 
operation limits failure. 
Operation documentation technical documentation that separately or in set with other 
documents determines systems and equipment operation rules and 
(or) contains information that certifies the main parameter values 
and equipment characteristics (properties) guaranteed by the 
manufacturer, warranties and information on its operation during 
the established life-cycle 
Operation limits values of parameters and characteristics of the state of system 
(components) and NPP as a whole set in the design for normal 
operation 
Operation modes of Unit 
equipment  
 equipment in operation; 
 equipment on duty; 
 equipment on standby; 
equipment in operation - the equipment performs the design 
functions; 
equipment on duty - the equipment is ready for automatic 
operation. Its operability is checked at specified frequency 
equipment on standby - the equipment is ready for operation: 
electric circuits are lined up, PPI are checked and put into 
operation, cabinets are sealed, premises are locked and access to 
them is restricted, its operability is checked at the set frequency 
Operation state of the Unit state of NPP unit characterized by operation limits and conditions 
established in the NPP design project 
Operation instruction Operation document, which contains specific instructions to 
personnel on methods of performance of work under normal 
operation and in case of disturbances of normal operation 
Operation with deviations NPP operation with violation of operation limits or conditions, 
but without violation of limits or conditions of safe operation 
Operational conditions minimum requirements established by the NPP design project for 
the number, characteristics, state of operability, scope, frequency 
and other conditions of maintenance, monitoring and testing of 
safety related system (components), at which the limits of safe

Term Definition 
operation and (or) safety criteria are observed 
Performer an employee who directly performs a particular action in 
accordance with the operation instruction. 
Permissible power (Nperm) permissible value of RP thermal power depending on the 
composition of operating main equipment of the Unit and other 
operation limitations 
Pre-emergency situation Unit state characterized by violation of limits or conditions of safe 
operation, which has not developed into an accident 
Reactor minimum controlled 
power level (MCPL) 
minimal value of reactor power (neutron flux) which is reliably 
(with NPP design specified accuracy) determined by neutron flux 
measuring instruments provided for by NPP design for normal 
operation 
Reactor period the time during which the neutron flux density (reactor power) 
changes by e=2.71828 times 
Readiness for work the property of the system (component) to be able to perform the 
required function under given conditions at a given time or within 
a given time interval, provided that the necessary external 
resources are provided 
 
Regulatory documentation Documents that establish rules, general principles or 
characteristics relating to certain activities or their results 
Repair 
 
a set of operations to restore the operable or serviceable state of 
an item and (or) restore its lifetime 
Safe operating limits values of process parameters established by the design, deviation 
from which may cause an accident. 
Scheduled Unit shutdown Unit shutdown according to a preliminary request with the 
permissible rate of power decrease and with the Unit switchover 
to the set final state 
Short-term Unit shutdown Unit shutdown for no more than three days 
Start-up range the range of boric acid concentration in the primary circuit 
coolant for a specific RP state, at which the reactor core is 
expected to reach a critical state. The lower value of the interval is 
taken equal to the rated value of the boric acid concentration 
corresponding to the critical state. The upper value of the 
interval is taken equal to the lower one increased by 1 g/dm3 
of boric acid 
State of operability System (component) state, at which the values of all parameters 
that characterize the ability to perform the specified functions 
comply with the requirements of regulatory and technical and (or) 
engineering documentation 
Steady state of RP the state in which within 24 hours the thermal power changed by 
no more than 2% and the position of CPS CR groups changed by 
no more than 3% 
Steady-state boric acid 
concentration  
steady-state concentration of boric acid in the primary circuit 
coolant is the concentration exceeding by 1 g/dm3 the 
concentration that provides the reactor sub-criticality of at least 
[PAGE 445]
Rooppur NPP Technical specification of safe operation of Rooppur NPP 
Unit 1 RPR.0534.1.0.BN.DZ0001 
Version 2 
 
443 
Term Definition 
0.02 (excluding submerged CPS CRs) in the reactor core state 
with the maximum multiplication factor 
System (component) defect each individual non-compliance of system (equipment) with 
established requirements. 
System (component) failure event consisting in violation of the operable state of the system 
(component) 
System (component) tests experimental determination of quantitative and (or) qualitative 
characteristics of a system (component) as a result of impact on it 
during its functioning, modeling and (or) impact 
System (equipment) 
subdivision-owner 
a structural subdivision, functions of which include monitoring of 
the technical state of process systems (equipment) assigned to it 
and taking measures to maintain their serviceability (reliability) 
Type of tests classification grouping of tests by a certain characteristic 
Unit cooldown a set of operations on systems and equipment that ensure the Unit 
switchover from the “cold” to the “hot” state with a temperature 
decrease rate for normal operation and for disturbances of normal 
operation 
Unit heat-up a set of operations on systems and equipment that ensure the Unit 
switchover from the “cold” to the “hot” state with the permissible 
rate of metal temperature increase 
Unit operation mode  NPP Unit changeover from one operation state to another. 
Operation mode of the Unit characterized by operation limits and 
conditions established by the NPP design project 
Unit shutdown reactor changeover to sub-critical state. Unit systems and 
equipment can remain in operation, on standby or be taken out of 
service for repair. Shutdown can be emergency, unscheduled and 
scheduled 
Unit start-up a combination of operation modes including Unit changeover 
from the “cold” state to the “hot” state; NPP Unit changeover 
from the “hot” state to the “reactor at minimum controlled power 
level” state; raising the reactor power above MCPL to a level 
sufficient to connect the turbine generator to the power system 
Unscheduled shutdown Unit shutdown with the permissible rate of power decrease 
(unloading) without a preliminary request and with the Unit 
switchover to the set final state
